

 ### Chapter 731: Confrontation

First, a man in a Confucian robe ascended the city wall and, with inexplicable divine abilities, instantly killed a large number of monster tribes. Following this, Xie Songhua summoned his bamboo box to wield his sword, completely destroying the life-bound flying sword of a monster swordsman at the Jade Purity realm. The latter immediately fell from his realm into the Nascent Soul stage, teetering on the brink of losing that stage as well. Whether he could still be considered a swordsman was now up for debate; after all, innate sword embryos are rare and hard to come by. It’s not as if one could easily cultivate a new sword just because their realm in sword cultivation was high and their life-bound sword was destroyed. Thus, this unfortunate monster, who was the first to strike, had suffered a tremendous loss during this siege, losing not only his realm but also the various premiums that came with the identity of a swordsman. To say he could easily switch to practicing other magical techniques and return to the upper five realms would be an understatement; he would no longer be a swordsman of the Sword Qi Great Wall, which was akin to reaching for the heavens.

The monster tribes' assault in the battlefield where Chen Ping’an, Liu Xianyang, and Qi Shou were located had evidently stalled.

According to the rules of the Sword Qi Great Wall, Xie Songhua had today made a significant effort with his sword, taking advantage of the time, place, and favorable circumstances, thus achieving a remarkable feat.

This accomplishment was no small matter; because the monster that he had ambushed and killed was one of the most precious swordsmen in the savage world, Xie Songhua could be considered to have slain half a celestial monster or equivalent to a complete Jade Purity realm monster. However, the choice between the two was ultimately up to the swordsman himself. If he chose the former, he would need to kill another half celestial monster to obtain corresponding spoils. Choosing the latter would lead to a small loss, but thankfully, he could immediately collect money and treasures from the Hidden Official.

Yet, it was clear that Xie Songhua was not finished; he still wished to strike again.

Qi Shou sighed, "All the good fortune has gone to Sword Immortal Xie; I need to be careful."

Decisively, Qi Shou summoned his last flying sword, the Jumping Pearl, creating a sword formation around him to prevent being ambushed by upper five realm monster swordsmen.

Turning to ask, "Did you get any share of such a big profit?"

Chen Ping’an sat cross-legged on the ground, pressing down on the long sword laid across his knees, and shook his head, "No."

As bait, he had received no additional profit.

Liu Xianyang laughed and asked, "Are you two friends?"

Chen Ping’an still shook his head.

Qi Shou sneered, "Friends? More like enemies. As soon as we step down from the city wall, this second shopkeeper would love to calculate my demise, and I wouldn't mind using my realm to crush him."

Liu Xianyang nodded, "That’s quite similar to our hometown, where the people are simple-minded."

In the savage world, there were numerous military supervisors and battle commanders. Once the monster army showed signs of stagnation in their assault, they would unleash a massacre.

Thus, in the battlefield where the three were, the monsters continued to charge forward. Not only that, but it seemed they had devised additional strategies, sending in a group of monster cultivators who understood talismanic methods, haphazardly throwing a bunch of yellow paper talismans in an attempt to obscure the battlefield's visibility. In no time, dust flew everywhere, and spiritual energy became chaotic. The leading line of monsters consisted of massive beasts, responsible for being the first to die, likely hoping to force Liu Xianyang to act more in order to find clues.

Qi Shou remained calm as he faced the onslaught. On the battlefield, the soaring kites and heartstrings flickered rapidly, as many towering monsters had their limbs severed by sword light, crashing to the ground with mournful howls.

Qi Shou had always been ruthless in battle, leaving behind no mercy, whether it was outright slaughter or skinning and flaying, refusing to show bare bones until he was satisfied. He would often leave opponents grievously injured but alive, letting them struggle on the battlefield, waiting for death, particularly those monster cultivators who could morph into human forms. They would frequently meet their doom beneath Qi Shou's flying swords, disemboweled and left to die. Should any monster cultivator show compassion and attempt to rescue them, they would meet a similar fate.

Chen Ping’an took a sip from the water elixir in his sword nurturing gourd and continued to strike at the enemies. He pursued a lethal blow with every attack; if a monster's body was too resilient, or if they survived after crucial acupoints were pierced, he would follow up with one or two more strikes from his needle-like sword, Thunder Pin.

During this time, there were indeed monster cultivators acting as concealed assassins, attempting to use secret techniques to restrain the flying swords, trying to perish together. However, in this game of deceit and disguise, Chen Ping’an was an expert. Also, the sword he wielded, Chuyi, was slightly slower and remarkably resilient. There had been one extremely concealed assassin monster who had deliberately sustained injuries, covered in blood and flesh, even using a monster as a shield against Chuyi. However, that sword merely pierced through the forehead of the monster in front of him before disappearing in a flash, retreating just as the monster's core shattered. The assassin, before dying, gazed blankly toward the city wall, seemingly confused. The sword that had not fallen into the trap and had merely been affected by the spiritual energy remained completely undamaged, but Chen Ping’an's mental energy had been significantly drained.

As Qi Shou had pointed out, over time, Chen Ping’an, who was not a swordsman, would find it hard to maintain the energy to keep attacking.

But right now, this was merely the opening act of the offensive and defensive battle.

However, Qi Shou was also well aware that when the swordsmen needed to leave the city wall to fight, Chen Ping’an would find it much easier.

Liu Xianyang still did not reveal his sword or life-bound flying sword, nor did he take action. From north to south, he was standing where Xie Songhua had been guarding, and regardless of how many came, they would all perish.

There was no reasoning to be had.

Chen Ping’an couldn't help but say, "Be careful; you might attract the attention of powerful monsters."

Liu Xianyang, with ripples in his heart lake, responded, "The greatest and only trouble with my swordsmanship is the height of my killing power, which is far from outstanding. Besides that, there’s no issue."

Then Liu Xianyang continued, "Listen closely; remember every word I say."

Chen Ping’an was about to speak when Liu Xianyang did not even look at him, laughing, "Stop wasting my time. When Liu Dajie speaks, you just listen. Just because I teach you all the mantras and tips, do you think you can learn them?"

Chen Ping’an fell silent.

Liu Xianyang continued to convey the mantras through thought, aware that Chen Ping’an had a good memory since childhood. Therefore, he explained the mantras as he spoke, not worried that Chen Ping’an would misremember, making his explanations extremely complex and tedious.

The content being discussed was precisely the ancestral sword scripture of Liu Xianyang's family.

Liu Xianyang's ancestral treasure consisted of two items; besides the sword scripture, there was also a set of old, tattered armor that had seen better days. Originally, it was a piece of bluish-black armor that had been obtained by the Xu family in Qingfeng City. After the head of the Xu family acquired the precious armor, he became a formidable Nascent Soul cultivator in the Baoping Continent, extremely powerful, and leveraged the indestructible armor to position Qingfeng City as a prime candidate for the next sect on the continent, second only to their ally, Zhengyang Mountain.

The Xu family could marry into the prominent Yuan family of the Great Li, even if it was the legitimate daughter marrying a side branch; in the long run, it was still a mutually beneficial marriage. The reason the Yuan family agreed to this unappealing marriage during the chaotic situation in Qingfeng City was largely due to the head of the Xu family's cultivation base and their potential to reach the upper five realms.

Liu Xianyang's plan back then was to sell the armor and keep the sword scripture. The price was to part with half of his life. If it hadn't been for the rules of the Lizhu Cave Heaven, that mountain-moving ape would have undoubtedly taken the other half of his life as well.

There was really no reasoning to be had.

However, Liu Xianyang had now become a scholar, and at that time, while lying on the sickbed in the Ruan family's sword shop, he had unexpectedly learned swordsmanship in a dream while on the brink of death. Thus, rules had to be followed, and grudges had to be settled, without hindering one another.

Liu Xianyang asked, "Did you remember everything?"

As he spoke, wisps of sword intent flowed around him as if providing him protection.

Chen Ping’an nodded, then said, "I think I won’t be able to learn it; the threshold is too high."

Liu Xianyang laughed, "Then just keep your mindset in check; don’t compare yourself to Liu Dajie in terms of talent. Is learning swordsmanship really that hard? To me, it’s just average, but to you, of course, it’s quite difficult. But speaking of which, what’s the biggest craft in our hometown? Isn’t it making porcelain? Didn’t we learn that too? So right now, you’re in a similar situation to when you first learned to make porcelain. Back then, you thought you could never master it and be a proper kiln worker? Frowning all day, being a gloomy person—look at how it is now! The emperor himself is begging you to help him create a few pieces of porcelain. Are you willing? It all depends on your mood, doesn’t it? My ancestral swordsmanship, of course, has a lot to it. You will learn slower than me, but you can still learn it; there’s no need to rush. In everything, you can’t be better than me, Liu Dajie; you need to accept that and get used to it."

Chen Ping’an whispered, "I’ve really gotten used to it."

Liu Xianyang laughed heartily, "Good habits don’t need changing!"

On the line where Chen Ping’an and Liu Xianyang were heading south, there was a large military tent surrounded by numerous guards, with a small inconspicuous wooden sign hanging at the entrance, simply stating "Jia Shen."

Inside the big tent were numerous desks filled with scrolls and documents piled high, including many heavily damaged military books that were not original copies but transcriptions. Even so, they were treated as precious treasures, and the monster cultivators would read these military texts with great care.

With fewer books available, those who read them cherished them more, willing to examine them word by word, reading deeply rather than just skimming.

The military tent occupied a vast area, with nearly a hundred monster cultivators gathered here, not due to their cultivated appearances or youthful looks, but because they were genuinely young.

Among them was a young swordsman named Bei Qiao, sitting cross-legged with his back against a sword rack.

Next to him was a peer named Yu Si, who was also a swordsman among the hundred swordsmen of the savage world, but like Bei Qiao, he still had no surname.

A boy lifted the curtain and stepped inside.

Yu Si looked up and smiled, "Tun Tan, how were the results this time?"

"Not as good as last time; I only destroyed three flying swords."

The boy held up three fingers, then shook his head, squatting beside Yu Si and Bei Qiao, grumbling, "It’s really hard to get close to the third sword formation. In my battlefield, if there was even a slight commotion, a celestial swordsman would come to stabilize the formation, protecting those unstable mid-five realm swordsmen. I almost got severed in half by a sword energy. It was very dangerous."

Then the boy's smile brightened, "But I’m not too far from the battlefield where Chen Ping’an is stationed. He’s neighbors with Qi Shou, and Qi Shou really did break through. He held the battlefield with just two flying swords; that was impressive. Later, a scholar emerged with a very strange technique, and anyone who bumped into him wouldn’t know how they died. Still impressive."

A girl sitting behind a desk glanced at a map and said slowly, "The celestial swordsman you encountered should be Situ Jixue, a Jade Purity realm swordsman from the wilds of Golden Armor Continent. His life-bound flying sword is called 'Iron Rider,' and he carries a sword named 'Heroic Pass.' His killing power isn't exceptionally outstanding, but he’s well-rounded and quite remarkable. To escape from under his sword is already quite a skill. Tun Tan, remember, military achievements can accumulate slowly, but don’t die. That battlefield of yours is under Mu Ji’s command. You’re one of the selected hundred swordsmen; if you die, it will implicate Mu Ji. He’s worked hard to get a chance to award you with a surname; don’t let it all go to waste."

A bashful boy sitting near the girl raised his head and said softly, "Don’t die. Otherwise, even if you get a surname, I’ll feel guilty for a long time."

The boy named Tun Tan grinned, "Got it."

The hundred swordsmen of the savage world are the designated seeds of the Dao by the Tuo Yue Mountain, and their importance is second only to the celestial monsters at the ascension stage.

Every swordsman, regardless of their current realm, was valuable.

If one were to die, both the Jiazi Tent and Tuo Yue Mountain would hold them accountable, and the penalties would be severe.

At this moment, there were more than five people inside the Jia Shen tent.

Tun Tan, Bei Qiao, Yu Si, the girl who had unveiled Situ Jixue's details, and a boy who was somewhat of a loner in the corner.

Mu Ji turned toward a desk, habitually speaking softly, "Have we found out about that Confucian disciple's root of techniques, especially whether or not he’s a swordsman? The losses in this small battlefield have already exceeded our expectations, and we need to respond appropriately. The prior attempt to send a celestial swordsman to assassinate Chen Ping’an has failed, but as long as your conclusions indicate we need to deploy another celestial swordsman, I’ll send a flying sword message to notify the swordsman to launch a sneak attack. If that fails, I’ll personally head to the ‘Jiazi’ main tent; you don’t need to feel pressured about that."

A man shook his head, "We still need to let more die to gather more clues."

Mu Ji nodded.

The girl said, "Chen Chun'an from Nan Po Sha Continent has personally come to the Sword Qi Great Wall. That scholar must be from the second sage line, and this is beyond doubt. In fact, we can allocate fewer troops to the battlefield he guards because over there, a concealed flying sword message will surely come soon. Once it’s confirmed from the Jiazi main tent, they will naturally inform us. If the message includes details about this person's identity, we still have two celestial swordsman slots left in the Jia Shen tent, so we might as well use them together. At that time, whether we kill that scholar or Chen Ping’an, or even take a step back to target Qi Shou, it will allow both celestial swordsmen to act according to the situation."

Mu Ji thought for a moment and nodded, "Viable."

Then the bashful boy took a piece of yellow paper from a stack, folded it into a small paper kite, and gently tossed it toward the main tent entrance, "Send the order down; on the sixth line of Jia Shen, ease the offensive. Aside from not allowing retreat, prioritize saving lives."

The paper kite flew out of the Jia Shen big tent.

The young swordsman with the strange name, Yu Si, joked, "Tun Tan, although you’re not at a high realm now, you have many tricks. If you get the chance, once the swordsmen leave the city wall, you should go meet that Chen Ping’an. Compared to me and Bei Qiao, who only know how to charge blindly, you’re much more likely to gain an advantage."

Tun Tan thought for a moment and nodded, "Let’s give it a try."

This Jia Shen tent was one of the sixty large tents named after the heavenly stems and earthly branches among the savage world's army. Besides the commands from the Jiazi main tent, each military tent specifically managed the dispatching of troops for a designated battlefield.

Since it could start with 'Jia,' it already indicated the importance of this tent. According to military law, even celestial swordsmen and monsters would be executed on the spot if they dared to trespass into a tent starting with 'Jia.'

Inside the Jia Shen tent, everyone performed their duties in an orderly manner, and overall, the atmosphere remained relatively relaxed.

The young woman who had the map open raised her head and said solemnly, "For our growth, and to secure several continents in the future for the Haoran world, we need to guard a few. Just saying, in the Jia Shen battlefield alone, we have already lost nearly ten thousand troops for nothing. Each of our contributions is inscribed on bones; don’t think this is a trivial matter."

A pale-faced boy sitting alone in a secluded corner sneered, "Troops? Can those brainless ants even be counted as troops? Their deaths are better; it helps us seize the timing and saves the army rations, killing two birds with one stone. Our savage world can't support so many useless people. Dying here is their rightful end; they’ve finally made a tiny contribution."

He glanced at Bei Qiao and Tun Tan nearby, "That Chen Ping’an, leave him to me. Anyone who dares to compete with me, don’t blame my flying sword for being blind and accidentally injuring allies."

It was indeed a Li Zhen who had transformed from a child into a young man, still possessing part of the ancient convict’s fragmented soul, and then reconstructed his body using the secret methods of Tuo Yue Mountain, ultimately piecing together a complete soul.

Bei Qiao remained unmoved.

Tun Tan still wore a bright smile, “No problem.”

Yu Si grinned, "I wouldn’t dare; I have no right to be an ally of Young Master Li Zhen."

That arrogant young man suddenly laughed, staring intently at Yu Si, "I advise you not to learn from the people over in the Haoran world, speaking in a strange, ambiguous manner."

Yu Si raised both hands, looking pitiful, "I’ll keep quiet, I’ll keep quiet."

Mu Ji frowned, raised his head, and with some seriousness, said, although still softly compared to Li Zhen and Yu Si's previous tones, "Li Zhen’s defeat was only by a line; Yu Si, that’s no reason to gloat. You are swordsmen of a higher caliber; you should have a higher mindset."

Yu Si immediately composed himself and nodded.

Then Mu Ji turned to Li Zhen and said, "Losing is losing; it’s your own inadequacy, Li Zhen. Being able to survive afterward is also your skill as a disciple of Tuo Yue Mountain. I won’t concern myself with that. I’m only responsible for the wins and losses of the Jia Shen battlefield. Every little fluctuation must be accounted for. In the coming fierce battles, you, Li Zhen, still need to obey orders. Ignoring military discipline and acting on your own will bring down the entire Jia Shen tent, and you’ll bear the consequences. But at the right time, if you still wish to seek out Chen Ping’an as an opponent and settle the score with him, even if it means exchanging lives, you are free to do so. The Jia Shen tent will not obstruct you. I personally would even be willing to use my share of the military achievements from the Jia Shen tent to help create an opportunity for you to face Chen Ping’an, because to fight alongside someone like Li Zhen, who dares to die again, is an honor for me."

Mu Ji looked around and said solemnly, "Why did Li Zhen go into battle? Why was he under the city wall fighting that Chen Ping’an? Don’t you all know? Do you even deserve to mock Li Zhen now just because he lost once and died once? If that’s the case, then for countless years, our savage world has never won a single battle, not even one! So many ascended predecessors, along with the entire Tuo Yue Mountain, are they not a joke?! If you have the ability, go to the Haoran world and mock the people there; you can mock them all you want!"

Mu Ji took a deep breath, his expression dimming as he muttered, "Saying these things to you doesn’t make me happy."

Li Zhen seemed to have listened to Mu Ji in this Jia Shen tent, truly no longer bickering with Yu Si and the others, closing his eyes to cultivate while refining five life-bound items.

The girl teased, "Mu Ji, your words are quite eloquent."

The young man, Mu Ji, smiled shyly, feeling a bit embarrassed.

Almost as if a mute, Bei Qiao spoke for the first time, "The flying sword from the Jiazi tent is coming soon."

Sure enough, a message flying sword arrived at the Jia Shen tent.

After Mu Ji read the confidential message, his expression became serious, "We only know that the scholar is named Liu Xianyang, a citizen of Baoping Continent, and not a pure Confucian disciple of the Chen family, so we still don’t know his foundational cultivation."

The girl sighed, "Then we should prepare for the worst and do whatever it takes to uncover the truth."

Mu Ji suddenly said, "Yu Si, you personally go to the battlefield. Remember to disguise yourself well; if you take a sword, exit the battlefield immediately without any hesitation. Chen Ping’an’s sword strikes aren’t that powerful, but his observations of the battlefield are meticulous. Knowing his temperament, I dare say he definitely has more than just that female celestial swordsman as a backup. As long as you survive on the battlefield, another celestial swordsman will soon be assigned to keep an eye on you."

Yu Si decisively stood up, eager to go, though he complained, "The retribution came so quickly."

Mu Ji turned his gaze toward Bei Qiao.

Yu Si dashed out of the Jia Shen tent without giving Mu Ji a chance to change his mind.

Mu Ji shifted his attention to Tun Tan, "I’ve calculated that with your current accumulated military achievements, you’re still quite a bit short to buy that Yiluohe precious item. No worries, I’ll take the lead and pitch in. In the future, whoever pays will receive dividends each year. Who else is willing?"

The girl shook her head, "I’m also saving money; I can’t contribute."

Mu Ji replied, "You can contribute. You’ll earn it back before the great battle concludes; trust me, it absolutely won’t delay your acquisition of that item."

Li Zhen opened his eyes and said, "Is it necessary to buy it? I can just go and ask for it directly."

Mu Ji shook his head, about to refuse.

Li Zhen had already stood up, addressing the girl, "Which one do you need? Just say it; I’ll bring it all back, no need for a second trip."

The girl, without hesitation, named the precious item, laughingly clasping her fists in thanks.

Li Zhen walked out of the Jia Shen tent expressionlessly.

Looking up toward the Sword Qi Great Wall, he could see the northern city wall, which was vague, but from the northern city wall, the battlefield was fully visible.

Li Zhen withdrew his gaze, paused for a moment, and turned around, rare enough to clasp his fists and bow in respect.

Beside Li Zhen was a burly man with a large beard, carrying a saber and a sword on his back.

The man nodded, "You go ahead and busy yourself."

Li Zhen rode the wind away.

Bei Qiao exited the Jia Shen tent, calling out to his master.

The man said, "Your master wants to see someone, so you, as his disciple, must do something for him: kill that Chen Ping’an."

Bei Qiao nodded silently. 

*(End of Chapter)*

 # Chapter 732: Sword Refinement (Part 1)

A resounding horn echoed across the battlefield, signaling the demon race's retreat. 

This skirmish, which had lasted for two weeks, ended with the demon army failing to breach the city walls. On the battlements, the sword immortals maintained their magnificent presence. The great demons from the wild lands were notably less active, with only a handful of ascendant and immortal-level great demons showcasing their powers—merely a few instances without truly engaging in battle. As such, they were overshadowed by the might of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

During this period, two battles stood out as the most remarkable. The first featured an individual named Zuo You, who wielded a sword with remarkable skill, going deep into enemy lines and nearly destroying a relatively forward military encampment of the Gengwu Army. This incited the involvement of two ascendant-level great demons. Yet, Zuo You did not falter; his sword energy surged forth, creating a vast expanse of white sword light. From the city walls, it appeared as if a miniature world had manifested, with endless streams of sword energy emanating from Zuo You, forming an immense half-dome that blotted out the sun. The demons that crossed this path found their bodies and souls shattered, reduced to mere dust.

On the Sword Qi Great Wall, Zuo You himself was nowhere to be seen. 

Only the sword energy and light remained visible.

Recently, the ascendant sword immortal Mi Hu, who had quietly broken through his bottleneck, stood beside his still-Jade Pith realm younger brother, Mi Yu. The two brothers felt differently about the situation. Mi Hu believed that Zuo You's sword energy could have been even more exhilarating; this was how a true sword immortal should be. In contrast, Mi Yu wore a pained expression, feeling that perhaps Zuo You's sword energy was a bit excessive. 

If Zuo You's tendency for solitary action was one side of the coin, then the other battle truly unfolded in the heavens, where Chen Chuan'an intervened, pulling down a round moon from the heights of the celestial canopy into the mortal realm. 

Panic swept across the entire wild world, with many fearing that the ever-growing moon would indeed descend upon them slowly. 

The gray-clad elder of the Moon Holding Mountain did not intervene; instead, he looked up and remarked with a smile, praising Chen Chuan'an's cleverness. 

Indeed, Chen Chuan'an was renowned for reaching new heights among the Ascendant Saints.

Beyond the Central Continent, on the eight great continents, the likes of Chen Chuan'an from the Posa Continent, the Fire Dragon from the North Julu Continent, and Liu Dacai from the Aiai Continent each had their strengths. Even the arrogant Qi cultivators from the Central Continent would not dare to dismiss the three pillars from these continents lightly.

The gray-clad elder allowed the peak ascendant great demon, who called himself the Master of the Lotus Flower Temple, to fully exert himself against Chen Chuan'an. 

This ascendant-level Taoist great demon had refined half a month's worth of moon essence, standing at a significant advantage in terms of timing and location.

However, he still could not prevent Chen Chuan'an's extraordinary techniques from bringing the large moon down toward the earth. 

The perceived slowness was, in truth, an illusion; only ancient deities or enlightened beings could truly comprehend the rapid descent of such a celestial body.

Outside the battlefield, the higher-level cultivators of the wild world, especially those approaching the Upper Five Realms, could feel the overwhelming suffocating presence of the moon and saw the moon palace's scenery. They could also discern lifeless mountain ranges, and the more perceptive Upper Five Realms cultivators could even spot desolate palace ruins and ancient bones, as well as enormous, suspended garments resembling lakes.

In the past, a military sage had once proclaimed a sentiment that leaned more towards flattery than criticism: "It’s a pity that the pure Confucian doesn’t dominate; his writings have failed to reach the heavens." 

Had this person witnessed Chen Chuan'an's efforts during this battle from the Sword Qi Great Wall, he surely would have reconsidered his statement.

As for the Sword Qi Great Wall's familiarity with the Nine Continents of the Wild World, it was not primarily with the Central Continent but rather with the Southern Posa Continent, close to the Suspended Mountain, and particularly with the pure Confucian Chen Chuan'an.

This was largely due to A Liang's fervent promotions, claiming that among scholars, Chen Chuan'an was an exceptionally unique figure—akin to a sage wielding a hammer, proficient in both literature and martial arts.

However, that moon ultimately was not completely pulled down to the mortal realm; the Master of the Lotus Flower Temple exerted all his strength, stalemating with Chen Chuan'an for a full half-hour.

Thus, that night, the round moon hung closest to the ground, exceptionally large and bright.

These two battles were undoubtedly the most fitting examples of divine beings clashing.

The Sword Qi Great Wall was greatly boosted in morale, with sword cultivators now drawing their swords even faster. The sword energy waterfall, which gathered tens of thousands of personal flying swords, surged even more violently.

However, this wave of offensive, compared to the rushing and dying demon army, saw relatively few demon cultivators truly engaging in battle.

As a result, the battle achievements amassed by the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall were mostly meager.

In this context, the female sword immortal named Xie Songhua from the Aiai Continent became a surprising standout, raking in significant battle achievements.

After the demon army ceased their offensive, they no longer left bodies on the battlefield exposed to the elements, as they had before, permitting some sword cultivators from the Sword Qi Great Wall to "pick up money" on the battlefield.

Instead, they began to respect the fallen demon cultivators, making efforts to collect the bodies and bones along with all their belongings, meticulously cataloging and returning them to their descendants.

The Sword Qi Great Wall, of course, would not allow the demons to sweep the battlefield with impunity.

The key point was that the demon army's temporary retreat was laden with significance.

One great demon held up a golden pot, intricately carved with a pattern resembling a mouse, and upon summoning it, all the spirited magical artifacts and treasures—these ownerless items—automatically left the battlefield to rush toward the golden pot.

Another great demon wielded a dark jade plaque sculpted in the shape of a dragon, and upon grasping it tightly, it emitted a brilliant light. Small black dragons, mere finger-lengths, slithered out from the plaque. Upon moving away from the plaque, they transformed into colossal beasts, their four claws crashing down heavily, easily kicking up dust dozens of feet high in an attempt to annihilate the sword cultivators retreating from the city walls.

Once, during an assault on the city, a great demon named Chong Guang summoned one of his personal treasures—a bowl of water. He blew a breath onto the surface, creating a deep vortex that shimmered like a starry river.

The souls of the demon cultivators on the battlefield began to funnel toward the south, attempting to merge with that water bowl.

Collecting souls could return them to the wild world beyond the battlefield or reserve them within the treasured artifacts, preventing them from being refined by the unyielding sword energy and intent of the Sword Qi.

The purest and most refined spiritual energy of heaven and earth seemed indifferent to people, but for cultivators attuned to the right timing and location, it presented a mysterious sort of affinity.

The ancient sword intent of the Sword Qi Great Wall was the best example of this.

However, the scattered limbs, severed corpses, and blood soaking into the earth would dramatically alter the battlefield's fortune.

The sword immortals had to intervene; they could not erase everything, but they would clear as much as they could. Otherwise, the "heavenly timing" that originally belonged to the Sword Qi Great Wall would shift towards the wild world.

This was the sword cultivators' strongest support aside from the primary sword immortals and the wall beneath their feet.

Thus, an unusual scene unfolded on the battlefield: although both armies had ceased hostilities, the actions of the great demons and sword immortals became increasingly frequent.

More and more treasures left behind on the battlefield and broken magical artifacts were being contested and retrieved by both sides. 

In the midst of this contention, many were shattered on-site.

However, compared to the previous confrontations between the two armies, the activity of the sword immortals and great demons, though grand, remained limited.

After the truce, a brief respite followed, with sword cultivators allowed some time to recover—typically half a fortnight at most, or a few days at the least.

Chen Ping'an did not immediately leave the city walls; he continued sitting cross-legged, observing the distant skirmishes between both sides.

Liu Xianyang approached and sat beside Chen Ping'an. He was about to reunite with his classmates and friends. This journey to the Sword Qi Great Wall primarily focused on "learning," and as for slaying demons, regardless of how the other disciples of the Ascendant Saints viewed it, Liu Xianyang was not overly concerned. If not for Chen Ping'an's presence, Liu Xianyang might not have been willing to engage in battle; he had always lived a more relaxed and carefree life than Chen Ping'an.

As for when they would leave the Sword Qi Great Wall, no one knew; it depended on Chen Ping'an's wishes. Liu Xianyang scratched his head, gazing into the distant battlefield where fierce sword lights flickered, and said, "All my battle achievements will count toward you."

Chen Ping'an hummed in acknowledgment and smiled as he handed over his sword nurturing gourd.

Liu Xianyang shook his head. "I won't drink it. Even if I'm thinking of getting wild after drinking, I need a pretty girl by my side, right?"

He had heard that this guy had recorded the Sword Immortal Seal Rubbing at the Sword Qi Great Wall and planned to ask Chen Ping'an to help him carve a pair of seals—one straightforward, inscribed with "Liu the Great Sword Immortal," and the other more sincere, saying "Liu Xianyang, who guards his virtue like jade."

Chen Ping'an quietly asked, "That demon cultivator, how did he manage to remain unharmed after you struck?"

Liu Xianyang laughed. "He's also a sword cultivator and has protective treasures; it’s not so easy to kill him."

Nearby, the area around Qi Shou was bustling. Many people gathered there, as Qi Shou had just broken through to the Nascent Soul realm right before the major battle began and was now guarding a region alone, which certainly warranted celebration.

As the leader of his small mountain, Qi Shou was quickly surrounded by dozens of friends, both male and female.

Some were familiar faces to Chen Ping'an, such as Ren Yi, the sword cultivator from the Dragon Gate who had first defended the gate in the streets. 

Then there was Pu Yu, the Golden Core realm sword cultivator responsible for guarding the second gate. He was a tall, handsome young man in white. 

A few female sword cultivators of similar age also gathered around to congratulate Qi Shou, though part of their motivation stemmed from wanting to see Qi Shou’s two charming neighbors. They were completely different from the highborn young ladies of the wild world, openly looking at Chen Ping'an and Liu Xianyang without hiding their interest. Their so-called whispers were anything but discreet.

On the Sword Qi Great Wall, during the previous shifts in the fierce battle, the familiar sword cultivators occasionally shared stories from other battlefields, including tales about the shopkeeper and the scholars from the Posa Continent. 

They had plenty to chat about. 

As for who among the sword cultivators had died and whose flying sword had been destroyed on the battlefield, it was mostly just a nod of acknowledgment, signaling that they were aware—nothing more.

Chen Ping'an shook his sword nurturing gourd and joked, "Isn't that enough? Are you still not drinking?"

Liu Xianyang hopped off the city wall, muttering, "I'm leaving, I'm leaving."

Once Liu Xianyang had gone, one of the female sword cultivators smiled and asked, "Shopkeeper, what’s your friend's name? Does he have a partner or a little wife?"

Chen Ping'an laughed, "Didn't you ask him when he was here?"

The girl giggled, "I was just too shy."

Chen Ping'an felt somewhat helpless; earlier, she had looked at Liu Xianyang as though he were naked, without a hint of shyness.

Her name was Situ Longqiao, a daughter of the Situ family from Tai Xiang Street, a bottleneck sword cultivator of the Viewing Sea realm, and a close friend of Dong Budie. Among sword cultivators of the same age at the Sword Qi Great Wall, she was of moderate level but had a bright personality and a strong sense of the Jianghu (martial world). 

The interesting events at the Sword Qi Great Wall often became more amusing through her colorful storytelling, and many rumors originated from her and Dong Budie's keen observations, with many truths seeming unbelievable while the lies felt more real.

Back then, when Dong Budie approached the Ning family, he had asked Chen Ping'an to help carve three book seals, one of which was for Situ Longqiao.

The shopkeeper was known for his integrity and fairness; Situ Longqiao swore that everything about him was true. 

"The dragon's eye is a fair statement; when it comes to spending money, Dong Budie's as free as flowing water, and after fighting, Wang Xinshi will say it's my responsibility."

She was now among the latest five great sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

In contrast, the previous five great sword cultivators included A Liang's exceptional gambling skills, the gentle temperament of the Hidden Official who never harmed anyone, the straightforwardness of the Old Deaf Man, the grace of Lu Zhi, and the sentimentality of Mi Yu, which weren't necessarily related to swordsmanship or cultivation.

At this moment, Chen Ping'an and Situ Longqiao could also be considered a meeting of experts. 

Situ Longqiao suddenly asked, "Is Yandang Mountain famous in the wild world?"

Chen Ping'an shook his head. "It's just an inconspicuous mountain on the Baoping Continent, with excellent feng shui, but it hasn't gained much fame yet. However, I have a good friend who travels the mountains and rivers and enjoys writing travelogues. He mentioned this place, praising its extraordinary scenery, including the Great Longqiao, which left a deep impression on me."

Situ Longqiao sighed, "I thought it was one of the famous Five Peaks."

She then smiled broadly. "No matter, it's still good."

Because the seal Dong Budie had given her contained a rare and intriguing inscription: "Resting at the Great Longqiao of Yandang Mountain, under the starry night, unable to sleep, I jump barefoot into the grass."

After receiving the seal, she had asked many friends with rich family libraries about the Great Longqiao of Yandang Mountain, but none could provide satisfactory answers.

Chen Ping'an recalled something and smiled, "But I have good news; Yandang Mountain is very likely to become the new East Peak of Baoping Continent, promoted to one of the Crown Prince Mountains. Its future fame should grow substantially."

Situ Longqiao was taken aback. "Crown Prince Mountain? What a ridiculous title."

Then she burst into laughter. "Well, it’s still good news."

Situ Longqiao turned back to Qi Shou and flew back toward the northern city.

Guo Zhujiu rushed over and squatted beside her master for a while, whispering, "Master, don't worry; I won't tell Mistress. Mistress is great, but I still lean more toward you."

Chen Ping'an chuckled softly. "You and Sister Situ are both fairies in my hometown."

Guo Zhujiu asked curiously, "Fairies? Do they fart? If they do, does it stink? Do they intentionally hold it in their skirts? Otherwise, they wouldn't be fairies, would they? If I were a man admiring a fairy, I couldn't stand that. So, if I were a fairy, I'd just hide under the quilt, secretly fart, lift the quilt corner, and fan the wind; it shouldn't stink too much."

Chen Ping'an had long since grown accustomed to Guo Zhujiu's whimsical thoughts. He took another sip from the magic gourd, feeling the nearly depleted spirit energy revive him slightly. He patted the little girl's head and stood up. "Let's go find your mistress."

The master and disciple headed toward Ning Yao.

Guo Zhujiu hopped along, unfortunately not carrying her small bamboo box, casually asking, "Master, how many great demons did you kill this time?"

Chen Ping'an laughed. "Just staying alive is quite good enough for me."

Guo Zhujiu quickly responded, "Master, have mercy; just leave their heads for now."

Chen Ping'an asked, "How's your father doing?"

Guo Zhujiu grinned, "I ran into him on the way and he allowed me to find you first; I'll head home later."

This simple phrase, about their "chance encounter," brought warmth to Chen Ping'an's heart, lightening his mood after experiencing such a large-scale battle.

Chen Ping'an was responsible for a central position on the battlefield, not too close to Ning Yao and the others.

Guo Zhujiu wasn't afraid of the distance; being with her master, going anywhere was good. Perhaps as they walked, little Junior Sister would surpass that not-so-tall big sister.

As they walked to the left, they passed by the Jade Pith realm sword cultivator Wu Chengpei, who still hadn’t drawn his sword once, using the entire battlefield as a whetstone to refine his sword.

The Sword Qi Great Wall housed countless unique personal flying swords, some transforming into the golden body of an ancient deity, some creating talismanic formations, others entwined with lightning, unleashing the Five Thunder Law upon their release. There were also two celestial sword cultivators with their flying swords, one transforming into a dragon and another named "Eye Opener." Together, they enhanced each other’s power to a level that rivaled the sword immortals themselves. 

Such variability was astounding.

No wonder the Sword Qi Great Wall needed no other Qi cultivators.

Pang Yuanji had not left the city walls either, accompanied by a girl who admired him, Gao Youqing, the younger sister of the Gao Ye Marquis.

Seeing Chen Ping'an and Guo Zhujiu, Pang Yuanji smiled and nodded.

Chen Ping'an made use of this opportunity, smiling and asking, "Brother Pang, how many great demons have you slain?"

Pang Yuanji replied with a grin, "About the same as you."

Chen Ping'an said, "You, a great earth immortal, shouldn’t be competing with a second realm cultivator; it's unbecoming."

Guo Zhujiu ran to Gao Youqing's side, stood on her tiptoes, and patted Gao Youqing's head with a kind expression, saying, "Youqing, remember, a married woman is like spilled water; you’re not married yet, so you must restrain yourself."

Gao Youqing swatted Guo Zhujiu's hand away, glaring, "Green End, stop talking nonsense."

Yet the girl’s gaze couldn’t help but drift toward the elegant Pang Yuanji in white.

Chen Ping'an and Guo Zhujiu continued on, with Chen Ping'an noticing a young man on the city walls passionately gesticulating and signaling Guo Zhujiu to be quiet.

However, just a few steps later, Guo Jianlong felt something was off and quickly realized who the kind shopkeeper was. Without hesitation, he called his friends and hastily flew back to the city.

Over by Ning Yao, two unfamiliar faces appeared.

They were Chen Shi, a disciple of the pure Confucians, and Qin Zhengxiu, a gentleman from the school at the base of the Posa Continent.

Neither of them had engaged in demon slaying like Liu Xianyang; it was simple: they weren’t sword cultivators, and the demon army had no chance of approaching the city walls, so they couldn’t be of help. Moreover, the sword cultivators’ techniques relied on tight coordination and impeccable execution, while Chen Shi and Qin Zhengxiu's spells and abilities, despite their great power, could easily become a hindrance.

Thus, the two close friends were primarily there to explore, walking along the city walls before returning to greet Chen Sanqiu and the others during a lull in the battle.

Having previously taken the "Righteous Qi" from the Sword Qi Great Wall, the pure Confucian gentleman had quickly become close friends with Qin Zhengxiu, and they had both entered the ranks of gentlemen at the same time.

That gentleman hoped that Qin Zhengxiu would send his regards.

Qin Zhengxiu was chatting with Die Zhang.

Die Zhang was discussing the intricacies of the recent battle, explaining that the Sword Qi Great Wall didn’t need to rush to maximize their casualties early on. Instead, they would gradually tighten the front lines to slowly whittle down the demon army. Yet, should the moment of urgency arrive with the demon army at their doorstep, many sword immortals would leave the city walls to firmly hold the front lines, cutting the battlefield while the earth immortal sword cultivators led the charge down to engage the demons.

The lower-ranked sword cultivators of the Middle Five Realms would only need to defend the city walls.

Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo were crouched to the side, watching the excitement while secretly laughing, mimicking the shopkeeper’s stance, as if they were farmers observing the harvest.

It was rare to see Die Zhang speaking softly and quietly with others.

Ning Yao closed her eyes to meditate.

After Qin Zhengxiu introduced himself and mentioned his relationship with the pure Confucian gentleman, Ning Yao rarely spoke more, leaving the crowd to independently nurture her sword intent.

Dong Huafu was chatting with Fan Dazhe about what to eat and drink upon returning to the city. Dong Huafu praised Fan Dazhe for his commendable performance and suggested buying a jug of Qing Shen Mountain wine to celebrate.

Suddenly, Chen Shi spoke up, "There should have been a traitorous sword cultivator who, at the cost of a personal flying sword, secretly sent messages to the demon race."

This was not a particularly popular assertion.

This was likely one of the reasons why Chen Shi found himself at odds with many as soon as he left his family.

However, Ning Yao and the others showed no unusual expressions.

"Whether it rains or the daughter gets married, the shop must make money. Who can stop that?"

Dong Huafu turned to say, "To survive, one must at least pay the price of a personal flying sword. I’ve heard that ordinary scholars who don’t cultivate have considerable knowledge, but they can’t endure pain. What’s that saying? Without a knife at home, no well in the backyard, it looks too ugly to hang oneself—too hard and cold water?"

Qin Zhengxiu furrowed his brow.

Chen Shi instead laughed, "There are indeed such sayings. We can’t help it; there are simply too many scholars in the Righteous Qi World, both good and bad, and all types of people."

Dong Huafu cast a glance at the young scholar and nodded, "You’re quite agreeable; treat me to a drink later."

Chen Shi found it amusing and asked, "Aren't you the one treating me?"

Dong Huafu chuckled, "Dazhe, come on."

Fan Dazhe immediately replied helplessly, "Even shopkeepers can't make Dong Heitan spend money."

Qin Zhengxiu turned to see two newcomers approaching—one was a young man in a law robe from the clothing workshop, carrying a long sword from the sword workshop, his face pale and resembling a sickly person lacking combat prowess. But thanks to Liu Xianyang, Qin Zhengxiu recognized him as Chen Ping'an from the Baoping Continent, now a direct disciple of the Confucian sage, and the younger junior brother of the sword immortal Zuo You. Previously, when Liu Xianyang and Chen Ping'an had fought side by side, Qin Zhengxiu had been thoroughly impressed, realizing that Liu Xianyang had hidden talents. Even Chen Shi, who had a good relationship with Liu Xianyang, was discovering for the first time that Liu Xianyang was a sword cultivator.

Chen Ping'an smiled and bowed. "Greetings, gentlemen."

Qin Zhengxiu and Chen Shi returned the bow in kind.

Dong Huafu muttered, "A disciple of the Ascendant Saints meeting a disciple of the Confucian sage; even if they don’t fight, they should at least argue."

Ning Yao opened her eyes and said, "I’m off."

Chen Ping'an summoned his talismanic boat and stepped onto the ferry.

Qin Zhengxiu and Chen Shi declined Chen Ping'an's invitation, saying they wanted to stroll around the Sword Qi Great Wall a bit longer.

The talismanic boat headed north.

On the ferry, aside from Chen Ping'an, everyone else was a sword cultivator.

Chen Ping'an and Guo Zhujiu sat to one side, rowing vigorously. 

Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo were on the other side, also putting in effort.

Dong Huafu shook his head. "This is embarrassing."

Fan Dazhe wholeheartedly agreed.

Over on the city walls, Qin Zhengxiu watched the scene unfold. 

On the ferry, aside from Chen Ping'an, everyone was a sword cultivator but none were using their swords.

Chen Shi laughed and said, "Liu Xianyang often brags about how clever your hometown’s Chen Ping'an is, how quickly he learns. Aside from being a bit taciturn and not loving to talk, he seems to have no faults. At first, he confidently assured me that Chen Ping'an would become the best kiln worker in the world. Later, Liu Xianyang stopped mentioning the dragon kiln."

Qin Zhengxiu remarked, "Perhaps Liu Xianyang himself didn’t expect that Chen Ping'an would become a disciple of the Confucian sage."

Chen Shi glanced at the receding talismanic boat. "I guess Chen Ping'an didn’t anticipate that Liu Xianyang would become a sword cultivator either."

He sighed, "My sister once said that the Li Zhu Dongtian in the Baoping Continent is a land of heroes and spirits; it’s a treasure of feng shui."

Inside the Jia Shen tent, the sword cultivator Yu Si entered. Aside from Li Zhen, everyone’s gaze turned toward him.

The young man in wooden sandals inquired, "How is it?"

Yu Si smiled, "This is impressive. I can tell he’s a sword cultivator, not a Confucian practitioner cultivating righteousness; his swordsmanship is exceedingly profound."

At this point, Yu Si raised his arm, a faint scent of blood wafting out. "Look, the law robe is completely unharmed."

Yu Si rolled up his sleeves, revealing bloodied and mangled arms that had been wrapped in several golden pages. He chuckled, "Lucky I had some protective items; otherwise, even if I didn’t die, I’d have lost a layer of skin to his undetected sword intent."

The boy in wooden sandals asked, "How did Liu Xianyang strike?"

Yu Si shook his head. "I'm afraid I really don't know; he came out of nowhere… It felt like just a glance from the seniors would give me goosebumps."

The boy frowned. "Was Liu Xianyang's sword energy too fast, so fast that it could pierce through the rivers of time without causing any ripples? For example, Qi Shou, who just broke through, his flying sword named Heart String has the innate ability to minimize the natural resistance of time on the sword, thus making it extremely fast. Or is Liu Xianyang's personal flying sword even more unusual?"

A young woman interjected, "The Great Sword Immortal Han Huaizi from the North Julu Continent and a new sword immortal from the Tai Hui Sword Sect, Liu Jinglong, both possess exceptionally intricate and strange personal flying swords. Although I don't know their names, one is known as 'Near the Path.'"

Yu Si shook his head with a smile, shaking his arm, feeling a bit of pain for those few golden pages that had been destroyed. "His realm shouldn’t be that high; he definitely isn’t an Upper Five Realms sword immortal. It’s just that his swordsmanship is quite peculiar."

A communication flying sword arrived at the Jia Shen tent.

After reading the confidential message, the young man in wooden sandals revealed a smile.

Inside the tent, everyone shared a look of amusement.

The young man in wooden sandals stood up, walked around the desk, and with his fingers together, drew a circle in the air.

Within the tent, a large scroll about ten feet high appeared suspended.

He spoke in a serious tone, "The Gui Wei tent has sent intelligence to all the military tents. This is the distribution map of the Sword Qi Great Wall’s stationed forces, detailing the approximate duties of each Upper Five Realms sword immortal, their relatively fixed positions, which are all noted in the letter. In addition, the powerful Nascent Soul sword cultivators and all the significant Golden Core sword cultivators are also specifically documented, particularly focusing on the youngest geniuses like Ning Yao, with some Dragon Gate and Viewing Sea cultivators marked individually."

He began to announce the names of important sword immortals and cultivators, including their positions and specific duties for defending the city. Every time he mentioned a name, the young woman would write it down on the scroll. Fortunately, everyone inside the Jia Shen tent had keen eyesight; even if their realms were not high, they could clearly read the small writing on the scroll.

The names on the scroll were color-coded: gold, vermilion, and black, corresponding to Upper Five Realms sword immortals, Nascent Soul sword cultivators, and all Middle Five Realms sword cultivators, including Golden Core.

The young man in wooden sandals emphasized, "Anyone whose name appears here, even if they seem insignificant with black ink, the lower their realm, the more we need to find opportunities to eliminate them."

The young woman responded, "Then I will circle these special names in gold ink?"

The young man nodded. "Yes, for instance, the daughter of sword immortal Guo Jia, Guo Zhujiu, and the younger sister of the Gao Ye Marquis, Gao Youqing."

On the scroll, there were the ten pinnacle sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall, alongside prominent figures like the great sword immortal Yue Qing, the head of the Yao family, Yao Lianyun, and the great sword immortal Li Tui from the North Julu Continent.

In previous sieges, the great demons of the wild world had not overlooked such details, but regardless of considerations, they could never keep pace with changes.

This time, the wild world had sixty military tents, including the Jia Shen tent, housing nearly five thousand cultivators. While the Jia Shen tent focused exclusively on their territory's battlefield situation, many other military tents needed to address specific major matters.

This was because the Jia Shen tent was relatively special, having too many potential sword immortals that they didn't need to worry about distractions. The Suspended Mountain’s Li Zhen, Bei Qi, Yu Si, and the young female sword cultivator Liu Bai, all five of the sword cultivator seeds gathered from the wild world, were present here.

In other military tents, such as the Gui Wei tent, they needed to pay extra attention to the movements of the main sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall, recording the strikes of every sword immortal on the city walls—why they struck, whom they struck at, the power and lethality of their strikes, whether they broke through their realms, and critically, whether they had purposefully held back their strength. If they did, they would be marked for review, observing whether their future performance on the battlefield would remain "courteous." If the answer was affirmative, it would lead to a reduction in the forces stationed at the corresponding military tents, ensuring that their offensive was not overly aggressive but also not too obvious. Otherwise, if both sides reached a tacit understanding yet the Sword Qi Great Wall saw through their intentions, there would be dire consequences for the sword immortal involved, especially given Chen Qingdu's temperament.

In this way, setting an example would deter the sword immortals from secretly showing goodwill.

The Xin Mao tent was responsible for the specific allocation of all Upper Five Realms cultivators within their own army to other military tents on the battlefield.

The Geng Yin tent managed military supplies. The Yi Wei tent was in charge of leading the subsequent forces to their predetermined positions behind the battlefield, setting up camp and preparing to move to the battlefield at any time, while also arranging appropriate advance routes.

As for why the pinnacle great demons of the wild world seemed mostly absent, aside from a handful, it was because they were all very busy. Launching an all-encompassing assault on the Sword Qi Great Wall was unprecedented in the history of the wild world. Behind the battlefront, numerous unruly factions did not obediently follow orders. 

Some particularly powerful great demons truly lacked judgment and thus needed to be suppressed. Additionally, many feigned compliance while secretly hiding their resources, and the most troublesome were the sword immortals who refused to act as proper sword immortals, instead taking on the roles of insidious assassins. They specifically targeted the leaders of the advancing demon forces in the north, hindering each troop's movement.

When a sword immortal was determined to kill and flee, it posed a tremendous problem.

Defeating a cultivator and killing a cultivator were worlds apart.

Why did they know Chen Ping'an was baiting them, yet the Jia Shen tent still wanted to kill him? Because Chen Ping'an had killed Li Zhen, which was not as simple as merely winning; a being like him, once fully grown, would become a massive headache, making it worth the Jia Shen tent's investment of an Upper Five Realms sword cultivator to target him. However, at that time, they had insufficient information, and without accurately evaluating the methods and lethality of the Aiai sword immortal Xie Songhua, the Jia Shen tent paid a heavy price, with the young man in wooden sandals unhesitatingly taking the blame for this oversight, even though it might cost him a chance to have his lineage recorded and named by the Suspended Mountain.

In war, people die—many people. It’s not a game. As long as they win, everything can be rectified casually. However, if they lose, the future rulers of the wild world will be uncertain.

The territory of the wild world was likely two times larger than that of the Righteous Qi world.

In comparison to the relatively prosperous Righteous Qi world, the wild world, in many ways, resembled a hollow shell—its lands barren and its resources scarce. 

While it certainly had unique advantages, it still paled in comparison to its neighbor.

Yet this enormous disparity was drawn from comparing one whole world against another.

Moreover, the demon race reproduced rapidly and expanded their lineage.

In addition, demon cultivators faced virtually no moral restraints.

There were also vast dynasties occupying extensive territories, possessing fertile lands that other factions coveted, and many spiritually rich locations rumored to rival the Righteous Qi world and the Qingming world in terms of their blessed lands.

Yu Si took a swig of cheap liquor, wiped his mouth, and laughed. "That Chen Ping'an, I caught a few glimpses of him on the battlefield. As Tu Tan said, very cunning; going against him in battle is quite troublesome."

Li Zhen replied, "The opponent's realm has dropped, and since he isn’t an innate sword cultivator, his current strikes must be quite strained. He’s managed to hold down his territory thanks to the support of Liu Xianyang and Qi Shou. Even so, calculating the lethality of his flying sword and the enemy's combat strength, paying attention to details, and engaging in a war of attrition are his strengths."

The young woman added, "To deal with this guy, we must form a crushing advantage."

The young man in wooden sandals asked, "So how about we attempt an encirclement? Li Zhen, you focus on the attack, Yu Si helps suppress him, while Tu Tan takes care of cleanup. Whether it works, we can try it out and see."

Beike suddenly said, "Replace Li Zhen with me."

Li Zhen's expression darkened.

Beike added, "It’s my master’s intention."

Only then did Li Zhen’s expression brighten a little.

Among the great demons at the peak of the wild world, even the notorious master of the bleached bones, Bai Ying, or the Lord of the Yaluo River, faced heavy criticisms.

Only Beike's master was a more easily seen figure; he roamed the world year-round, having no sect or residence, yet rarely faced any controversy. 

It was often said that if he had been willing to fight in that thirteen-person conflict, there would have been no subsequent troubles in the two siege battles.

Yet, he had directly refused. 

Two great demons who had broken their oaths perished, while several sect disciples lost their minds and sought revenge against him.

As a result, he never drew his sword, casually obliterating the leading Jade Pith realm demon with just a single punch, or so it was said. 

The other cultivators were all slain one by one by that young rogue sword cultivator Beike, leaving only a few fortunate ants to escape back to their respective sects, carrying messages before hurriedly returning to apologize. Eventually, the two Jade Pith realm demons became good subordinates to the master and disciple, serving them for several years and helping Beike nourish his sword.

The rule of the wild world was simple, straightforward: the bigger the fist, the more reason one holds.

If the wild world had its own authoritative history, every page would be drenched in blood.

Many factions, having barely formed the shape of a dynasty or a great nation, were trampled and destroyed by the capricious peak great demons. 

Many capitals painstakingly built over generations by various monarchs could be turned to ruins in a single night, strewn with blood.

For example, the bleached bone great demon Bai Ying and his six trusted generals were notorious for converting vast territories into cemeteries, all reduced to skeleton puppets and raising them like insects, ultimately leaving only a few usable materials.

Only sword cultivators, regardless of their level, could survive the various inexplicable disasters.

Because this was the rule set by the Suspended Mountain.

The seeds of sword cultivators in the wild world were treated even better than the seeds of scholars in the Righteous Qi world.

This was indeed the most curious matter; the common enemy of the wild world was the Sword Qi Great Wall and its sword cultivators.

Yet no matter how the wild world attempted to besiege the city and how dismal their attempts became, they maintained a pure respect for the sword immortals and sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

In the heat of battle, they showed no mercy.

Once the battle concluded, demon cultivators who had personally experienced the conflict might harbor deep-seated hatred toward the sword immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall, yet none would dare to curse or disparage them.

(End of Chapter)

 **Chapter 733: Sword Forging (II)**

Ning Yao returned to the Ning residence alone, claiming she needed to enter seclusion to forge a sword.

The others spent the evening drinking at the Stacked Peaks Tavern, where Fan Dacheng had already resigned himself to his fate of treating everyone after borrowing money. The drinking session progressed quickly; Chen Sanqiu and the others had already gone home, while Guo Zhujiu flew over rooftops to see the little bamboo box he hadn’t seen in a long time, feeling a deep sense of longing.

In the end, only the tavern's head steward, the second steward, and a crowd of thirsty patrons remained. Business was bustling, and Chen Ping'an squatted by the roadside, drinking. 

To his surprise, Yu Jianfu and Zhu Mei had also come over to drink.

Yu Jianfu held a wine jug and approached Chen Ping'an. The sword cultivator, who had been joking with the second steward, immediately laughed and made way, one more considerate than the other.

Yu Jianfu sat down on the steps beside him, while Zhu Mei stood nearby, her demeanor lacking the heroic flair that Sister Xi had in the martial world, something that was hard for a young girl to learn.

Yu Jianfu asked, “Chen Ping'an, your boxing techniques aren’t widely known in the Baoping Continent?”

Chen Ping'an shook his head, “Very few people learn it, just a handful. If we measure by the number of practitioners, it’s a minor boxing style. But in terms of the depth of boxing intent, it’s a major style.”

Yu Jianfu nodded, “Chen Ping'an, strive to enter the Realm of Far Journeys soon. Whether you and Cao Ci are considered geniuses or not, it’s not a bad thing if you’re ahead on the martial path, at least for me. Don’t be like those practitioners on the mountains, walking on a narrow path alone.”

Chen Ping'an raised his wine bowl and smiled, “Let’s encourage each other.”

After finishing his drink, Yu Jianfu left with Zhu Mei.

Chen Ping'an called out to the child Taoban before returning to the Ning residence. Upon reaching the entrance, he suddenly told Bai Momo, who was waiting, that he needed to return to the city wall for a moment.

He boarded the spirit boat and left the city, passing by the private residences of various sword immortals below.

Upon reaching the city wall, he first sought out his senior brother, Zuo You.

After sharing his thoughts, Zuo You smiled, “It’s best that you think this way; it saves me some trouble. With your current level of cultivation, what can you achieve? Ultimately, the direction of the greater situation will unfold as it should. Your small adjustments are nice but limited in their usefulness. However, before we get to that, I have a question for you. Setting aside realms and identities, just consider a possibility: if you were to die here, would it protect the Sword Qi Great Wall? Would you choose to die?”

Chen Ping'an fell silent.

Zuo You continued, “Anyway, it’s just an impossible possibility, so whatever answer you hold in your heart is yours to know. Don’t strain yourself too much; how can you contend with heaven and earth? Don’t think that overthinking is necessarily a bad thing. As Confucians say, there is a sequence to things, beginnings and ends; knowing the order is the way to approach the path. Buddhism teaches gradual enlightenment and sudden insight. Daoism speaks of accumulating knowledge like grains of millet. Take your time.”

Chen Ping'an gazed southward at the battlefield, softly replying, “Senior brother’s teachings will be etched in my heart.”

Zuo You recalled something and said, “In learning, you must not be negligent. I’ll give you two more little questions to ponder. Why do Buddhism and Daoism differ so much in their approach to sculpting statues of deities? And regarding the four great Bodhisattvas of Buddhism—wisdom, compassion, practice, and vow—if you were to follow the order of your teacher, which comes first for the best outcome? Is it wisdom first, leading to compassion, generating great vows, and then practicing? Or is it compassion first, making vows, and gaining wisdom through practice? Think about it.”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “Understood.”

Then he forced a bitter smile, “Senior brother, these are not small questions at all.”

Zuo You replied, “To me, they’re small questions. To your teacher, they’re not even issues.”

Chen Ping'an took his leave and, feeling a slight shift in his heart, decided not to visit the old sword immortal. Instead, he found himself confronted with another task.

Zuo You frowned, “Can’t you be a little more straightforward? Must you keep making things difficult for my little junior brother?”

If it weren’t for the old sword immortal’s high skills, Zuo You would have said something snarky.

Chen Qingdu approached Zuo You, hands clasped behind his back, grinning, “Having the highest sword skills is great; it keeps me feeling refreshed every day.”

Chen Qingdu’s gaze fell upon a remote small realm.

Inside this small realm was a proper academy, where a man in Confucian robes was imparting knowledge to a group of young students.

He began by discussing the foundational aspects of poetry, using the lines “The sun sets behind the mountains” and “Spring grass grows by the pond” as examples, explaining how these seemingly simple phrases actually capture the essence of nature and leave little room for later generations.

This scholar, known as Zhou Mi, was backed by a screen painted with exquisite landscapes, while his desk was cluttered with books and scholarly items, including the Four Treasures of the Study and various small tools.

The more extravagant the spiritual artifacts, often mere trinkets from the common cultivators or wealthy clans in the wild world, the more they were revered as treasures by many demon cultivators from the savage realms.

Zhou Mi was actually the second-highest-ranking major demon in the Abyss of Ancient Wells, second only to the gray-robed elder, and even ranked higher than the burly man Liu Cha who carried a sword on his back.

He was regarded as the “Ocean of Learning” in the wild world, the Mount of Moonlight in the realm of knowledge.

He was well-versed in a wide array of subjects, excelling in Confucianism, Buddhism, and Daoism, as well as poetry, calculations, calligraphy, painting, and phonetics.

Zhou Mi referred to himself as an old bookworm and was known as the Old Fox of Heaven.

Among his students were Shoucheng, Cai Ying, Tong Xuan, Tong Yin, Yu Zao, and Liubai from the Jia Shen account, all of whom were now considered top seeds among the Sword Immortals.

Furthermore, a significant number of his earlier disciples had become notable figures in the realms of military, commerce, and the arts.

All students under Zhou Mi’s tutelage had to wait until they broke through the Sword Qi Great Wall to be given their surnames.

In fact, the one responsible for compiling this genealogy was Zhou Mi himself.

Legend has it that the ancient demon Bai Ying once curiously asked, “Is Mr. Zhou aiming to become the head of education in our world?”

Zhou Mi replied with a smile, “Not enough.”

Today, Zhou Mi once again shared some trivial wisdom about being naive in life and worldly in deeds, and it went on for nearly half an hour.

He often first asked his students for their answers, and as the esteemed teacher, Zhou Mi would then provide his own. If anyone offered a particularly astute answer, he would directly reward them with a scholarly item; today, he gifted a student a seal inscribed with “Endless Streams and Mountains.”

When Zhou Mi first began teaching, he openly told all his first-generation students that the scholars of the Great Harmony had ceased to value principles, and there were reasons for this. The complexities of right and wrong, good and bad, were very intricate. However, the scholars of the wild world had yet to reach such a level; they simply lacked the qualifications to claim everyone is right because their foundation was too poor. Thus, at the beginning of their studies, they needed to harbor respect. All of Zhou Mi’s students had only one task: to copy the classics of a hundred schools each day.

Today’s final question was about the relationship between people and time.

This touched upon a fundamental principle. Zhou Mi firmly believed that the demon race had gained enlightenment, transforming into human forms, but only those who read books could truly be considered human.

With a smile on his face, Zhou Mi began to elaborate on his thoughts.

Before the age of ten, time flowed like a gentle stream, so slow that it felt like one would never grow up, unable to see the distant scenery.

After twenty, one hardly cared about the passage of time, indifferent to its speed; even a moment spent looking around seemed wasteful.

By thirty, time began to sprint, catching people off guard.

By forty, it resembled a mighty river rushing towards the sea.

After sixty, it transformed again into a tranquil lake, motionless.

At the moment of death, it felt like a waterfall suddenly plunging into a deep pool.

Some students understood this concept well, while others seemed indifferent.

Zhou Mi didn’t differentiate; he simply smiled and said, “The purer the knowledge appears, the less substantial its meaning seems. However, in my opinion, true authority in the world isn’t about holding a high position or having a strong fist, but rather how deeply one can truly influence the hearts of others. If you can absorb this, great; if not, it doesn’t matter. As long as you have a skill to stand by, you will always have opportunities to rise step by step. The path of the Great Way is truly magnificent; once you reach the Great Harmony, you may pick as you please.”

As Zhou Mi spoke, he turned to gaze at the painted screen, which was actually focused on a certain spot on the city wall of the Sword Qi Great Wall, smiling as he said, “Don’t claim that heaven is high and has no ears or eyes; don’t say that the earth is thick and has no compassion.”

Chen Qingdu laughed, “You still have a long way to go to establish your teachings.”

As night fell, a somewhat awkward man entered through a newly opened gate in the Hanging Mountain, coming from the Sword Qi Great Wall to the Respect Sword Pavilion.

Accompanying him was Yan Zuo, who had cast an illusionary spell, and Yan Ming, the head of the Yan family, who had conducted business across continents in the Great Harmony for countless years.

The Respect Sword Pavilion had already closed its doors to customers, so only the two of them walked through, with the awkward man starting to collect the paintings of the sword immortals one by one.

The head of the Yan family said, “Chen Ping'an, please help carve a seal. I’ll have Yan Zuo deliver the blank seal to the Ning residence later; I’ll pay you two grains of rain. You don’t need to think of the inscription; just write five words: ‘Entering the City is Like Visiting a Grave.’”

As Chen Ping'an folded up a painting, he thought for a moment and asked, “Can I add five more words?”

Yan Ming laughed, “What do you mean?”

Chen Ping'an replied, “When drawing the sword, it’s like offering wine.”

Yan Ming paused for a moment, then nodded, “I won't let you add five words for free; that’ll cost you two grains of rain.”

Chen Ping'an shook his head, “Uncle Yan, no need for payment.”

Yan Ming asked, “Is it too little, so you’d rather not have it?”

Chen Ping'an was left speechless.

Yan Ming gestured for Chen Ping'an to continue his work, remaining indifferent as he said, “Scholars who can strike with fists and swords at the Sword Qi Great Wall should speak a little more heartfelt truth. If I weren't a businessman, I’d think every word deserves compensation.”

Chen Ping'an carefully put away the paintings.

He couldn’t guess why the old sword immortal wanted him to do this, why he had to come to the Respect Sword Pavilion to retrieve all the sword immortal paintings. 

He just followed orders.

The two exited the Respect Sword Pavilion together. As Chen Ping'an descended the steps, he suddenly said, “Uncle Yan, can I sit here for a moment?”

Yan Ming nodded, “I’ll wait for you at the gate; don’t linger too long.”

After Yan Ming left, the night grew deep and quiet, with only a single moon in the sky of the Great Harmony.

Alone, Chen Ping'an sat on the steps, lost in thought.

Loving someone means taking care of her for a lifetime, dedicating your life to her.

I leave first, and the last thing I see is her. She leaves first, and the last thing she sees is me.

Can I find a friend to drink the best wine without caring about the price? To enjoy even the worst wine without reservation?

Can I keep alive some of those who have passed? As long as I remember their words and actions, I’ll feel I haven’t done enough.

Growing up isn’t just the slow passage of time; it’s not simply moving from one place to another; often it happens in an instant.

Where the heart desires, the flying sword follows; both body and soul are free.

But how exactly does one become a sword cultivator?

For some reason, the ancient remnant sword intent of the Sword Qi Great Wall seemed to not favor Chen Ping'an at all.

He released a breath, stood up, and made up his mind. Even without a particularly suitable personal item, he would make do this time, gathering the five elements, and he should quickly return to the third realm of Qi Cultivation, the Liu Jin Realm.

However, this move was akin to forcing growth in a plant that should be nurtured over time; afterward, it would likely lead to a prolonged stagnation.

Quietly, he returned with Yan Ming to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Following the old sword immortal’s earlier instructions, Chen Ping'an handed over the item containing all the paintings to Yan Ming, while he himself headed back to the Ning residence.

On the city wall, Chen Qingdu retrieved the item from Chen Ping'an, but instead of opening it to take out all the sword immortal paintings, he used a forbidden technique to return it to Yan Ming, saying, “Give it back to that kid; tell him the item has a minor issue and can’t be opened for now. We’ll discuss it later.”

Yan Ming left the Sword Qi Great Wall with a forced smile.

Chen Qingdu and Zuo You stood and sat, respectively, gazing into the distance.

Suddenly, Chen Qingdu asked, “Is your little junior brother a fool? Didn’t he already have that last item related to the five elements? Why hasn’t he refined it?”

Zuo You replied, “That’s the work of the Fire Dragon True Person, and it pertains to the fundamental true qi of pure martial artists. Given Chen Ping'an’s current level, he can’t separate it at all. One misstep could lead to losing everything. Chen Qingdu, don’t go speaking flippantly here. Do you want the Qi Cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall to fall three realms, or the pure martial artists to fall another realm before you’re satisfied?”

Chen Qingdu laughed, “Is your senior brother a freeloader? Why aren’t you helping out?”

That statement hit home because Zuo You truly couldn’t do anything.

The sword skills were too high, and the sword qi too abundant, making it easy to clash with the buried treasure of the Fire Dragon True Person, turning Chen Ping'an’s entire personal realm into a battlefield.

To be honest, as long as Chen Qingdu didn’t act, no one else could do it within the Sword Qi Great Wall.

But who would dare ask Chen Qingdu to do anything?

Zuo You indeed dared, but he knew that as long as Chen Qingdu himself wasn’t willing, it would be useless.

After a moment of silence, Chen Qingdu asked, “Can Chen Ping'an endure hardship?”

Zuo You nodded, “He can.”

Chen Qingdu smiled and asked, “If you want me to help strip away that fire seed and refine it into the fifth personal item, it will require some cost, and Chen Ping'an will need to walk a path similar to the one that shapes true spiritual deities. Rest assured, it’s only similar, not exactly the same. Otherwise, forget about him; even the old scholar would fight me.”

Zuo You hesitated for the first time.

Zuo You was troubled.

Chen Qingdu clicked his tongue, “What a waste of being a senior brother. You’re not as straightforward as the little junior brother. Chen Ping'an has already agreed.”
