Zuo You immediately stood, “I’ll guard the formation. As for what happens on the city wall, I won’t concern myself; I’ll make up for any missed strikes later.”

Chen Qingdu pressed a hand on Zuo You’s shoulder, smiling, “Zuo You, it seems you still don’t trust your little junior brother.”

Zuo You furrowed his brow and asked, “What’s the chance?”

Chen Qingdu held up a finger, “One chance out of one. Isn’t that enough?”

Zuo You was skeptical.

Chen Qingdu laughed, “With your sword skills so high, would I dare deceive you?”

Zuo You drew his sword from its sheath.

The entire Sword Qi Great Wall immediately sensed the anomaly.

Chen Qingdu, however, shifted slightly, grasping the sword’s edge, allowing the long sword to slide past his palm.

On the city wall, brilliant sparks erupted.

A battle erupted again. This time, Liu Xianyang wasn’t present and stayed by Chen Chunan’s side.

Once again, it was Chen Ping'an and Qi Shou acting as neighbors.

Qi Shou felt something was off; today, Chen Ping'an seemed a bit different.

Still clad in his robe from the clothing shop, he had a jade bamboo folding fan tucked at his waist. He turned to Qi Shou, smiling, “It’s only been a few days, but Qi brother’s demeanor surpasses the past!”

Qi Shou’s heart suddenly understood, but after another thought, he became uncertain. Heaven knows if this was yet another illusion, so Qi Shou retorted, “Keep your distance from me.”

Chen Ping'an opened his fan, gently fanning a cool breeze, carelessly summoning four flying swords, before shaking his head and sighing, “Qi brother, who gave you the confidence to look down on a third-realm great cultivator with a mere Essence Infant realm?”

Qi Shou ignored him, yet today he was particularly ruthless in striking down enemies.

Originally, Qi Shou wanted to ask why Zuo You had abruptly struck earlier, but now he didn’t want to say a word.

On the wall near the thatched hut, Zuo You silently inquired of the old sword immortal, “If the refinement of the personal item is successful and he endures that hardship, can he then nurture a personal flying sword? What would its quality be?”

Chen Qingdu looked confused, “Did I ever say that? Is there such a good deal in the world? A personal flying sword can’t be freely given.”

Zuo You turned his gaze toward the elderly figure at the entrance of the thatched hut.

Chen Qingdu composed himself and said, “I once borrowed a locust wood sword box. What’s borrowed must be returned, but I’ll let Chen Ping'an become a sword box first, or rather, a sword sheath. As for whether he can nurture a personal flying sword that is exceptionally gifted and naturally born, and what quality it will have, that depends on his own fortune.”

Zuo You took a deep breath and flew out from the city wall, once again departing the city with his sword, all alone, seeking out the great demon of the Ascended Realm.

In the secret chamber of the Ning residence.

A third-realm cultivator and a seventh-realm pure martial artist, Chen Ping'an, had only the shadow of his spirit travelling far into the Sword Qi Great Wall. His true body and external spirit remained in the Ning residence.

Because the old sword immortal said that the thoughts accumulated by that shadow were far too many and too mixed; no matter how he washed the sword, he couldn’t bring forth purity. Even if he did achieve a pure bright realm, that wouldn’t be Chen Ping'an anymore.

Chen Ping'an held his breath, focusing his mind, and the thoughts that circled in his heart repeatedly were words from a book—“The spirit soars to the extremes, the mind travels ten thousand fathoms, quietly contemplating, thoughts connecting across millennia.”

As his mind quieted, almost as if in deep sleep, only two thoughts from deep within his heart slowly drifted like a dragon swimming in the depths of a lake, yet they did not clash but rather coexisted peacefully.

Sword cultivators have freedom in body, mind, and life.

The power to kill is the greatest, surpassing the heavens!

Chen Ping'an suddenly opened his eyes and said in a deep voice, “I invite the old sword immortal to draw his sword.”

Within the secret chamber, a surge of sword light erupted.

In an instant, Chen Ping'an was left bloodied and battered, as if his golden body were made of paper, disintegrating in the blink of an eye; he was reduced to a bloody mess, and soon his limbs, organs, and even his eyeballs were completely dissolved in the sword light, leaving behind nothing but bones.

Eventually, even those bones ceased to exist.

In the endless night, a dazed young man stumbled down a road devoid of light, subconsciously moving forward.

As he walked, he came upon a hunchbacked child in straw sandals, moving slowly with a large basket on his back.

The child paused, looking up at the young man, sadness etched on his face, seemingly bewildered as to why he still struggled so much in adulthood.

Thus, the child’s heart ached, and he no longer wanted to move forward, crouching on the ground, leaning against the permanently unfilled basket of herbs, and began to sob.

The young man swayed, crouching down, staring blankly at the younger version of himself.

The two locked eyes.

The young man spoke three words.

“I’m sorry.”

Then the child wiped his tears and reached out his hand.

The young man took the child’s hand, stood up, and together they moved forward.

The young man remained bewildered, but from his heart, he began to share beautiful things he would encounter in the future, as if he completely forgot the hardships that could and could not be spoken of during growth, as if he couldn’t remember the unpleasant people and events, or the complexities of the world.

The child gradually smiled, looking up at his grown self with some longing.

Finally, the child paused, tightening his grip on the rope tied to the basket, his smile radiant, and pointed toward the road ahead for his grown self.

The young man looked up, and in the previously pitch-dark distance, a flickering light appeared, swaying uncertainly.

Suddenly.

Heaven and earth became clear, radiating brilliance.

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 734: Sword Cultivator

On the city wall, Qi Shou couldn't help but turn his head. Chen Ping'an was pulling out stacks of yellow paper talismans, feeling as if a new shop was opening. But who would buy these low-grade talismans? Were they meant for the beasts of the wilderness?

There were truly many talismans, with identical ones stacked one on top of the other. Thus, on over a dozen small hills, tall and short, there were over a thousand talismans, all accumulated somehow.

The paper was of very ordinary quality and was surely not worth much. The Sword Qi Great Wall didn’t sell such items, which clearly indicated that these were the shabby goods Chen Ping'an had brought from the Haoran world. Even the basic yellow talisman paper for Qi practitioners of the lower realms didn’t count; these were merely yellow paper talismans sold everywhere in the market. If he added a peach wood sword to the mix, they would be the typical gear of con artists wandering the foothills.

As Chen Ping'an set up his display, he turned to Qi Shou.

Qi Shou immediately felt something was off.

Chen Ping'an's gaze was as sincere as a father looking at his own son. He smiled and said, “Brother Qi, don’t miss out as you pass by. I, Chen, the good person from the Package Zhai, am entirely different from that tavern’s second shopkeeper. Don’t be fooled by the small size of my Package Zhai; I have traveled through the realms of the Bottle Continent, the Cedar Leaf Continent, and the Northern Blades Continent for many years, especially in the realm of talismans, which is renowned for its affordability and high quality. I’ve received countless gold plaques from customers who bought my talismans, all of them overflowing with gratitude and wanting to thank me—so many I can hardly stop them. Brother Qi, what do you think? We fight side by side, not just friends but better than friends. I can offer discounts; if you don’t have any divine money on you, that’s fine too—I’m open to credit, no interest. I’m very easy to negotiate with.”

Qi Shou pretended not to hear.

But he couldn’t escape Chen Ping'an’s incessant chatter. Chen Ping'an went on to explain the intricacies of over ten types of talismans, claiming that the Heaven Department's Thunder Talisman, though it stemmed from a side branch of thunder techniques, was extremely lethal. He explained how the Great River Flow Talisman was perfect for the blood-soaked battlefields and how the Soil Capture Talisman could raise mountains from the ground to impede the advance of the demon army, with the talisman summoning mountains being incredibly mystical.

Qi Shou was driven to distraction by the chatter and finally coldly replied, “Though I am but a minor Nascent Soul sword cultivator, not as impressive as the third realm master shopkeeper, I am still a sword cultivator. What use do I have for your talismans? To burn yellow paper at graves? The Sword Qi Great Wall has no such custom.”

Chen Ping'an picked up a stack of talismans, his patience unwavering, a smile still on his face as he explained to “Brother Qi,” “This is a great opportunity I obtained through countless jars of exquisite celestial wine. One drunken great sword immortal accidentally revealed a heavenly secret and privately taught me this ‘Pass Talisman.’ Pass means that it can let living people through, and on the battlefield, it can certainly send enemies to the underworld. Brother Qi, are you really not tempted? The great battle has not yet truly heated up; relying solely on flying swords to slaughter beasts has lost some of its excitement. It’s just like drinking at my tavern—no matter how good the wine is, no matter how it surpasses the Sword Qi Great Wall, it ultimately needs side dishes like pickles and noodles to truly be delightful.”

Chen Ping'an switched hands and picked up another large stack of talismans, “This talisman is even more remarkable; it’s a treasured skill of the great sword immortal, the ‘Sword Qi Bridge Crossing Talisman.’ Brother Qi, your realm may not be high for now, but I believe your discerning eye is sharp. Look at how intricate it is; each seemingly small talisman is practically a true talisman array. I won’t say much more; just the celestial cinnabar needed to draw these talismans consumes so much! How can you dismiss my talismans just because the paper isn’t top-notch? Brother Qi, I didn’t expect you to be such a superficial person. I’m quite disappointed. You killed a minor deity on the battlefield, and with the same kind of back-and-forth combat, you’ve at least outdone that minor deity. With your talent, you could easily be the eldest brother among the disciples of Mount Tuo Yue…”

Qi Shou shouted angrily, “Chen Ping'an, will you ever be done?! During the war, I advise you to focus on killing enemies with your sword! Even if you dare to risk your life, don’t drag others down with you!”

Chen Ping'an set down the two stacks of talismans and gently tapped his heart with his folded fan. Looking towards the southern battlefield, he smiled, “Since Brother Qi currently has no intention to buy, that’s fine. In this world of trade, fate is the first consideration. I’ll just observe how you, a heroic figure, take down the enemy. Some people over in the city have a few comments about your methods, saying they’re too ruthless. But to me, it’s great! That bit of arrogance from your noble family background, that pride as a genius sword cultivator, that unwillingness to allow peers to surpass you—those are minor flaws. But once you step onto the battlefield, you transform into a true hero. Being able to endure a Chen Ping'an you want to kill but can’t, and even suppressing some displeasure to help me fight and defend the battlefield, this sword cultivator Qi Shou truly embodies the demeanor of a top sword immortal…”

Qi Shou took a deep breath, “Is it that as long as I don’t buy your worthless talismans, you will keep going on and on?”

Chen Ping'an opened his fan and smiled, “No need to say more, Brother Qi, just focus on wielding your sword gracefully.”

Qi Shou withdrew his gaze and continued to navigate his flying sword, slaying the demons.

Compared to the first battle, the proportion of demon cultivators in human form among the attacking army was noticeably higher this time. No longer were they merely unrefined beasts that the sword cultivators on the walls could easily crush and wouldn’t even count towards military achievements. In that opening battle, those demons weren’t really considered proper cultivators; they were primarily driven forward, only useful for creating mountains of corpses to fill the chasms that the sword immortals had opened, blood and flesh staining the ground and affecting the natural elements.

In truth, Qi Shou looked down on several types of talismans belonging to the five elemental categories, but he was indeed somewhat interested in the Pass Talisman and the Bridge Crossing Talisman, especially the latter, because there were threads of sword qi flowing through the talisman paper, making it genuine. The essence of sword intent within the talisman was not much but was exquisite, and Chen Ping'an claimed it was taught to him privately by a great sword immortal, which made Qi Shou believe a bit of it.

However, Qi Shou found it easy to defend the battlefield himself and had no intention of engaging in business with Chen Ping'an. No matter how extravagant the claims, the reputation of the second shopkeeper selling wine at the Sword Qi Great Wall was already widespread, and even those in other taverns might struggle to make a profit. Chen Ping'an himself surely knew that.

The sword cultivator replacing Xie Songhua and Liu Xianyong on the battlefield was an old Nascent Soul who fell silent upon arriving at this wall—Cheng Quan, who had dropped back to the Nascent Soul realm from the upper five realms. He preferred to sit far apart from the sword immortal Zhao Ge, with whom he had argued for half a lifetime. They were seated on opposite sides of the city wall, and if they had a disagreement, they would hurl insults at each other. In the past, Cheng Quan spoke a lot when confronting Zhao Ge, but now, without Zhao Ge, he seemed to have no opponent and remained silent.

In fact, in the southern part of the city, there was a private residence left behind by a sword immortal, obtained through military merit by Cheng Quan's ancestor and later recorded under Cheng Quan's name. Because Cheng Quan's lineage had now completely perished except for him, it was a fate similar to that of the female sword immortal Zhou Cheng.

Cheng Quan’s sword strikes were exceptionally swift. His flying sword, “Water Mountain,” created peaks that seemed carved from jade in the sky above the battlefield, smashing the demons into pulp. Should any demon cultivator manage to escape death or dodge, he would toss down more peaks. Each peak, once shattered by a formidable demon cultivator using a magical treasure, would transform into a lake of blue water, instantly freezing the battlefield upon landing, causing the demons to look up and see more mountains crashing down upon them.

So compared to the actions of the two neighbors, with Chen Ping'an unleashing four flying swords and Qi Shou slaughtering demons, the battlefield on Cheng Quan's side was exceptionally clean and clear.

What further opened Chen Ping'an’s eyes was the sight of many relatively weak demon souls being effortlessly pulled into the lakes, ultimately shattering along with the freezing waters.

Actually, Cheng Quan also had a seemingly useless personal flying sword, “Tuo Bei,” but he also possessed a significant item, name unknown, that functioned like a bonsai, placing stones as mountains and water as rivers.

Years ago, Cheng Quan’s mentor, one of the sword immortals who led hunts in the wilderness, would first refine rivers and peaks and then bring them back to the Sword Qi Great Wall for his disciple Cheng Quan to refine. After the latter summoned the small mountains and rivers from the bonsai, combined with the divine ability of his personal flying sword “Tuo Bei,” extraordinary phenomena would occur on the battlefield, with surging rivers and rising mountains, further amplified by the intent of the Tuo Bei sword.

This was why, after the Thirteen Struggles, Cheng Quan was closely pursued by a great demon and was ambushed, leading to his fall in realm. Though he might seem inconspicuous among sword immortals, on the battlefield, facing a comparable opponent like Wu Chengpei, who wielded a flying sword called “Ganlin,” he would inflict significant casualties on the attacking army from the wilderness.

As Chen Ping'an turned to look, Cheng Quan calmly said, “Shut your mouth. I have no money to be swindled.”

Chen Ping'an laughed, “Alright then.”

Qi Shou was left in disbelief. What a guy! Why was it that while both were Nascent Soul sword cultivators, Chen Ping'an became so amiable upon reaching Cheng Quan’s side?

Not only that, Qi Shou noticed that the Chen Ping'an who had just been rebuffed didn’t hold a grudge but instead tossed a jug of wine worth five snowflake coins over to the old man from a distance.

Cheng Quan opened the seal, sniffed it, and disdainfully said, “Too bland; what kind of wine is this? Women like Zhao Ge would enjoy it.”

Despite saying that, he still drank.

Unexpectedly, Chen Ping'an tossed over a jug of strong liquor freshly sold from the tavern. Cheng Quan took a sniff and nodded, “Now that’s real wine! No wonder the tavern is doing well. If you opened a tavern on the city wall, I would buy from you.”

Chen Ping'an smiled, “No credit.”

Cheng Quan shot a sideways glance at the young man and asked, “I heard you got knocked down by a little girl’s punch at the Ning residence?”

Chen Ping'an lightly tapped his palm with his folding fan and said, “To be honest with you, Senior Cheng, displaying strength to deceive the enemy is my specialty. No matter who I spar with, the odds of me winning are quite high. Like this brother Qi here beside me.”

During the second battle, with the same flying swords, Chen Ping'an was even more relaxed and comfortable, his flying swords moving faster.

When it came to maneuvering flying swords, it was indeed his forte. He didn’t have to be bound by various principles, making his intent much purer. Principles are good, but too many can weigh one down, causing the flying swords to slow down naturally. A slight difference can mean a world of difference.

Cheng Quan found the young man’s words far more interesting than those of Zhao Ge.

Thus, the old Nascent Soul directly moved his position to sit next to Chen Ping'an and asked, “I’ve heard that the Haoran world has many wondrous mountains and rivers, capable of captivating the eye and heart?”

Chen Ping'an didn’t even turn to speak but gazed ahead, smiling, “It’s just that. Once you’ve seen enough, especially when you have to tread through them, you’ll grow tired. Everywhere you look is blocked, making it hard to feel free like a bird soaring over Zhongnan. In my hometown, cultivators who dwell in the mountains for long will become so still that they yearn to move, rolling down into the mundane world, only to return to the mountains, which isn’t particularly meaningful.”

Cheng Quan regretted moving to sit next to him; this guy had just been lively, but now he was rambling on, boring and uninteresting.

Chen Ping'an took out a book of the Bi Sword Immortal’s seals from his robes, turned with a smile, and handed it to Cheng Quan, “Senior Cheng, take a look and see if there’s any seal you’re interested in. Business has been so good that almost all of them have been sold, but if you ask nicely, I can carve more and even give a discount. Even if you don’t like them, you can just sell them again for a jug or two of wine—what’s there not to like?”

Cheng Quan opened the seal book, casually flipping through a page, and exclaimed, “Beyond the business aspect, whoever picks a seal, on the surface seems to be a matter of fate, but in reality, it represents a certain attachment. Giving it to you for free not only earns a profit but also allows one to read into a person’s heart. Second shopkeeper, what a good business!”

“Reading hearts, is it better to knock or to push? I think neither is good,” Chen Ping'an said, shaking his fan with a look of grievance, “Senior Cheng, don’t take advantage of your profound sword skills, which allow you to stand out among many sword immortals, to bully a junior like me. But at this moment, while you drink, read, and strike with your sword, your sword qi flipping through the pages, killing demons while enjoying your wine, you truly embody the elegance of a cultured person.”

Though Cheng Quan casually flipped through the seal book, when it came to striking with his sword, he was by no means careless. Chen Ping'an, now back in the role of the Package Zhai, was more agile than ever in his sword strikes.

Cheng Quan paused at the edge of a seal, wanting to turn the page, but out of the corner of his eye, he noticed the shameless little brat staring right at him. The latter smiled knowingly, as if to say, “I understand, you needn’t feel embarrassed.” Cheng Quan didn’t mind anymore, reaching out to touch those words, especially the “beautiful person” at the end, which made the old sword cultivator sigh.

“Old clothes and a broken hat, old roads through green mountains and rivers, morning dew and evening glow, the stars and rivers, lights and flowers for the beautiful person.”

He, Cheng Quan, and Zhao Ge had argued for a lifetime, never knowing whom she truly liked. She only said that whoever ascended to the realm of immortals first, she would like. At that time, Cheng Quan had a higher realm and better talent, so he claimed she would definitely like him. Zhao Ge insisted that her intentions were noble, hoping to encourage Cheng Quan’s determination.

Each had their reasoning, leading to countless arguments. Once, there was a female sword immortal named Song Yun Cai from the Sword Qi Great Wall, whose elegance was unparalleled. She, Cheng Quan, and Zhao Ge all came from the same crooked alley. During the years when they were all Nascent Soul sword cultivators fighting side by side, that alley, which produced three sword immortals, became so famous that even the Hanging Mountain and the distant Yu Long Sect and Nan Po Sha Continent had heard of it.

Cheng Quan tossed the Bi Sword Immortal’s seal book back to Chen Ping'an and casually said, “Once you become a sword cultivator, don’t be too worldly.”

Chen Ping'an put away the seal book. He hadn’t made any sales at the Package Zhai today, nor did he want to give away two jugs of celestial wine, but since Cheng Quan mentioned becoming a sword cultivator, as the saying goes, “Good things come in threes.” He smiled, “I’ll take your good words, and then I’ll become a sword cultivator.”

Both fell silent and struck with their swords.

Qi Shou couldn’t help but envy that second shopkeeper—he could talk to anyone.

An hour later, Cheng Quan suddenly said, “In my opinion, aside from any fist techniques or magical treasures, you have quite a bit of quick wit; that’s your most reliable skill. If I were to let you carve that last seal, keeping the edge unchanged but changing the inscription, what would you carve? To me, the Bi Sword Immortal’s seals combined with those fan inscriptions are a jumble of words. Anyone who has read a few books can copy them; at most, it’s just a little repurposing. It doesn’t count as true skill. The disciples of the Sage of Literature have tons of knowledge; it shouldn’t be limited to just this.”

This time it was Cheng Quan’s turn to be surprised; the second shopkeeper directly took out a clean seal and said, “I’ll trouble Senior Cheng to keep an eye on my battlefield. Of course, the military merits still count as mine.”

Having Cheng Quan help to strike against the enemies was quite steady.

Chen Ping'an was boldly taking a break, recalling four flying swords, three of which he placed into the sword-rearing gourd to recuperate. He only used the fifteen flying swords as carving knives. Not only did he change the inscriptions, but he also altered the edges of the seals.

After handing it back to Cheng Quan, the latter held it in his palm, lifted it up, and with a poker face, nodded, “It’s passable.”

The seemingly appealing yet not genuinely cherished new seal was tucked into Cheng Quan's sleeve.

Old friends are also beautiful people, generous and full of strange principles.

The youthful heart has a peak, suddenly stolen away by clouds.

Inscription: “Accidental.”

Chen Ping'an wasn’t in a hurry to strike again; he let Cheng Quan help clear the battlefield, muttering to himself, “Having a great beauty in heart, I’m not afraid of being seen.”

With the jade bamboo fan gifted by his student Cui Dongshan, he fanned himself and also helped the old senior cool off, grinning, “For the seal crafted just for you, the material is top-notch, and every character is carved with care. The original price isn’t high; one Grain Rain coin, plus since Senior is a sword immortal, there’s an 80% discount. Now, helping a junior kill demons, it’s only five Shallow Summer coins!”

Chen Ping'an lowered his voice and said, “If it were me, I wouldn’t even dream of discounts; one Grain Rain coin is just one.”

Cheng Quan didn’t respond to the young man; the old sword cultivator’s expression was dazed, and slowly a smile appeared on his weathered face as he murmured, “She was the most beautiful woman in the Sword Qi Great Wall back then, truly lovely.”

At this point, Cheng Quan earnestly said to Chen Ping'an, “She was even more dazzling than your Ning Yao.”

Unexpectedly, the scholar turned his face faster than he could turn a page.

Chen Ping'an exploded, “You’re talking nonsense!”

Cheng Quan’s mood brightened instead. This familiar scene didn’t faze him at all; he just drank the wine and took the seal, feeling it was inappropriate to curse back, and laughed, “Why are you cursing?”

Chen Ping'an asked, “If you suppressed your realm to that of a third-realm cultivator, do you think I would curse you?”

Cheng Quan smiled and reminded, “Second shopkeeper, if you keep this up, I won’t be polite.”

Qi Shou felt somewhat helpless.

The old and young were arguing as if two hundred people were about to start a brawl.

Fortunately, it didn’t delay their sword strikes against the enemies.

This was normal; one was an experienced old sword cultivator while the other was a meticulous second shopkeeper.

The only thing Qi Shou hadn’t expected was that the two sides could really go at it.

It seemed that Chen Ping'an had the upper hand, as some of his insults were delivered in his hometown dialect or the refined language of another continent. Cheng Quan didn’t understand and had to guess what the other was saying. At times, Chen Ping'an would look at him with a sympathetic gaze, mixing his insults and praises in different dialects and occasionally restating them in the language of the Sword Qi Great Wall. For Cheng Quan to retort, he had to figure out the truth of those words, putting him in a difficult position. His skills honed from years of bickering with Zhao Ge had inevitably lost some edge.

It was quite lively.

When Fan Dache came to deliver wine to Chen Ping'an, his scalp tingled.

Fan Dache only dared to come once; after that, he sent Dong Huafu, who had temporarily withdrawn from the battlefield, to deliver the wine. Dong Huafu enjoyed the lively atmosphere, sitting nearby and listening intently, finding that he learned quite a bit from the excitement. Moreover, Dong Huafu’s ability to fan the flames was a unique talent that no one could replicate.

After a while, the two armies faced off without a ceasefire; Cheng Quan and Chen Ping'an welcomed another respite.

In fact, Qi Shou was the one who suffered the most.

Chen Ping'an often brought him up, calling him “my brother Qi” and mentioning how young he was, a thirty-something lad who was already a Nascent Soul sword cultivator. “If you, Senior Cheng, had any self-respect, you’d stay as far away from Qi Shou as possible. You, Senior Cheng, your realm is low, but I’ve heard you only have two flying swords. How many does Brother Qi have? The key is that every single one of Brother Qi’s flying swords is of an exceptionally high rank, something that comes around once in a millennium. How can you possibly compare?”

With Cheng Quan’s temper, once he got riled up, he wouldn’t just curse Qi Shou; he’d go after his ancestors too.

At this moment, Cheng Quan laughed and said, “Little brother Chen, after sparring with you, I’ll head back to argue with that Zhao Ge woman for sure.”

Chen Ping'an shook his fan and smiled, “Let me say something fair: I can curse both of you by myself.”

Cheng Quan glared, “You give a little color and expect me to open a dye shop, huh? Want to spar again?!”

Chen Ping'an appeared silent but was quietly communicating with Cheng Quan.

Cheng Quan seemed to weigh the pros and cons before nodding, addressing Qi Shou, “That little brat with eyes on his forehead, young Qi, I see your extraordinary roots. How about I send you an opportunity?”

Qi Shou feigned ignorance.

Cheng Quan pulled out two stacks of talismans and handed them to Qi Shou.

A moment later, Cheng Quan returned, not to Chen Ping'an’s side but to the area once occupied by the female sword immortal Xie Songhua and the scholar Liu Xianyong.

Qi Shou examined the two talismans, the Pass Talisman and the Bridge Crossing Talisman, scrutinizing them. Both types were of higher quality than he had imagined, and drawn on such crude paper, it truly felt like a waste. After hesitating for a moment, he finally communicated with Chen Ping'an in his heart, “What exactly are you scheming?”

Cheng Quan remarked that Qi Shou's personal flying sword, the Jump Pearl, had not yet been refined to perfection and, while abundant in quantity, still lacked some potency. He then shared some insights on swordsmanship that Qi Shou had to consider seriously—even if they weren’t entirely suited for his swordplay, for a Nascent Soul cultivator who could easily fall into a stagnant state, even a tiny bit of Dao insight could not be underestimated.

In addition, Cheng Quan suggested that Qi Shou might as well do business with Chen Ping'an, as it wouldn’t be a loss. If it were, he could ask Zhao Ge for compensation.

Chen Ping'an smiled, “Helping others is helping oneself.”

He added, “As for whether to give the wilderness a little surprise, that’s up to you. I’ve never done any business that forces things; it’s all about mutual consent, making money happily and spending joyfully.”

Qi Shou fell into thought.

Earlier, Cheng Quan's proposal was simple yet complex. Simple, because that Jump Pearl flying sword, which was expected to reach the status of a celestial weapon, could transform into hundreds of true swords without losing sword intent. Since the quantity was sufficient, it could be supplemented with something extra, like adding another divine ability to the personal flying sword.

Complex, however, was the so-called “supplementing,” which was an incredibly intricate process requiring talismans to assist every single flying sword. Each flying sword must link with each other, forming a talisman array, and ultimately all Jump Pearl flying swords would be transformed into a large talisman array.

Moreover, Qi Shou harbored hidden worries, fearing that Chen Ping'an, during this process, would become too familiar with his personal flying sword, the Jump Pearl.

After all, this flying sword was far more crucial to Qi Shou than his ancestral half-celestial weapon, the “High Candle.”

Whether in life-or-death battles or slaying enemies on the battlefield, once Qi Shou could wield a thousand true Jump Pearl flying swords, what kind of scene would that be?

And what kind of feeling would it evoke in those opposing him?

As Qi Shou himself said, once he left the city wall, he and Chen Ping'an would be enemies.

Chen Ping'an suddenly chuckled, “Have you ever considered that with the strength of the Qi family, as long as you thought of this, once your Jump Pearl’s rank reaches the peak, if you learn this talisman technique from me, all you have to do is follow the template and spend some money, wouldn’t you gain an unexpected harvest? Is it more of a loss for me to become familiar with the unique divine ability of the Jump Pearl or for you to gain an extra layer of genuine combat strength? Brother Qi, you decide for yourself.”

Qi Shou looked down at the two stacks of talismans that had yet to be returned, furrowing his brow. “After breaking through, I can now wield nearly seven hundred Jump Pearl flying swords. Can your yellow paper talismans really form an array? How do you calculate the price of each talisman? If they turn out to be useless, when facing a demon cultivator of the upper five realms, won’t they be easily crushed? How do you plan to handle that? The most critical point is, will you really impart all the intricacies of the talisman array to me? Let’s say I’m a purely sword cultivator; with the ongoing battles, how can I find time to learn those talismans? If you only drew a big pie, what good would it do if I paid but couldn’t enjoy it?”

Chen Ping'an clicked his tongue, “Brother Qi, you’re not being generous enough. Partnering with me in business won’t lead to losses; it will only be a matter of how much you gain! I’m not just saying this randomly; I have done things that you can all see as facts.”

Finally, Chen Ping'an turned his head, folding his fan, his expression regretful as he shook his head and sighed, “Brother Qi, do you really see me as a life-and-death enemy outside the battlefield, deserving of the Sword Immortal Dao that you treat as a trifle?”

With a flick of his fan, he summoned the two stacks of talismans back to his side and smiled, “If the trade doesn’t go through, we remain righteous. Allow me to offer you a piece of sage advice, ‘A gentleman respects what is within himself and does not envy what is in the heavens; thus, he progresses each day.’”

Cheng Quan laughed in his heart, “Is the business already in the red?”

Chen Ping'an replied, “That’s human nature; if it were me, I wouldn’t agree easily either.”

Cheng Quan nodded, “The talisman array is indeed a worthless endeavor; it’s good that Qi Shou isn’t fooled by you.”

Chen Ping'an smiled, “But I can’t say that. My talisman technique is quite hard-won. Once it’s completed, its power is indeed considerable…”

Cheng Quan paused, “Wait a moment, do you mean to say that whether it succeeds or fails, you can’t guarantee it?!”

Chen Ping'an answered, “Can I or Qi Shou guarantee that it will be completed immediately? Moreover, drawing talismans is something that requires genius and skill; it’s only natural. What’s wrong with wasting a few hundred talismans? Brother Qi has money; why fear such losses? If I had a bit less conscience, I would’ve pulled out stacks of yellow talisman paper instead; that would truly be something divine beings would feel pained over.”

Cheng Quan laughed heartily, “Little brother Chen, helping others, practicing your talisman drawing, and still making a profit; what a great scheme!”

Chen Ping'an smiled, “Aren’t you complaining about how fat the pig is before slaughtering it?”

Cheng Quan was immensely entertained.

However, Chen Ping'an finally added, “But looking at this grandest war in the world, I sincerely look forward to seeing Qi Shou unleash a thousand swords. Even if you’re not yet a sword cultivator, just imagining that scene makes my heart long for it.”

“A gentleman respects what is within himself and does not envy what is in the heavens; thus, he progresses each day.” 

This sage teaching, this good principle, actually came from the writings of Chen Ping'an's teacher. If one could envy what others possess while also respecting what is within oneself, wouldn’t that be better?

This small doubt, this trivial insight from reading, must be shared with his teacher in the future.

Qi Shou asked, “How much for each yellow paper talisman?”

Chen Ping'an tucked the fan into his waist, bent forward, and scampered over to Qi Shou, muttering, “I’ll trouble you, Brother Qi, to help me kill some enemies for a moment, and I’ll explain it to you in detail. In any case, I can guarantee that the more talismans you buy, the greater the discount! Our brotherly bond, so clear, is worth a fortune!”

Then at Qi Shou’s side, Chen Ping'an turned and shouted, “Senior Cheng, Brother Qi needs a little support here; show a bit of your senior demeanor. In no time, Brother Qi will return to the wall!”

Chen Ping'an led Qi Shou away from the city wall, squatting together at the base of the wall, piling the yellow paper talismans by his feet. He gathered his voice into a line, whispering, “Different talismans have different prices. Brother Qi isn’t the kind of person who would nitpick over details, so I’ll directly offer a fair packaged price: a thousand talismans, not one less, for only three Grain Rain coins.”

Qi Shou was about to get up and leave.

A thousand yellow paper talismans—how many silver coins could that buy in the Haoran world? At most, a few dozen.

Even if the celestial cinnabar used for drawing talismans consumed quite a bit, considering Chen Ping'an’s stingy character, being able to draw over a thousand of them would hardly yield high quality, and how many snowflake coins could it cost? At most, a few Shallow Summer coins.

Chen Ping'an didn’t stop him, just spoke to himself, “My talisman array is related to the Three Mountains and Nine Lords. Of course, it’s not just a direct copy. To be honest, with my current level, I can’t draw it up, but the fundamental of the talisman array truly has great significance, and it’s closely related. Besides that, I will definitely put forth my entire skill in drawing talismans, not holding back at all. If I can save you even one talisman, I will. Of course, it must be said beforehand; this is an ancient talisman array that has been lost for a long time, not something simple to draw. There will be some losses, so Brother Qi, prepare yourself mentally. As for how to attach sword intent to the sword body with the talismans, that is another extraordinary unique skill.”

Qi Shou squinted and smiled, “How will these thousand drawn talismans assist my flying sword? Did you plan this deal with me from the start, so each talisman is tailored for this purpose? And that even we, as neighbors, could have guessed early on?”

“Look at you, Brother Qi, using a gentleman’s heart to gauge a saint’s belly. You’ve wronged me,” Chen Ping'an said, feeling a bit embarrassed. He picked up a stack of talisman paper, rubbing his fingers over each, revealing that aside from the first and last few, the rest were blank. Chen Ping'an helplessly said, “Drawing talismans is an extremely meticulous task. Last time, when I fought with Li Zhen, I lost far too many valuable talismans. I was heavily injured, falling three realms. Brother Qi, can you imagine how painful that was? Since then, I have been stretched thin, needing to practice both my fist techniques and recover my realm. I haven’t had the chance to draw these talismans. So I forgot to mention, the labor costs for drawing the talismans and the loss of many achievements in slaying demons…”

Qi Shou coldly chuckled, “Cheng Quan helped you slay demons; you won’t lose any military merit.”

Chen Ping'an responded with a “Oh,” “In that case, let’s just discuss the labor costs for drawing the talismans. In the Haoran world, we have this custom of a ‘pen fee,’ so Brother Qi, just a token amount will do—two or three Shallow Summer coins, a mere drizzle.”

Qi Shou replied, “The Sword Qi Great Wall has no such custom.”

Chen Ping'an said, “Then three Grain Rain coins really can’t be discounted any further.”

Qi Shou said, “Are you trying to milk me dry?”

“Brother Qi, I won’t allow you to belittle yourself like this, claiming you’re getting swindled,” Chen Ping'an said, laughing heartily.

After saying this, Chen Ping'an let out a rare, hearty laugh, patting Qi Shou on the shoulder. “I’m reminded of an old friend who would still think fondly of our future reunions; Brother Qi is bound to be like him, lucky enough to live until the end.”

Qi Shou shrugged off Chen Ping'an’s hand and frowned.

Chen Ping'an raised his head and looked at Qi Shou, smiling, “It seems I haven’t misjudged you, Brother Qi; there’s no need to divide life and death on the battlefield.”

Qi Shou asked, “What do you mean?”

Chen Ping'an smiled, “You’ll have to guess.”

Qi Shou chuckled, “Aren’t you afraid I’m laying a trap for you? Don’t forget, I have many Jump Pearl flying swords; you still don’t know how many I actually possess. Can you keep your eyes on every detail of my battlefield?”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “I’m quite free; I’m good at this.”

Qi Shou recalled something.

He had heard from the family elders that all sword immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall had recently received a strange order, with each sword immortal instructed to hold back their strength at different stages.

This was definitely not something the head sword immortal would willingly do.

Willing to betray, daring to defect, that was easy enough.

As long as one hid deep enough, it could be considered a skill. But if one didn’t hide well and the head sword immortal saw through it, that would surely result in death.

So it must have been someone from outside who suggested it.

In addition, many young sword cultivators had received a peculiar talisman from the clothing workshop that could conceal their forms.

In the past, while it wasn’t that no one from the Sword Qi Great Wall could draw such talismans, no sword cultivator had ever thought it necessary.

Some sword cultivators might have wanted to do so, but they could only bury that idea deep within, suspected of cowardice.

So there were indeed outsiders who could persuade the old sword immortals to forcibly make young sword cultivators post this talisman.

Moreover, on the city wall, aside from the peak ten and certain key positions that couldn’t be moved, many sword immortals began to quietly rotate their guard positions.

Qi Shou asked, “Did you say something to the head sword immortal?”

Chen Ping'an smiled, “Now it’s not only the beasts of the wilderness who want me dead; many sword immortals who need to find a way out also want me dead.”

Qi Shou looked at him strangely, “You’re really not afraid of death? What’s your aim?”

Chen Ping'an lightly tapped his shoulder with the folding fan, “When I want to die, you wouldn’t even conceive of my methods. When I want to live, you’ll find it even harder to imagine.”

Qi Shou simply sat down on the ground, leaning against the wall, and stretched out his hand, “Bring me a jug of wine.”

Chen Ping'an sat beside him, tossing over a jug of bamboo sea cave wine, while he took down the gourd that temporarily housed his four flying swords.

Rumor had it that the spring banners from the Hanging Mountain were about to mature and drop, each gourd being of very high quality, but their price was too steep and long since had a price but no market.

Qi Shou said to Cheng Quan, “Senior Cheng, wait a moment; let me have a bit more wine.”

Chen Ping'an immediately shouted, “All the military merits from my brother Qi’s drinking skills count towards me!”

Qi Shou felt a bit helpless; he was speaking to Cheng Quan with a sincere heart.

While drinking, Qi Shou asked, “What about the old accounts between you and me?”

Chen Ping'an smiled, “The Qi family’s past bullying is all laid bare; I can actually accept it. Being strong, direct, and straightforward is another way to treat people with sincerity. This principle, whether I like it or not, I just have to endure it, as it’s too simple, too worry-free, and even allows for right and wrong to cover each other, compensating in turn. If when it comes time for me to strike with fists or swords, the previous matters remain unchanged, that’s simple—one for one, I’ll return it all to you. Qi Shou, many real difficulties are not because I look down on you; it’s in the Haoran world that it becomes heart-wrenching, filled with troubles. If you ever get the chance to visit there, remember to tread lightly.”

Qi Shou shook his head, “I’m not particularly interested in the Haoran world; I’d rather take a trip deep into the wilderness to learn from the strongest sword cultivators.”

Chen Ping'an laughed, “Wielding a sword to travel the land, leaving home for thousands of miles, without any attachments—now that’s truly a sword immortal.”

Chen Ping'an put away the sword-rearing gourd, “Let’s get to work and make some money.”

Qi Shou summoned seven hundred and thirty-two Jump Pearl flying swords, clustering them by the wall, ready to return to the wall.

Suddenly, Chen Ping'an said softly, “If all the key talismans were replaced with yellow talismans or even better paper, combining the talisman array with the sword array would be incredible. Once Brother Qi unleashes his swords from the city wall, wouldn’t the power surpass even the heavens?”

Qi Shou stopped in his tracks, curious, “How much would that cost?”

Chen Ping'an thought for a moment, looking north, and smiled, “I’m in a good mood; I’ll only charge you the same divine money.”

As Qi Shou turned around, he heard Chen Ping'an say, “Just five coins.”

Qi Shou turned his head.

Chen Ping'an asked, “Brother Qi, after our heartfelt exchange, isn’t it worth at least two Grain Rain coins?”

Qi Shou shook his head sternly, “Not worth it.”

Chen Ping'an sighed in resignation, “Brother Qi, you always look down on yourself; that’s not good.”

Qi Shou leaped up to the city wall, thanking Senior Cheng.

---

Inside the secret chamber of the Ning residence.

Chen Ping'an opened his eyes, astonished to find his body intact and unharmed.

Confused, Chen Ping'an stumbled out of the secret chamber and made his way to the training ground. The journey was eerily silent.

He didn’t see Granny Bai, walking all the way to the Dragon Slaying Cliff, as if in this vast universe, he was the only one.

Looking up, someone appeared as if parting the heavens, arriving at the training ground.

Chen Ping'an’s heart stirred; he felt inexplicably restless, in a place where he had never intentionally opened a qi abode, it stirred violently, but this strange sensation quickly faded.

The one who came to the Ning residence was the head sword immortal, merely projecting his soul out of his body.

Chen Ping'an clasped his fists, saying, “Thank you, head sword immortal, for wielding your sword, and again for shielding the heavens and earth.”

Chen Qingdu smiled, “Wielding the sword is true, but where does the shielding the heavens and earth come from?”

Chen Ping'an was even more puzzled.

Chen Qingdu said, “Over tens of thousands of years, countless sword cultivators have had their personal flying swords but remain unaware; that’s truly rare.”

Chen Qingdu chuckled, looking around and nodding, “Being in this situation, what a caged bird.”

Chen Ping'an suddenly understood.

His heart felt light and satisfied.

Chen Qingdu asked, “Capturing your enemy in the heavens and earth, is that enough? What about the second personal flying sword?”

In an instant, the space between heaven and earth was filled with flying swords, layers upon layers, densely packed, countless.

In my world, all are caged birds.

If I’m not a sword cultivator, who is?!

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 735: Betrayal

Chen Qingdu glanced at Chen Pingan.

Chen Pingan immediately sheathed the unnamed flying sword, and with a thought, all the flying swords vanished without a trace of sword light, hidden within the crucial Qi chamber, finally coalescing into a single sword.

This kind of flying sword that almost entirely disregarded the flow of time was, in fact, quite unreasonable. Its existence was thanks to this life-bound sword being placed within the small realm created by another life-bound sword. The overlapping powers of the two allowed for such an elusive effect.

The life-bound flying sword refined by a Qi practitioner, even if it had undergone great refinement, still belonged to the category of external objects. In contrast, a sword cultivator's own life-bound flying sword was a matter of life and death, possessing various unimaginable powers. 

The Song Needle Thunder was a replica from the Sword of Hatred Mountain, requiring no further explanation; it was more of a complement to talismans, utilized purely by martial artist Chen Pingan for fleeing or fighting for his life.

The first and fifteenth are genuine relics of ancient sword immortals. However, even after being greatly refined by Chen Pingan, it still couldn't unleash its powers or the subtleties of swordplay, remaining stuck at the levels of speed, resilience, and sharpness—this could be considered a waste of talent. After exhausting all his efforts, Chen Pingan had not succumbed to self-pity over the years.

As Chen Pingan retracted the mysterious powers of the other life-bound flying sword, the small realm enveloping both him and the Elder Sword Immortal Chen Qingdu dissipated.

Bai Lianshuang stood at a distance in the corridor, and upon confirming her suspicions, she turned away and wiped the corners of her eyes with the back of her hand.

In truth, when Chen Pingan had earlier left the secret chamber of Ningfu in a daze, the old woman had already sensed something unusual. At that time, Chen Pingan was still disoriented, not fully aware that he had cultivated a life-bound flying sword, nor did he realize that this flying sword had manifested, deploying its life-bound powers to protect its master. Thus, wherever Chen Pingan walked, it created an almost natural small realm around him.

Bai Momo was as astonished to see the elderly figure as she would have been if her own son-in-law had finally cultivated a life-bound flying sword. She quickly bowed and clasped her hands in respect to the Elder Sword Immortal before silently departing. As she left, the old woman raised her hand repeatedly.

Chen Pingan took a deep breath, first clasping his fists in respect to the Elder Sword Immortal before bowing, yet remained silent.

Everything was conveyed without words.

Chen Qingdu walked slowly up to the Dragon-Slaying Cliff, with Chen Pingan closely following.

As he walked, Chen Qingdu spoke, "She once had great merit for the human race; this is an old story I remember well, one I have kept for ten thousand years. When you first arrived at the Sword Qi Great Wall, I had already noticed some clues. Although the three caverns no longer had her three strands of sword energy lingering around them, that aura was one I knew all too well. After all, my swordsmanship came from her previous master. However, aside from worrying that this might be a scheme of some hidden puppet master, I also have my selfishness. I, Chen Qingdu, owe her a favor; how I repay it and when, I decide for myself. So, I pretended not to see her little hints, neither rebuilding the Eternal Life Bridge for you nor assisting in cultivating your life-bound flying sword, all so that I can still have a reunion after ten thousand years. I owe her, not you, Chen Pingan. If she is unhappy, she can come find me at the Sword Qi Great Wall."

Chen Qingdu sat on a bench, facing south towards the Sword Qi Great Wall, and sighed, "How many ancient people are my old friends, even juniors? How many ancient deities and savage beasts have been my enemies, even the souls lost under my sword? There is a great desolation here that you wouldn't understand."

Chen Qingdu chuckled, "It's been many years since I've looked at the city walls from such a distance. I remember when it was just built, I stood over there on today's Tai Xiang Street, joking with Long Jun and Guan Zhao, saying that with this high wall, it could withstand for ten thousand years. And indeed, it has."

Turning to Chen Pingan, Chen Qingdu expressed his approval, "Today's fortunes are not something you begged for, nor something anyone bestowed upon you; it is something you fought for yourself."

Chen Pingan stood up and clasped his fists, saying, "I must still thank the Elder Sword Immortal for your teachings and guidance."

Chen Qingdu replied, "If we put it that way, it’s somewhat acceptable. However, looking at the process through the lens of a good outcome, there's kindness everywhere. Looking back at life with a bad ending, there's malice at every turn."

Chen Pingan laughed, "As a junior, I only speak of the facts, highlighting the good. I have no courage to drone on about grievances with the Elder Sword Immortal."

This was the truth. If the first time at the Sword Qi Great Wall had gone smoothly, with the Eternal Life Bridge rebuilt and him becoming a sword cultivator on the rise, there would have been far fewer surprises. He wouldn’t have needed to carry a long sword to Tongye Continent to seek the East Sea Observance, which possibly could have avoided the subsequent bloodshed in Old Dragon City, the ordeal of the Book Lake where he had to rely on heart cultivation due to insufficient realms, the dire situation set up by Jingguan City’s Gao Cheng and He Xiaoliang, and the exhausting, thankless battles against the heavenly tribulations. If all those changes had occurred, it would have been an entirely different landscape, and whether that life was better or worse, he would never have the chance to know.

As for the current predicament at the Sword Qi Great Wall, if he were to complain, Chen Pingan could argue with the Elder Sword Immortal for several days.

Chen Qingdu nodded, "You, kid, have some ties with your elders, after all."

Chen Pingan quietly asked, "When can I reopen that item of mine? When the war escalates, I will definitely accompany Ning Yao and the others to leave the city and fight."

He only stated half of his thoughts.

The other half being that without that item, I wouldn’t be able to gather scraps and earn my honest money. If I were to carry a large sack around, how could I avoid running into the dragons and such? Wouldn’t I have to speak some just words?

Chen Qingdu was puzzled, "For such trivial matters, why not ask Yan Ming instead of me?"

Initially, Chen Pingan was skeptical, always feeling that with Uncle Yan's style and having been chosen by the Elder Sword Immortal to help him smuggle through the Inverted Mountain to the Sword Respect Pavilion, how could he let such a large flaw occur with an item containing the sword immortal's painting? However, he quickly understood—indeed, it was a trivial issue—he could just borrow an item from the wealthy Uncle Yan.

Chen Qingdu didn't mind Chen Pingan's little calculations, estimating that this kid would borrow, but whether he would return it was hard to say.

However, the so-called ties with elders were quite accurate. Uncle Yan, who had immense expectations for his only son Yan Zhuo, would not hesitate to lend him an item, whether for public or private matters.

Although Uncle Yan’s swordsmanship was not high, he was excellent at generating wealth, so he would have a special fondness for Chen Pingan. This was quite different from Yue Qing's changed impression of this young outsider; Uncle Yan had regarded Chen Pingan highly from the very beginning.

While appearing indifferent to everything, Chen Qingdu was, in fact, keeping every junior sword cultivator in his heart.

Suddenly, Chen Qingdu said, "Your two life-bound flying swords are not merely an offense and defense. Unlike your peers Qi Shou and Gao Ye, their several flying swords have considerable killing power and are not to be underestimated. However, the further they progress, the less possibility there is of connecting multiple flying swords together compared to you."

One must know that Confucian sages preside over the academy, while the mountain gods and water deities reign over their mountains and rivers, capable of reaching a higher realm.

As for Chen Pingan's life-bound flying sword, which the elder praised as a "caged sparrow," whether it has such an elevated divine ability remains to be discovered and excavated by Chen Pingan himself.

Once one becomes a sword cultivator and possesses a life-bound flying sword, having passed the most difficult barrier of "creating something out of nothing," the path of cultivation thereafter would provide the confidence to discuss lofty ideals and enjoy freedom of body and mind.

Chen Qingdu stood up, smiling, "Finally, there are some decent means at your disposal."

On the verge of returning to the Sword Qi Great Wall, the elder turned to Chen Pingan and asked, "How was it, being washed by sword intent along with the flow of time, that feeling of having one's form disintegrate while the bones stand firm?"

Chen Pingan also rose, forcing a smile, "It was incomparably harder to endure than when I practiced punches back in my homeland; I absolutely don’t want to go through that again."

Chen Qingdu smiled, "What a coincidence."

Chen Pingan, beads of sweat forming on his forehead, shook his head with a serious expression, "Elder Sword Immortal, could we skip the coincidences?"

Chen Qingdu insisted, "It was indeed a coincidence."

Chen Pingan resignedly said, "As you say, senior."

Chen Qingdu chuckled, "This time, the process of form disintegration and body melting will take much longer."

Chen Pingan trembled, asking, "Now that I’m a sword cultivator, why must it be so?"

Chen Qingdu provided an answer that Chen Pingan would never have imagined: "The resentment of youth is not to be trifled with."

After the elder finished speaking, he vanished from sight.

The entire Ningfu's Dragon-Slaying Cliff and that small pavilion unexpectedly transformed into a small realm that even a sword immortal's strike would find hard to breach. Chen Pingan was suppressed within, sitting in the center of the pavilion.

From the top of the pavilion, sword light poured down like an exceedingly slow-moving strange waterfall, crashing down upon Chen Pingan's head. His golden-body martial physique felt as if it were a piece of porcelain, about to shatter but not quite, revealing countless cracks, especially where his head and face, the first to "bathe" in the waterfall of sword intent, bore the brunt. If Chen Pingan could still have his Yin spirit venture forth, he would find that his real body appeared even more ghastly than the face of the lady of the Flying Eagle Fortress from Tongye Continent. Not only was the skin damaged, but even his eye sockets began to slowly crack. The most torturous part was that this transformation spread gradually, akin to the growth of vegetation. This was in stark contrast to his earlier experience in Ningfu's secret chamber, where he had faced a rapid onslaught—two extremes.

And when the waterfall hit the ground, it did not break free from the Dragon-Slaying Cliff and the small pavilion's realm; instead, it resembled an ancient well collecting heavenly rain, with the water level gradually rising above Chen Pingan’s knees.

This was more than just a matter of placing oneself in the path of a white blade; it was akin to a grinding death where heaven and earth converged.

Washing the sword—only sword cultivators washed swords; who would wash their own physical body as if it were a sword being refined?

The old woman sensed the heavenly phenomena from afar and felt relieved, "I never expected my son-in-law has become a sword cultivator and is practicing his sword even more diligently."

Over at the Sword Qi Great Wall, the left and right asked, "How is it?"

Chen Qingdu smiled, "First, you must hold a long sword, aiming the tip directly at the beasts of the wild world. Then, with the life-bound flying sword, you can restrain Chen Qingdu. As your senior brother, what do you expect of your junior?"

The left and right maintained serious expressions, replying in unison, "It's the big senior brother and the little junior brother."

Chen Qingdu clicked his tongue, "I ask you to save some face for the Confucian lineage."

The left and right were in high spirits, and this time, they truly did not care, but couldn’t help furrowing their brows, asking, "Now that you have a life-bound flying sword, why not rush to the battlefield immediately?"

Chen Qingdu replied, "I asked him to come, but that brat has become a sword cultivator and is too proud to come."

The left and right laughed heartily, "Still, Elder Sword Immortal cares about face."

Suddenly, Chen Qingdu said, "A war is ultimately not just a fight; your little junior brother understands this better than you. However, there are some words I will tell you later."

This time, the demon clan's army attacking the city soon created an extraordinarily spectacular surprise.

On the battlefield, five towering mountains directly stood tall, lined up in succession, all being the highest peaks of the wild world. This was the Mountain-Relocation Divine Ability of the great demon Zhen Guang, and after this battle, this ascending realm great demon would be severely injured, essentially withdrawing from the subsequent siege warfare, taking time to recuperate within the General's tent. The cost of relocating the Five Peaks was certainly not limited to the loss of Zhen Guang’s cultivation.

For example, the mountain gods originally stationed at these five peaks were all high-level mountain deities of the wild world. Now, they had merged with the mountain altars and golden bodies into the luck of the Five Peaks.

If it weren’t for this, even if the great demons of the wild world could move the Five Peaks, they would not have been able to break through the sword qi torrents, and thus would never have reached this battlefield.

Though these five mountains seemed only to be halfway compared to the Sword Qi Great Wall, to all the sword cultivators at the Sword Qi Great Wall, it was a monumental problem.

Not only did the demon clan advance rapidly and stably on the battlefield, but also the five mountains that appeared out of nowhere each had a protective great formation shimmering with treasure light. Within the formations were the powerful cultivators from the wild world who had set up their formations long before. They had essentially given half their lives in exchange. For Zhen Guang to successfully throw the five great mountains here, it required not only his own cultivation but also the meticulous layout of the demon clan during the first unveiling battle, creating geographical changes on the battlefield. Coupled with the spells and treasures of the mountain cultivators, they had decisively severed the roots and water veins of the mountains, ultimately refining the five peaks and delivering them to the ascending realm great demon Zhen Guang, allowing for such a grand display.

Thus, the cost was enormous, yet once accomplished, it was time for the sword cultivators at the Sword Qi Great Wall to risk their lives and flying swords to pay the debt.

Additionally, the great demon who was once the ruler of the Yiluo River, the dragon-robed woman of imperial crown, appeared to have taken over for the previous skeletal great demon Bai Ying, now responsible for the latest stage of the siege.

She went by the alias Yang Zhi, and in the wild world, not everyone was unaware of her true name. However, those qualified to know this matter were all ancient beings who knew her well. Whether they could call out her true name mattered little; they would not genuinely fight to the death. She had transferred all the rivers and lakes under her jurisdiction, including the Yiluo River, to another great demon. But before relinquishing her assets, she naturally held back, capturing several great rivers' waters into her life-bound object.

At this moment, the five peaks stood tall, and she personally occupied one of the mountain tops. She didn't reveal her monstrous true form but appeared like a noblewoman casually wandering through the mountains. At the foot of one of the great mountains, she smiled and gently bent down, shaking out five green water pearls from her dragon-robed sleeves, saying with a smile, "Go, let the mountains remain still while the waters flow, and serve as a moat."

In the end, a turbulent river appeared at the foot of each of the five peaks, encircling them. The waters were fierce, brimming with murderous intent, and many lonely souls and wandering ghosts that had survived on the battlefield would soon be turned into vengeful spirits as they were drawn into the waters.

In fact, before the rivers and mountains were intertwined, many sword immortals, each with their own roles, decisively drew their swords almost simultaneously. Some split mountains, while others saved many life-bound flying swords of mid-level sword cultivators who couldn’t retreat in time.

Even though the sword immortals struck quickly, over a hundred life-bound flying swords of sword cultivators were directly suppressed and shattered by the five suddenly appearing mountains.

If it weren’t for a sword immortal not known for their great killing power using their life-bound flying sword to manifest a golden body, stubbornly shouldering the mountain, effectively stalling its rooting momentarily, the losses in the battlefield where mid-level sword cultivators had unleashed their swords would have been unimaginable.

This time, even Nalan Shao Wei did not hold back; she slashed out her slender, bright red flying sword, which instantly transformed into a long, fiery red dragon, wrapping around one of the great mountains. The mountain trembled under the impact, stones rolling down, and countless plants being crushed.

The dragon of Nalan Shao Wei’s flying sword clashed with the river of the peak great demon Yang Zhi, with the dragon raising enormous waves and crashing against the mountain.

Lu Zhi almost simultaneously drew her sword to cut the mountain, while Yue Qing, Yao Lianyun, and Li Tuimi also took their turns to strike.

Indeed, this ploy of the wild world was fraught with endless consequences.

Its impact on the subsequent battlefield dynamics was profound. One wrong move could give the enemy a foothold akin to five cities, and with the various methods of the other great demons, it would be easy for them to encompass the entire battlefield, turning it into a treacherous standoff between mountains and city walls.

Around the five peaks, celestial maidens adorned with colorful ribbons and holding pipa instruments appeared, standing at the height of ordinary women, yet numbering in the thousands, forming an additional protective great formation.

They each played the pipa, producing heavenly sounds that were both gentle and powerful, intertwined with the spiritual energy of the waters. The mist rose, ultimately transforming into strands of emerald silk that soared skyward, connecting with their flowing garments, as if draping the five peaks in a translucent green veil.

Li Tuimi directly challenged the central mountain, where the dragon-robed woman manifested a pitch-black dharma form, grasping a massive flying sword that Li Tuimi had intended to use to slay some demon cultivators on the mountain peak. However, after being personally blocked by the great demon Yang Zhi, Li Tuimi, the premier protector of the Yan family, not only didn’t worry about whether his sword would be seized and injure the sword immortal's foundation, but instead erupted in fierceness, summoning a second life-bound flying sword, "Silver Thread," and lifted it between the mountain and the city walls, launching a long silver sword light aimed straight at the dharma form’s brow. Li Tuimi himself rode the wind forward, holding his long sword in a straight line, like a long rainbow hanging in the air.

The dharma form was enormous, while the sword immortal's figure was minuscule, almost like an ant shaking a tree.

Li Tuimi's celestial companion, along with three direct disciples, had all died at the hands of the great demons of the Yiluo River.

So, a solitary figure was he.

At this moment, if not now, when?

The woman smiled seductively, "The courage of a great sword immortal is indeed considerable. Let me take away that courage."

At the five peaks, two large protective formations, and thousands of demon cultivators specializing in talismans, along with over a thousand pieces of magical artifacts, plus Yang Zhi personally overseeing one of them.

Even if the sword immortals worked together with all their might, how could they easily shake the foundations?

The left and right didn’t care; even if they were unfamiliar with that sword immortal, they felt that anyone who dared to say something so brazen should not die!

Knowing that the bloodthirsty Li Tuimi had already made up his mind to blow himself up along with his two swords and his entire being to destroy most of that central mountain, it was to win a chance for the sword cultivators behind him to shatter the mountains. If the five peaks were allowed to firmly root themselves in the battlefield, forming an increasingly stable foundation of roots and water veins, future wars would only become more challenging.

Having all five peaks intact was vastly different from just losing one while retaining the other four.

Li Tuimi simply advanced with his sword.

In a great battle, how could any of our sword immortals die? Would everyone just sit back and watch while those younger generations, like Yan Xiaopang, perished first? 

For ten thousand years, such a saying had never existed at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

The left swung his sword and cleaved the pitch-black dharma form in two.

But Li Tuimi, instead of retreating back to the city, burst forth in brilliant sword light and plunged into the summit of that central mountain.

"Everyone, I, Li Tuimi, shall go ahead."

Yang Zhi raised her brow, and her墨色龙袍 (black dragon robe) suddenly floated away from her body, covering the mountain like a cloth obscuring a bonsai, instantly enveloping the entire mountain to prevent that reckless sword immortal from completely destroying the mountain formation and its roots. This way, the relentless assaults of the opposing sword immortals would be hard to withstand, and the hidden plots lying deep would emerge prematurely. If the mountains gathered on the battlefield, and if the Sword Qi Great Wall did not exert enough pressure, then the enemy would naturally stabilize their foothold, as if pushing the battlefield hundreds of miles closer to the Sword Qi Great Wall. If the sword immortals did not relent and did not strike decisively, it would be even better, as it would become a situation where they mutually fed each other, each time sending in troops, each time falling short, and thus would consume each other. This was precisely the situation that the wild world desired to see because those who could provide reinforcements from the Sword Qi Great Wall were certainly at the Jade Pure realm level.

In the unveiling battle, the wild world intentionally struck lightly, but in this second round, they intended to inflict serious injuries on the Sword Qi Great Wall—directly killing off a batch of sword immortals!

But Li Tuimi's act of seeking death had infuriated the former mistress of the Yiluo River.

Yang Zhi and the other four peak great demons, sharing a telepathic link, instructed one another not to rush, especially the elder hidden in the central mountain, whom Yang Zhi firmly forbade from acting independently.

What surprised her even more was that the left and right, failing to save their comrades, made an unimaginable strike. Just as Li Tuimi resolutely self-destructed his golden core, primordial infant, all his souls, and both swords, he was being suppressed by Yang Zhi's dharma robe of celestial rank, not expected to even destroy half of the protective formation. The impact on the roots would be minimal, but the left directly wielded a sword, breaking through the black dragon robe enveloping the mountain and cleaving Li Tuimi!

Originally, Li Tuimi, whose sword light had been restrained by the black dragon robe, laughed silently and left this world completely.

After this strike, Li Tuimi died, and both of his life-bound flying swords exploded with a thunderous roar, resulting in a celestial sword cultivator leaving no trace of his soul, causing the entire mountaintop to shatter. Not only that, but over a hundred demon talisman cultivators, below the primordial infant level, directly linked to the protective formation, died en masse, which then caused the entire great mountain's roots, which had been slowly stabilizing, to violently quake.

After the left dealt out that sword that would undoubtedly invite endless controversy in the Haoran realm, he did not withdraw but instead surged forth with a torrent of sword qi, landing on the now significantly shorter central peak, driving his sword into the mountaintop.

How big could a mountain be? Could it truly withstand the sword qi of the left?

Great demon Yang Zhi was furious; she decisively sacrificed a celestial robe to stabilize the mountain’s luck. Moreover, she instructed one of her peers, also a great demon, who was her half companion, not to intervene. Killing the left would be too difficult; she would just entangle him herself while needing to slay a few more sword immortals like Li Tuimi from the other four mountains. Otherwise, wouldn’t this second-stage layout turn into a huge joke?

She revealed her true form, her massive body soaring high to the mountain summit. As for the collateral damage to her own talisman cultivators along the way, Yang Zhi didn’t care a whit.

Except for the central peak, which was in great turmoil, the other four peaks remained relatively stable—but only relatively speaking.

The Hidden Official, who had been toying with braids, watched this scene with bright eyes, feeling invigorated.

She turned to glance at Chen Qingdu.

The elder said, "Go play yourself."

The Hidden Official slightly bent her knees, and the city walls trembled violently. The little girl, as petite as she was, left the city.

She directly crashed through one of the mountains.

After landing, she brushed off the dust from her head and began to dart back and forth across the ground, repeatedly using her head to bore through the mountain's body.

Every time the little girl opened a mountain, she would be somewhat covered in dirt, yet she wandered joyously, looking quite happy.

The two friends from Aiai Continent, who seemed more like fishermen or woodcutters than sword immortals, Zhang Shao and Li Ding, exchanged smiles. 

If it were just the usual back-and-forth battles, that would be fine; they would take every moment they could, and killing more beasts would not weigh on their conscience. But since the enemy had just brought forth this water and mountain tactic, how could they allow a bunch of creatures lacking in literary knowledge to gain momentum and take the lead?

Absolutely not.

Thus, without needing words, the two sword immortals, almost simultaneously, took off from the Sword Qi Great Wall. Like two hastily falling meteors, they chose a mountain, one landing at the foot and the other halfway up.

In the world, fishermen enjoy boating, and Zhang Shao was no exception; yet this would be his last chance to enjoy the mountains and waters, and he did not need to be overly pretentious.

Sword immortal Zhang Shao stepped directly into the river of the Yiluo River's affiliation, smiling, "Zhang Shao, sword cultivator of Aiai Continent."

Meanwhile, Li Ding, who climbed the mountain behind Zhang Shao, smiled knowingly, "What a coincidence; I too am a sword cultivator from Aiai Continent."

The two sword immortals calmly faced death, directly destroying the entire mountain’s roots and water veins.

On the city walls, the Elder Sword Immortal squinted at a certain spot, then took a step forward.

The gray-robed elder at the northern gate smiled, "No need to rush; we are responsible for wrapping things up. As long as you don’t act, I certainly won’t. After all, Chen Qingdu's greatest ability is merely to watch as each of his juniors dies before his eyes."

The gray-robed elder looked towards the great demon Yang Zhi and instructed her.

Within each of the five peaks, the greatest trump cards no longer concealed themselves, whether they were ascending realm great demons or celestial sword cultivators, all emerging from their hidden locations. As for whether the mountains could continue to root themselves in the battlefield, the lives of the thousands of talisman-cultivating demon cultivators on the mountains, and how long the protective formation could withstand the sword immortals' strikes, had become irrelevant.

The four great demons flew towards the central peak to join forces with Yang Zhi, who revealed her true form.

Surrounding the left and right!

In the central peak's territory, a short elder hovering on his sword suddenly grew to a height of several dozen feet, his white brows and hair flying, shouldering a long staff, slowly rising into the sky. During this time, every time he opened his mouth to inhale, dozens of pipa girls were swallowed up like chewing beans.

Dong Sangeng laughed loudly, "That little brat..."

Chen Xi and Qi Tingji intended to follow Dong Sangeng away from the city walls.

The three old sword immortals each bore a monumental mark on the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Yet Chen Qingdu said, "Let the left and right forge swords with lives at stake; the Haoran realm is not a place for idle fighting; here, we have enough. Life that is too smooth and solitary does not lead to great swordsmanship."

Dong Sangeng was heading toward the battlefield, while the Hidden Official, still playing on the battlefield, along with the left and right, needed to confront Yang Zhi and the elder on their swords, alongside the other four great demons.

On the city walls, Yan Zhuo bit his lip, remaining silent.

Elsewhere, Cheng Quan and Qi Shou were wholly focused on the battlefield, not noticing Chen Pingan, who remained motionless, his face a mask of struggle.

Once Chen Pingan's Yin spirit was free to act, it was already too late.

On the battlefield, an unexpected occurrence larger than the sudden appearance of the mountains took place.

The Hidden Official shattered the sword intent, directly piercing through the left's abdomen.

Had the left not dodged at the last moment, he would have had his heart crushed.

Immediately retreating several miles, the left was caught by Dong Sangeng, who endured the full force of the elder’s strike, pulling the left away from the battlefield.

The entire Sword Qi Great Wall, aside from a few sword cultivators, was stunned, shocked beyond measure.

The Hidden Official spat out a mouthful of blood, turned her head to look at Chen Qingdu, and raised her middle finger, "The old never die ought to die; may you die!"

Chen Qingdu remained expressionless, merely glancing at the Hidden Official, his gaze then turning to Dong Sangeng and the left, muttering to himself, "Left, your little junior brother warned me earlier to be wary of that Hidden Official."

Aside from Dong Sangeng, even Chen Xi and Qi Tingji had to tread carefully, for Chen Xi harbored too much resentment, and Qi Tingji had too much ambition. Most importantly, both of these old sword immortals, who had achieved great feats, felt no guilt toward the Sword Qi Great Wall, yet bore profound hatred toward the entire Haoran realm.
