However, Chen Pingan had only recorded thirty-seven major incidents regarding these two old sword immortals and six key phrases, still unable to definitively predict whether they would turn against the wild world; it would ultimately be up to the Elder Sword Immortal.

On the ground, the Hidden Official waved her hand, summoning the sword cultivators Zhu An and Luo Shan, who had been attacking a nearby mountain, to stop their swords and join her, turning their backs to the Sword Qi Great Wall and heading towards the wild world.

On the Sword Qi Great Wall, Pang Yuanji swayed, ultimately collapsing on the city walls, tears streaming down the face of this young sword cultivator.

He couldn't understand why it had come to this.

Without that overwhelming presence, Chen Pingan finally moved freely, but he neither scolded Chen Qingdu for deliberately hiding the truth nor checked on his injured senior brother, the left. The world’s right and wrong, good and bad, ebb and flow—it was never simple. So, Chen Pingan merely sat in place, opening his folding fan to cover most of his face, revealing only his piercing eyes, firmly fixated on the southern battlefield, slowly saying, "Let the fight begin."

(End of Chapter)

 **Chapter 736: The New Hidden Official**

The battle was exceptionally brief and intense, its scale so small that the rapid casualties felt like a chance encounter between scouts from opposing armies.

The Wildlands did not immediately launch the next offensive. It was evident that many key military commanders had not anticipated this outcome, and with so many surprises, they had to adjust various strategic details within the established framework.

As a result, the battlefield yielded only three remaining mountains. The central peak, which had been thoroughly shattered by the skirmish between the Left and Right, was completely destroyed. The other peak was devastated by two foreign sword immortals from the White Snow Continent, who paid with their lives to destroy the mountain's foundation and waterways, and then it was brutally cleaved in two by Lu Zhi's sword light.

The remaining three mountains were already in disarray. One had previously been ravaged by the Renowned Officials’ faction, the Sword Immortals Luo Shan and Zhu An, which was likely the last achievement of these two traitorous sword immortals.

If they were to meet again in the future, it would be a matter of exchanging swords, asking questions, and sharing life and death with former comrades and fellow sword immortals.

Atop those three peaks, some lucky talisman practitioners from the demon race who had not perished could only await their demise. Even if they managed to escape far away, what would be the point? Their lives were already tied to the fate of the mountains. Some among them, with fierce tempers and ruthless decisiveness, called upon friends to coordinate efforts to reopen the mountain defense formation, fighting to the last breath in hopes of forcing the Sword Immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall to expend at least one more sword strike.

Sword Immortal Zhao Ge Yi found Cheng Quan and together they flew with their swords toward a mountain. Zhao Ge Yi aimed to protect Cheng Quan's formation and help him assimilate the mountain's energy for his own use.

“Damn it! I feel like a traitor just stepping out of the city!” Cheng Quan exclaimed, filled with grief and anger. “Those treacherous bastards, Zhu An and Luo Shan! Before today, I would have willingly traded my life for either of them! Zhao Ge Yi, tell me, will you stab me in the back too in the future? If you will, be straightforward about it. When we get to the mountaintop, I just hope you strike quickly and decisively, like a man, so I can die faster.”

Zhao Ge Yi retorted angrily, “How could Song Caiyun possibly like someone as useless as you?!”

Cheng Quan’s face fell.

The Sword Qi Great Wall had won this stage of the war, but no sword cultivator atop the wall felt any joy.

The Hidden Official had actually betrayed the Sword Qi Great Wall, leading the traitorous Luo Shan and Zhu An to throw themselves into the Wildlands. The Hidden Official had even severely injured the previously invincible Left in the earlier battle.

Except for those sword immortals with sufficiently clear hearts, almost all sword cultivators felt a shadow looming over their hearts, especially the younger ones.

Chen Ping’an, with his folding fan at his waist, rode a talisman vessel toward the thatched cottage.

Inside the small thatched cottage, which had once been the temporary dwelling of the Sword Immortal Wei Jin from the Storm and Snow Temple, the Left sat on the bed, his abdomen punctured by a fist, a gaping hole that sword energy struggled to mend.

Sword energy could not produce flesh and bone, as this was merely the second dangerous melee. The Left needed to use sword energy to counter the aftereffects of the Hidden Official's punch.

Otherwise, for a top-tier sword cultivator who refined their body through sword crafting, even severe injuries should not provoke such horror in the nearby Dong San Geng, who felt it was dire.

Dong San Geng guarded the doorway, his voice raised in anger. “Chen Qingdu, what the hell is going on?! Is the Hidden Official possessed or something?!”

From a distance, Chen Qingdu did not turn his head, calmly stating, “You’re not blind; what you see is the truth.”

Dong San Geng was livid, for this old sword immortal had always had a good impression of the Hidden Official, thinking of him as a rare kindred spirit. Moreover, the old sword immortal’s most cherished grandson, once seen as the next candidate for the Sword Immortal title, Dong Guanpu, had shared a strong bond with the Hidden Official in their youth.

Dong San Geng had already spotted the young man, who had just put away his talisman vessel, and was still fuming, loudly confronting Chen Qingdu. “Then why didn’t you just kill him?!”

Chen Qingdu sneered, “Dong Guanpu defected to the Wildlands. That scandal is known to the entire Sword Qi Great Wall. Do I need to know it? Did I kill him before things blew up?”

Chen Ping’an pretended he hadn’t heard anything.

Years ago, after the sword immortals gathered at the wall, the eldest sword immortal personally slew Dong Guanpu before Chen Ping’an's eyes. However, back then, he was still quite naive and did not truly understand the Sword Qi Great Wall.

What puzzled Chen Ping’an the most was when Ning Yao later remarked that the young Dong was a good person.

As a sword immortal, a member of the Dong family, betraying the Sword Qi Great Wall was undeniably true. But was he really a good person? 

How was one to reconcile this?

Perhaps for the eldest sword immortal, defending the Sword Qi Great Wall was simply about keeping it intact.

Dong San Geng suppressed his fury and told Chen Ping’an that his senior brother wouldn’t die, then directly left the scene.

Chen Ping’an did not enter the thatched cottage but gently closed the door behind him.

Having witnessed such a grand and harrowing war where both sword immortals and great demons fell, one could not help but feel their insignificance more deeply.

Having seen all the choices made by the eldest sword immortal, Chen Ping’an felt that if he could revisit the Heart-Questioning Session at Shujian Lake, even with the same cultivation level as back then, he could truly move as he desired.

He did not linger at the cottage but headed toward Ning Yao and the others.

Ning Yao glanced at Yan Zhuo and then shook her head at Chen Ping’an.

Chen Ping’an nodded, signaling he understood.

Yan Zhuo’s eyes were red, hands clenched on his knees.

The chief offering of the family, the sword immortal Li Tui Mi, had fallen.

This old man had once been the object of Yan Zhuo’s hatred in his youth; many painful words were spoken by Li Tui Mi, who looked down upon the young master of the Yan family, turning the once-cherubic Yan Zhuo into a laughingstock across the Sword Qi Great Wall. Otherwise, given the Yan family's standing and resources, if not for their own people initiating trouble, who would dare to mistreat the only heir of Yan Zhuo?

Even though Yan Zhuo had later transformed through countless battles to become a true sword cultivator and made life-and-death friends with Ning Yao and Chen Sanqiu, Li Tui Mi, as a family offering, had still refused to acknowledge him.

Yan Zhuo had begged Li Tui Mi several times to teach him swordsmanship, but the old man had only ever claimed to be an old bone, living a humble life, too afraid to instruct the heir of the Yan family, as that would mislead him.

Who would have thought that when Li Tui Mi finally agreed to teach, his face stern yet a hint of laughter in his eyes, that he would suddenly perish, becoming the first major sword immortal to die on the battlefield.

Chen Ping’an sat beside Yan Zhuo, offering no words of comfort, for here in the Sword Qi Great Wall, with Yan Zhuo beside him, there was no need.

Anyone could endure this.

As for the pain of losing a loved one, who would be unfamiliar with it? Besides the deceased Li Tui Mi, there were those still alive, such as Wu Chengpei, Tao Wen, Zhou Cheng, and others, all sharing the same fate.

Sword immortals were no exception, let alone those sword cultivators. As for the countless broken natal flying swords and those suffering immensely, who were not in the same boat?

The last words of the eldest sword immortal, fortunate only for Chen Ping’an to have heard them, carried too much weight and significance.

For instance, the Hidden Official, knowing Dong Guanpu was a traitor, had deliberately avoided punishing him.

Chen Qingdu would not say much more, dragging it out, letting that thoughtful young boy, Dong Guanpu, live a day longer, if only to allow him to live another day.

If it weren’t for your Dong San Geng’s insufficient swordsmanship and insufficient military contributions, failing to intimidate the great families of Tai Xiang Street and Xuan Hu Street, inciting their collective ire, and being unable to protect the traitorous grandson’s life through military achievements, you would have been able to keep Dong Guanpu alive. This led to a group of sword immortals demanding justice from the Sword Qi Great Wall. Otherwise, if the Hidden Official’s faction had chosen to ignore it, Chen Qingdu would have turned a blind eye, permitting the Dong family to detain the unworthy grandson, or at most, sending him to Old Deaf’s prison—nothing more.

Ning Yao sat next to Chen Ping’an. “Are you alright?”

Chen Ping’an quietly replied, “Very well.”

Ning Yao had many questions, but there were so many that she didn’t know how to start.

Chen Ping’an gently said, “You don’t need to worry about anything; leave the thinking to me.”

Together, they gazed toward the south.

Yan Zhuo suddenly asked, “Am I in the way for you two?”

Chen Ping’an opened his folding fan, fanning Ning Yao with a smile, “Everyone should be more aware of their surroundings.”

That young man, who was about to sit next to Ning Yao, paused midway, neither standing nor sitting, striking a peculiar pose.

Unexpectedly, Chen Sanqiu sat beside Yan Zhuo, Fan Dache sat next to Dong Huafu, and Die Zhong sat beside Chen Sanqiu.

In the end, everyone turned to gaze into the distance.

Silently waiting for the next battle.

Pang Yuanji remained silent for a long time.

Regarded as the next generation's appointed Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall, his heart was filled with despair and gloom.

Next to Pang Yuanji sat the young sword cultivator Gao Youqing, sitting dumbly, wanting to speak but hesitating, never daring to say a word.

Gao Ye Hou approached Pang Yuanji and sat beside him, saying just two words: “Bear it.”

Pang Yuanji's gaze was vacant.

Gao Ye Hou remained silent for a moment before saying, “If you really want to know the answer, don’t sink too deep into despair. Instead, strive to one day personally ask the Hidden Official, let her tell you the answer herself!”

Pang Yuanji mumbled, “You aren’t me, and I’m not you; that’s impossible.”

Gao Ye Hou scoffed, “Fine then, from today on, the Hidden Official’s faction may as well be extinguished.”

Unexpectedly, behind the two, a little girl had quietly arrived, her arms crossed over her chest, declaring, “I’m here to take care of the incense; that’s settled.”

Pang Yuanji forced a smile and turned to ask, “Lv Duan, why didn’t you leave the Sword Qi Great Wall back then? Sword Immortal Guo Jia and Chen Ping’an actually hoped you would go.”

Guo Zhu Jiu’s eyes sparkled as she shook her head. “No matter how much I respect and admire my father and master, that’s their opinion. As a sword cultivator, shouldn’t I have my own way of living and dying?”

Pang Yuanji could only smile bitterly.

He understood the reasoning, but what could he do?

Gao Ye Hou raised his thumb and laughed, “Lv Duan, well said!”

Guo Zhu Jiu looked at Gao Ye Hou with resignation. “What are you praising me for? You should commend my master for teaching well. That’s two praises in one; you’re not very insightful.”

Gao Ye Hou was momentarily speechless.

It seemed that only Ning Yao and Dong could gain the upper hand when dealing with the young Lv Duan.

Gao Youqing, unable to hold back, broke into laughter.

Guo Zhu Jiu cast a pitying glance at the little girl. “Crying and laughing, you’ve really lost your mind; turns out you’re just a little brat.”

Gao Youqing tugged at Gao Ye Hou’s sleeve. Gao Ye Hou laughed, “So now you’re looking for your brother?”

Guo Zhu Jiu shook her head, imitating her master’s gesture of hands tucked into sleeves, and walked away, muttering, “Little brat, a little girl who won’t grow up, throwing water that can’t be spilled; so troublesome.”

Gao Youqing’s face flushed bright red.

Gao Ye Hou felt a bit troubled himself, dealing with such a sister with her elbow turned outward.

Pang Yuanji’s smile was forced as he continued to look toward the south, farther south, as if still hoping to catch a glimpse of his master.

On the Sword Qi Great Wall, all the sword cultivators from the White Snow Continent who were familiar with the two sword immortals, Zhang Shao and Li Ding, were also filled with boundless sorrow.

The two sword immortals, known for their carefree lives in the White Snow Continent, had been recognized as peaceful and uncontentious, yet they had died on the battlefield in the Wildlands.

The White Snow Continent prioritized commerce, meaning it had many merchants. In truth, these sword cultivators, thirty-two in total, had varied levels of cultivation, yet they were considered oddities in their homeland.

Among them, the two with the highest cultivation levels were the generous Zhang Shao and Li Ding, both Yu Pu realm sword immortals.

The sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall regarded those few White Snow Continent sword cultivators without any strange glances, but deep inside, they felt discontent.

There was no need to elaborate on the Northern Ju Lu Continent; it was the realm with the most sword cultivators, unmatched by any other. The Southern Po Sa Continent was closest to the Hanging Mountain and the Sword Qi Great Wall, with hundreds of sword cultivators, thus there was no reason to compare. However, apart from these, the Fu Yao Continent, Liu Xia Continent, and Jin Jia Continent had far more sword cultivators than the White Snow Continent.

Only two remained with fewer sword cultivators than the White Snow Continent: the Bao Ping Continent, the smallest in the realm, but it had previously produced the sword immortal Wei Jin, a young sword immortal able to rival the local sword immortals in talent and great achievements, alongside Chen Ping’an, who was not even a sword cultivator but earned the respect of sword cultivators.

The last continent was the Tong Ye Continent, known for its dislike of interacting with other continents.

The Bao Ping Continent was plagued by internal strife, while the Tong Ye Continent was troubled by great demons.

Only the White Snow Continent remained peaceful, even likely to be the most stable place when the heavens above the realm collapsed, as it was the farthest from the Hanging Mountain, separated from the Southern Po Sa Continent by a vast territory filled with stars.

Yet, boats from the White Snow Continent heading to the Hanging Mountain were flourishing in business.

However, within the Sword Qi Great Wall, compatriots were seldom seen.

It made sense; the pursuit of the Dao was paramount, life was singular, and while the path of cultivation was magnificent and secure, why would one come here to die? Those who came could hardly blame those who did not.

Now that Zhang Shao and Li Ding, two sword immortals from their own continent, had died, it should have been an event that would embolden the younger generation of the White Snow Continent’s sword cultivators. 

Yet, there was not a hint of pride or relief; instead, it only deepened their gloom and dissatisfaction.

Somewhere atop the wall, a group of scholars in Confucian robes gathered.

Among them, Chen Chunan wore a grave expression.

He stood with his closest friends, Liu Xianyang and Qin Zhengxiu, and said worriedly, “If we defend, many will die—more and more. If we don’t defend, we’d be letting down the many who have already died, including the local sword immortal Li Tui Mi and the White Snow Continent’s Zhang Shao and Li Ding, who are so close. If I were that eldest sword immortal, my heart would have collapsed long ago.”

Liu Xianyang squatted down, chewing on a root he had picked up from who-knows-where, mumbling indistinctly, “Sword immortals and sword cultivators have long gotten used to the eldest sword immortal being stationed at the Sword Qi Great Wall. It’s been so long that it’s hard for anyone to truly imagine what this senior’s heart feels like.”

Qin Zhengxiu said solemnly, “Over the past ten thousand years, including this one, there have been a total of ninety-six great battles. We’ve never lost.”

Liu Xianyang added, “The battlefield is on the southern land and in the hearts of the people in the north. So while we’ve always won, we’ve continually lost as well.”

Chen Chunan suddenly spoke up, “Our Hao Ran realm cannot escape blame; it is a grievous mistake.”

This elder, who held the title of the most revered Confucian in the Hao Ran realm, spoke not in a whisper but directly.

Aside from Liu Xianyang, Chen Chunan, and other gentlemen of the Confucian school, the faces of those present changed slightly.

The Hidden Official, along with Luo Shan and Zhu An, swaggered into the general's tent.

An old man in gray stood outside the tent, smiling, “Don’t worry about us not having a fight. As long as you’re at the Ascension stage and didn’t contribute to this siege, you can choose anyone to fight. If you kill them, who dares to complain? Just keep killing.”

The Hidden Official nodded, reaching out to tug at a braid, shaking it lightly, and grinned, “Once we’re in the Hao Ran realm, give me half a continent's worth of Ascension stage cultivators, and I’ll kill them all. Those turtles with their shells full of meat will be thoroughly smashed!”

The gray-robed elder did not refuse; why would he refuse? This little girl before him was undeniably the best seed of the Dao in the Wildlands. The alignment of the Dao was unparalleled. Being beside Chen Qingdu was a constant torment for her; the Sword Qi Great Wall was never a place for her cultivation but a prison that constrained her true self. As a sword cultivator born and raised in the Sword Qi Great Wall, the Hidden Official certainly possessed a natal flying sword. Yet, she had never unleashed it in battle; she would only wield a sword from the sword shop, break it, and switch to fighting with her fists.

The gray-robed elder seldom felt regret, but one of the few regrets was that this Hidden Official, who had grown up in the Sword Qi Great Wall, hadn’t been born in the Wildlands and hadn’t gone to Mount Tuo Yue for cultivation early on. Otherwise, all fourteen seats in that ancient well would have shifted positions.

This elder from the Wildlands currently had only one person following him, a big-bearded man who carried a sword and a knife.

Luo Shan looked at the famous sword immortal in the Wildlands and asked, “Why didn’t you draw your sword or attack, letting Dong San Geng save the Left?”

The big-bearded man replied indifferently, “Since you’re a sword immortal and a lady, I’ll waste a word on you. Who I kill or spare doesn’t require me to explain to outsiders.”

Luo Shan was about to speak when he was stopped by Zhu An, who held his wrist.

The gray-robed elder laughed, “There’s no need to be so formal. According to the rules set by Mount Tuo Yue, you are esteemed guests of the Wildlands, and that will hold for a thousand years without a hint of doubt. If Liu Cha draws his sword against you, it will count as questioning the Dao of Mount Tuo Yue, right?”

At this moment, the elder looked at the big-bearded man.

Liu Cha remained silent.

Then the gray-robed elder casually said something, addressing not only the man named Liu Cha but also Luo Shan and Zhu An, as well as many great demons in the general's tent, “Our Wildlands is indeed an unrefined barbaric land; it is neither the Sword Qi Great Wall nor the Hao Ran realm. My rules are few but effective; those who defy them shall all die.”

The Hidden Official said seriously, “By the way, that foolish disciple of mine, Pang Yuanji, even if he goes out looking for death, don’t kill him. I’m still hoping he’ll ask me for a sword once again.”

The gray-robed elder chuckled helplessly, “Such trivial matters need not be mentioned. Just have Luo Shan and Zhu An each go through the Jiazi tent and the Wu Wu tent, and they should get the hang of things.”

The Hidden Official asked, “What about me?”

The gray-robed elder replied, “In the place that Chen Qingdu calls a rat nest, beneath the well, there are still some damned great demons that were lucky enough to survive; if you’re feeling bored, go kill them all. It might help you break through earlier.”

The Hidden Official blinked, “Are you afraid I’ll team up with Chen Qingdu and destroy your behind?”

By going to that rat nest and slaying those surviving Ascension stage great demons, she could steadily raise her cultivation, and in doing so, establish a connection with the entire Wildlands. 

She wanted to break through the Ascension stage bottleneck and become an immortal being on par with that old blind man; this was the price she needed to pay. The world is a furnace? Cultivation is a thieving act? Even the Ascension stage cannot escape this kind of shackle; to truly break through this barrier, one must achieve great feats, using their own small world to refine a part of the greater world! If all is refined, one becomes a sage of Confucianism or the Buddha and Dao patriarchs!

The gray-robed elder laughed heartily, “Just say whether you’re going or not.”

The Hidden Official beamed, rising into the air like a rainbow, speeding toward the rat nest.

At the Sword Qi Great Wall, what could she refine? The Sword Qi Great Wall? The Sword Qi Great Wall is Chen Qingdu; Chen Qingdu is the Sword Qi Great Wall!

But the Wildlands was different, for that gray-robed elder had not truly refined the entire world either, so she had her chance, and perhaps in the future, she could even wrestle with this ancient ancestor of the demon race.

Liu Cha frowned and asked, “Must we really clear the path for her like this?”

“One sword path, one knowledge, two great benefits—enough for you and Zhou Mi to fill your bellies. Good fortune can’t just be hoarded by you two,” the gray-robed elder chuckled, “If Chen Qingdu dies again, when I reach the Hao Ran realm, the Li Sheng should emerge from his retreat.”

“I want to see if it’s true that in times of chaos, a hero will rise to turn the tide in the Hao Ran realm.”

Liu Cha asked, “And Bai Ze?”

The gray-robed elder scoffed, “Similar to the old blind man; completely disappointed and utterly unhelpful.”

Liu Cha suddenly said, “In darkness lies light.”

The gray-robed elder laughed and asked, “Have you ever thought about which realm this phrase applies to best? Purely speaking, which realm has the purest thoughts?”

The gray-robed elder extended both hands, “In the Hao Ran realm, the hearts of the people are declining. But we are on the rise. This is the most unstoppable trend of all.”

The elder clenched his fists softly, whispering, “When we reach the Hao Ran realm, it will be your turn to draw your sword.”

Liu Cha nodded, “Then let it be so.”

The gray-robed elder suddenly patted the big-bearded man on the shoulder. “Once you get there and make the other side feel the pain, you’ll have the opportunity to see that Ah Liang again. At that time, we can compare skills, and I allow you to use a piece of land from the Hao Ran realm as a wager for your duel.”

Ah Liang had traversed many places in the Wildlands, killing countless demons, yet he had also genuinely become a friend to a sword hero, and that was this Liu Cha.

After Ah Liang returned to the Sword Qi Great Wall, he once joked with a group of children that Liu Cha had not disappointed anyone.

He was robust, rugged in appearance, heavy on righteousness, unrestrained, and could recite poetry.

Of course, after saying these trivial pleasantries, Ah Liang quickly returned to his nature, spat in his palm, slicked back his hair, and, with those astonished children, “leaked secrets,” before getting to the main point.

“That fellow is incredible, yet he still gets captivated by my charm. Without a second thought, he offered me his sword as a gift. I refused, and he insisted on using his knife as a pen, which is a shame, considering I’m a proper scholar. Liu Cha, isn’t this self-humiliation? If you don’t see me nodding in agreement, that guy wouldn’t stop writing—water from ancient times flowing into my palms, with fierce energy stretching a thousand miles, wearing down the ancient blade, and don’t take small grievances lightly... What? You haven’t heard a single word? Doesn’t matter; it’s average writing anyway. If you can’t remember, then forget it. But if any of you meet that Liu Cha on the battlefield later, don’t be afraid. If you can’t win, just shout that you’re a friend of Ah Liang.”

However, that self-proclaimed scholar Ah Liang, a gambler and drunkard, had spent over a hundred years at the Sword Qi Great Wall, never donning a scholar’s robe or hanging a jade pendant, never truly resembling a scholar.

When he left, he even did so without his sword, only with a knife and a conical hat.

No one knew that when Chen Qingdu bid him farewell, he said solemnly, “Once you leave, don’t come back. An outsider has no business staying at the Sword Qi Great Wall for so long. Even if you don’t leave, I must drive you out.”

The man only grinned while massaging the eldest sword immortal’s shoulder, jokingly saying, “If there’s good wine, save some for me. Whether I drink depends on my mood, but saving it is a matter of brotherhood.”

Yet in the end, before leaving the area near the thatched cottage, he turned his back to the elder and said, “If the Sword Qi Great Wall turns its sword point against me, then I won’t return. No matter how good the wine, who would I drink it with?”

After the battle against the skeletal great demon Bai Ying and the former master of the Fallen River, the role of commanding the demon army shifted to a great demon with countless palaces and pavilions, known by the name Huang Luan.

Huang Luan sat alone on the railing, as if in a celestial city filled with ethereal energy and the calls of cranes.

Within the city, there were the twenty seasonal climates, some elegant residences filled with the sounds of autumn cicadas, while others had newly sprouted willow leaves like delicate brows; the air above the Taoist temple was filled with “growing jade,” with snow piled on the ground. There were many enchanting talisman beauties, either applying yellow flowers in front of mirrors or fanning away fireflies.

In the residence where Huang Luan sat, there flowed a stream known as Ruoye Creek, which Huang Luan cherished most deeply. The water was crystal clear, inhabited by a talisman-formed old fisherman with white hair, and a beautiful girl washing silk, doing the same thing year after year.

Beneath this cloud city lay the demon army, now fully assembled and steadily advancing, composed of cultivators with considerable cultivation levels—over fifty thousand troops, all at least in the Cave Dwelling realm, equipped with spirit tools and magical treasures.

Thus, there was no need to breach the three sword formations of the Sword Qi Great Wall, nor to swarm the siege.

From the Sword Qi Great Wall, a torrent of flying swords cascaded southward.

This time, the Wildlands would also unleash a river of comparable might, formed from countless spirit tools and magical treasures, with radiant brilliance soaring to the heavens, advancing toward the northern city wall.

You have your Sword Qi Great River, and I have my treasure river.

It would be a direct collision of rivers.

Since they had already decided to exhaust half the strength of their realm to attack this lonely Sword Qi Great Wall, how could they not have some decent display?

Using spirit tools and magical treasures in exchange for natal flying swords, they would see who felt the pinch more.

There were no plots or schemes, no clever layouts, just a mutual consumption of their resources.

If the earlier Huang Luan had been slightly more capable, not so utterly useless, able to hold the five mountain peaks firmly as a base, the damage to the Sword Qi Great Wall would have been even greater.

However, who would have thought that Li Tui Mi and the Left's strikes would disrupt the entire arrangement? Not only did they fail to kill more Ascension stage sword immortals, but they also almost lost everything in return. This also significantly affected Huang Luan’s siege, as otherwise, if the battlefield had been a bit closer to the city walls, the enemy would have suffered casualties much faster, and the Sword Qi Great Wall’s natal flying swords would have suffered losses as well.

Five Mountain Lords of the Ascension stage and thousands of talisman practitioners sacrificed their lives to refine the mountains, then had the heavy light transported to the battlefield. The accounts in the military tent were meticulously recorded.

If not for the Hidden Official’s defection, it would have created a huge problem; after all, the current siege was no longer as crude as before; they began to calculate carefully. Those military tents were not mere decorations; the cultivators within, even if their cultivation levels were not high and included many young children, were viewed seriously by the great ancestors and Mount Tuo Yue. Any military order that left the military tent had to be weighed by someone like Huang Luan, as well as the existing powers like Yang Zhi and Bai Ying.

Huang Luan raised his hand high and lightly waved it forward.

The demon army unleashed their treasures.

In the night, it seemed as if a brilliant galaxy suddenly hung in the sky.

Even a long-standing ancient existence like the great demon Huang Luan had to admit that this scene was spectacular and refreshing, though he wondered if he would have the opportunity to see such a sight again in the future. Once he reached the Hao Ran realm, based on previous calculations, it seemed unlikely he would have such a chance.

Huang Luan exclaimed, opening the barriers with a smile, “A rare guest, indeed!”

It was Yang Zhi, who had suffered significant losses to his celestial armor and law robes. Despite being broken and battered in battle, he had gathered most of the fragments to present to this nostalgic lady. However, if he truly wanted to repair it, it would be troublesome and not worth it; instead, it would be better to go to the Hao Ran realm and seize a few more items.

Today, dressed in simple clothes, the woman known as Yang Zhi sat beside the railing, her expression gloomy.

Huang Luan laughed, “What’s the matter? Are you trying to steal my credit?”

Yang Zhi replied, “I’m just helping you earn some credit. The great ancestor hasn’t said anything serious, but it’s clear he’s not too happy. After this battle, I’ll have to return to the Wildlands to personally hunt down those sword immortals who are wandering about.”

Huang Luan glanced toward the Sword Qi Great Wall, feeling regret. To be honest, even he had been kept in the dark about the Hidden Official’s betrayal. He had not anticipated such a change in events.

Yang Zhi asked, “What about the northern city? What is the timing for our pieces to strike?”

Huang Luan laughed, “How would I know such things?”

The army beneath them was not stationary; they were continuously advancing, casting various chaotic natal items from afar.

The torrent of sword energy clashed with the treasure river, a dazzling spectacle, like ancient deities forging swords, with countless sparks erupting, splashing everywhere like falling fire rain, illuminating both the Sword Qi Great Wall and Huang Luan’s celestial city, making them shine brilliantly.

In addition to this, there were the ants rushing madly on both flanks of the army, not just for show but genuinely sacrificing their lives to fill the battlefield. This was the “helping hands” Yang Zhi had mentioned, for these ants were the vassal forces and main troops of Yang Zhi. A peak great demon responsible for minor achievements in exchange for major errors would not merely be sitting beside Huang Luan enjoying the scenery, nor would he just take a few swings at the torrent of sword energy; many of these ants would die, directly thinning out some of the old powers they had worked hard to build up.

The Wildlands had one of the best aspects.

Under the fist, they had to accept fate obediently.

If they were unwilling to die, they would die first.

Moreover, it was not solely about dying; many military records would meticulously document every battlefield’s losses and achievements. Dying wasn’t too much of a loss, and if they survived, they would reap rewards many times over. The vastness of the Hao Ran realm meant that once they passed the Sword Qi Great Wall, they would have ample opportunities to make money. Countless heavenly materials and earthly treasures awaited the Wildlands to seize.

Huang Luan suddenly smiled playfully, “When did the Sword Qi Great Wall’s sword immortals become so orderly when drawing swords?”

This handsome man, full of the aura of an immortal, lightly tapped the railing, lamenting, “It’s over! With this, the enemy’s losses are bound to fall below the military tent’s expectations. Yang Zhi, is your bad luck so heavy that it drags me down? Look, those Yuesheng, Mi Hu, and the others, who were said to have poor relationships, all seem to be very meticulous about their formations now. Those rebellious sword immortals are engaging in small-scale fights, seamlessly coordinating with one another. But this scene tonight allows nearly all sword immortals to maximize their natal divine abilities. Isn’t that both surprising and troubling for you and me?”

Yang Zhi’s face darkened as he coldly laughed, “Knowing they are doomed, they resist stubbornly.”

After observing for a moment, Huang Luan sighed, “To gather the battle lines and have the sword cultivators retreat three li? Is this still the Sword Qi Great Wall I’ve heard of?”

Yang Zhi puzzled, “If it’s troublesome, then why are you still watching?”

Huang Luan smiled, “Let those young folks in the military tent practice a bit more. It’s all a show for the back row anyway. Besides, I don’t think this battlefield will suffer too badly. In the future, if we want to stalemate with the Hao Ran realm, we can’t rely solely on a few of us.”

Yang Zhi turned to look toward a distant place where a larger battle formation was yet to reach the battlefield.

They were all local sword cultivators of the Wildlands!

No matter how precious the lives of sword cultivators were, they couldn’t just be kept as decorations.

Those who could question the Sword Qi Great Wall and use it as a whetstone to sharpen their swords, while surviving, were the true sword cultivators.

At the Sword Qi Great Wall, a rather bizarre small hill had been hastily assembled, and over ten people, about half of whom were outsiders, gathered there.

Thus, the latest sword cultivators from the Hidden Official’s faction converged here, marking the first time in history that the Hidden Official’s faction had recruited foreign sword cultivators.

As for the roles of supervising officer and record keeper, they were still entrusted to the previous sword cultivators of the Hidden Official’s faction and the Confucian disciples, but the identities of the former Hidden Official’s faction members had already been lost.

After gathering these people, Lu Zhi quickly left, leaving behind two scrolls sent by the Taoist saints.

The two large scrolls were unfurled by Lu Zhi along the promenade. One scroll depicted the scene of the sword energy torrent clashing with the treasure river. The other, further south of the battlefield, illustrated the layout of the demon army's formation in the Wildlands, albeit a bit unclear; yet, the more northward it went, the clearer the details appeared, as if there was a watershed split by time and opportunity.

Lu Zhi only said that everyone temporarily need not bear the responsibility of drawing swords to kill enemies, as they were all regarded as part of the Hidden Official’s faction. Beyond that, this remarkable female sword immortal with exceptional combat capabilities did not utter another word.

Most sword cultivators exchanged glances, unsure of what to do.

Firstly, many did not know each other, and secondly, they were completely lost about what was expected of them.

Mi Yu felt the most awkward, as he was the only one at the Ascension stage.

They couldn’t just stare blankly at each other, so the highest-ranked Mi Yu said, “Let’s introduce ourselves first. I’m Mi Yu, a Yu Pu realm sword cultivator.”

A handsome young man in white smiled and said, “Lin Junbi, from the Central Continent, just entered the Dragon Gate realm.”

One after another, people began to introduce themselves.

“Deng Liang from the White Snow Continent, Yuanying realm.”

“Song Gaoyuan from Fu Yao Continent, Jindan realm.”

“Cao Jun from Liu Xia Continent, Dragon Gate realm.”

“Xuan Can from Jin Jia Continent, Jindan realm.”

In addition, from the Sword Qi Great Wall, there were Pang Yuanji, Dong Buduo, Situ Weiran, Gu Jianlong, Wang Xinshui, Guo Zhu Jiu, and Chen Ping’an.

The happiest was Guo Zhu Jiu, because her master was also present.

She squatted beside her master, both big and small keeping their sleeves tucked, clearly showing they were family.

The most anxious was, of course, Gu Jianlong.

After her master introduced himself, Guo Zhu Jiu began to clap vigorously.

“Chen Ping’an, lower fifth realm.”

Chen Ping’an turned to smile at his disciple, “Steady.”

Guo Zhu Jiu nodded vigorously.

Lin Junbi said, “Even if this group of demon beasts retreats, there will definitely be another group of sword cultivators coming to question us. This is probably why we’ve gathered here—to think of as many possibilities about the enemy as we can, and to strategize our responses. The situation is extremely urgent; aside from Sword Immortal Mi, our cultivation levels are not high, so our responsibility is actually to plug gaps. We can’t help much, but if we brainstorm together, we should be able to contribute a little.”

While Lin Junbi spoke, Chen Ping’an sat cross-legged on the edge of the scroll, holding his folding fan, lightly tapping his palm, and gazing intently at the battlefield depicted on the scroll.

Lin Junbi looked toward Mi Yu, who nodded in agreement, though he felt a bit awkward all over.

Lin Junbi then turned his attention to the second-in-command.

Chen Ping’an did not lift his head, smiling, “Let those capable take on more work; Junbi can issue commands.”

Lin Junbi felt a bit out of place. 

However, he did not hesitate; recognizing the priorities, Lin Junbi, at this moment, felt as though standing at the side of a chessboard, competing against the entire Wildlands. Helping the Sword Qi Great Wall gain even a slight advantage was also a victory for himself and the Shao Yuan Dynasty.

Thus, without hesitation, after a moment of contemplation, Lin Junbi began to assign tasks to everyone.

He tasked Pang Yuanji and Dong Buduo with counting and categorizing all the natal flying swords and divine abilities of their own sword immortals, while Situ Weiran and Deng Liang would record the semi-immortal weapons and key magical treasures of the enemy cultivators. Xuan Can and Song Gaoyuan were responsible for keeping track of the consumption of both sides' flying swords and magical treasures, while Cao Jun and Wang Xinshui would monitor the changes in the demon cultivators’ formations, and if they had the bandwidth, to look for any hidden high-level enemies...

Chen Ping’an looked toward Gu Jianlong and greeted, “Gu, what a coincidence; where in life do we not meet again?”

Gu Jianlong hurried over to Chen Ping’an, squatting down, full of righteousness, “What are you joking about? How could I let the second-in-command call me ‘Gu brother’? Just call me Xiao Gu!”

On this side of the promenade of the wall, a series of low tables finally appeared, with everyone sitting cross-legged. Mi Hu needed to compile the documents he had been recording and then hand them over to Guo Zhu Jiu for distribution, so everyone could read and share information.

As for some crucial intelligence, given how close they were, they could simply speak directly.

Only Chen Ping’an had no substantial task.

The reason was simple: after Lu Zhi sent people to bring tables and writing materials, she stated one line.

“From this moment on, Chen Ping’an is the new Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall.”

Mi Hu felt rather helpless.

Pang Yuanji felt relieved. As long as it wasn’t himself succeeding the Hidden Official, anyone else would be fine, and this second-in-command was the best of all.

Lin Junbi’s expression was complex, fleeting. He increasingly suspected that the current transformations in the sword immortals’ formations were indeed due to this man’s suggestions.

Gu Jianlong, on the other hand, was smiling despite himself.

Guo Zhu Jiu applauded alone, her applause echoing like thunder.

The youngest and lowest-ranked Hidden Official in the history of the Sword Qi Great Wall stood up, took the ancient jade tablet symbolizing the Hidden Official's identity, shook his sleeves, and sat back down, hanging the jade tablet at his waist, alongside the Sword Cultivation Gourd.

On the desk, aside from the writing materials, there were stacks of blank ledgers waiting to be filled, as well as a folded jade bamboo fan resting there.

Chen Ping’an interlocked his fingers, gazing at the familiar arrangement on the table, smiling faintly. It felt great, as if he were already seated in his small world without even unleashing his natal flying sword.

What new Hidden Official? 

It was merely a transition from a harmless burden to a more adept accountant.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 737: Settling Accounts with the Entire World (1)

In the wild and untamed world, it was still unclear that atop the Sword Qi Great Wall, they were missing one of the most powerful Hidden Officials in history, while simultaneously welcoming a new Hidden Official with the lowest cultivation level ever recorded.

Even if they were aware of this, it would likely be treated as a grand joke.

In fact, even among those at the Sword Qi Great Wall, there weren’t many who took it seriously. Especially the Sword Immortals, who merely regarded it as another “whatever” move from the big boss Sword Immortal.

With the new official taking office, Chen Ping’an immediately set about his tasks, accomplishing three things in total.

The Hidden Official lineage owned two private residences outside the city—one for summer retreats and one for winter. All the secret files accumulated over a century were moved to the corridor, stacked high behind Chen Ping’an, forming a mountain of documents.

The previous Hidden Official had neither taken the jade tablet inscribed with the ancient characters for “Hidden Official” nor destroyed the archives that held the lineage's legacy spanning thousands of years.

Aside from the “mountain” behind Chen Ping’an, he also had a treasured artifact moved over—a sword room.

Two flying swords were specially forged by the sword workshop for the Hidden Official lineage’s sword cultivators. At Chen Ping’an’s request, the swordsmiths engraved each person’s name on them.

Chen Ping’an, Mi Yu, Pang Yuanji, Dong Buduo, Gu Jianlong, Wang Xinshui, Guo Zhujiao, Lin Junbi, Deng Liang, Song Gaoyuan, Cao Jun, and Xuan Can.

These were all the sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

However, the two flying swords belonging to Chen Ping’an were inscribed with the characters for “Hidden Official” instead of his name.

The third thing he did was to speak plainly to his “subordinate” sword cultivators, delivering a straightforward message, “Everyone, including myself, we are a total of twelve sword cultivators present here. We’re all quite intelligent and should understand something—our common point is that our cultivation levels are not high, and our sword techniques are negligible in the current offense and defense battles. However, our minds are functioning well. When we encounter issues, we’re willing to think a bit deeper. It has become second nature for us. While the average sword cultivator might think something through once, we may have already considered it several times. This is what we call practice makes perfect. Granting the title of Hidden Official to each of you is the utmost recognition, but this is not a guaranteed position. Every suggestion we make, especially those that ultimately affect the strategies of the sword formations, will involve the lives of countless sword cultivators—potentially thousands or even the lives of many Sword Immortals. My only requirement is that everyone must put in their utmost effort. If I find anyone lagging at any stage, whose mind seems sharp but is actually lacking, I will directly expel them from the Hidden Official lineage. No matter how valuable your face may be, it cannot compare to the lives of sword cultivators or their life-bound flying swords.”

“So, this is definitely not a light matter. Please prepare yourselves mentally; we need to be responsible for every fallen warrior. The greater challenge lies with those sword cultivators whose lives are worse than death, or those who have lost family and friends in battle. They might harbor resentment towards the twelve of us—towards us sword cultivators who only seem to talk. It’s only natural for them to hate us, and we cannot change that. However, we must not lose hope; not even a little. If anyone bears grudges and intentionally sabotages us, once I discover it, I will have Sword Immortal Mi Yu deliver a sword strike to kill them. I will not listen to any excuses. The moment I suspect someone, that person will die. So, I have one final question: who wants to withdraw from the Hidden Official lineage? Now is the time to back out. Otherwise, instead of scheming against me, Chen Ping’an, and competing in cunning, it’s better to go out there and kill demons, earning some merit—it’s definitely better than wasting time here.”

The other eleven sword cultivators were silent, their expressions resolute.

Chen Ping’an nodded, “Good. Even Lin Junbi, this promising young sword cultivator, hasn’t hesitated to stake his life and future here. I believe we can trust in our unity.”

Lin Junbi suddenly felt a prick of anxiety.

Was Chen Ping’an going to take this opportunity to settle personal scores?

Chen Ping’an narrowed his eyes, surveying the faces of the sword cultivators, and slowly continued, “We are no longer here to cultivate or forge swords; we are to represent the Sword Qi Great Wall and conduct the largest transaction with the beasts of the wild world beneath Heaven. We need to make a deal that will save the lives of as many of our sword cultivators as possible, while costing the enemy as many lives as possible! Everyone, such an opportunity will never come again in our lives. No matter how rich your fortune may be in the future, how high you climb the path to the great Dao, or how you transcend to become an immortal, or reincarnate in the next life, you will never encounter such an opportunity again. Even if you become the leader of a sect in the righteous world, commanding countless sword cultivators, how many Sword Immortals will willingly risk their lives at your command?! You must cherish this moment, for this is a feat that only the twelve of us can accomplish in this world, both past and future!”

Guo Zhujiao, sitting behind the desk, had a resolute expression, suddenly clasping his fists but saying nothing.

Dong Buduo followed suit, equally spirited, raising his fists high.

All the others, including Lin Junbi, Gu Jianlong, Wang Xinshui, and even Sword Immortal Mi Yu, clasped their fists one by one.

Especially the younger sword cultivators from distant lands were even more invigorated. 

Those who dared to come to the Sword Qi Great Wall to practice their swordplay, especially those who refused to leave after the great battle, had pure and lofty ambitions!

Chen Ping’an said, “Don’t rush to issue orders to the Sword Qi Great Wall. Let’s first familiarize ourselves with the battlefield. Follow Lin Junbi’s established plan and carry out your duties. In half an hour, I will make another decision.”

To Chen Ping’an, Lin Junbi’s plan was too crude, but it was the product of his quick thinking and could not be overly criticized. However, after half an hour, or rather, from then on, the Sword Qi Great Wall would respond in this way to the strategic cooperation against the wild world’s sixty military camps, and Chen Ping’an did not feel that his Hidden Official lineage had any chance of winning.

Chen Ping’an began to flip through the old secret documents of the Hidden Official lineage, reading quickly. There were more than ten blank books beside him; when he found key points, he would jot down notes. At the same time, he occasionally glanced at the battlefield scroll and observed the subtle changes in the expressions of the eleven people.

The elegant handwriting belonged to the Bamboo Hut Sword Immortal.

The sharp strokes were by the female Sword Immortal, Luo Shan.

What a meeting of minds through words.

The content was clear and concise, without any faults to be found.

Even though three Sword Immortals had defected from the Sword Qi Great Wall, regarding this archival record, it could still be said that they had acted diligently.

Exactly half an hour later, Chen Ping’an, holding a closed folding fan, did not open it but lightly raised it before giving the table a firm knock, saying, “Continue to keep an eye on the battlefield; listen to my words without distraction. From now on, everyone must focus on three things: the first is your primary duties; everyone must keep a firm watch on the scroll. The second is that everyone must start taking notes for the convenience of others. When someone needs it, they can directly request it from others as a reference. The third matter is transmitting messages with flying swords at certain moments.”

Chen Ping’an continued, “Let’s start with the third matter. The flying swords from the Hidden Official lineage’s sword workshop are incredibly fast. Aside from major strategies, which I will personally communicate to all sword cultivators via flying swords, for other minor adjustments to the sword formations, you each have your tasks. Mi Yu, Dong Buduo, and Gu Jianlong will be responsible for transmitting messages to all local sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall, dividing the Great Wall into three major territories: left, center, and right. Guo Zhujiao and Wang Xinshui will handle all notifications to the upper five realms’ Sword Immortals.”

Upon hearing this, Mi Yu frowned. This seemed unreasonable; logically, he should be the one contacting the other Sword Immortals.

Chen Ping’an explained, “Sword Immortal Mi Yu, if a Sword Immortal talks to another Sword Immortal, the disparity in cultivation levels creates a mental threshold. It’s not pure, and it can lead to complications. Opportunities on the battlefield are fleeting; hesitation can cause everything to be lost. Do you understand?”

Mi Yu nodded.

In fact, this Hidden Official was being quite polite; there were even more underlying reasons he didn’t mention, such as Mi Yu’s poor reputation among the other Sword Immortals at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

In contrast, the lower-cultivation Guo Zhujiao and Wang Xinshui, as flying sword messengers, would be much more straightforward and businesslike. If Mi Yu, known for his flashy reputation, were to issue commands, many Sword Immortals would simply not take him seriously.

Chen Ping’an continued, “If you have such doubts in the future, feel free to ask me directly. If you can persuade me to change my mind, that would be best. Additionally, Pang Yuanji will be responsible for contacting the old Hidden Official lineage’s overseers and military merit recorders from the Confucian School. Since their numbers are few, Pang Yuanji will also be in charge of a sword cultivator from the Central Plains. Lin Junbi will cover the sword cultivators from the Southern Poso Continent, Deng Liang will contact all sword cultivators from the Northern Julu Continent, Song Gaoyuan will transmit messages to the Golden Armor Continent, Xuan Can will be in charge of the Flowing Clouds Continent, and Cao Jun will handle the White Ice Continent.”

Many of these newly appointed Hidden Official lineage sword cultivators were skilled in mental calculations and strategies, proficient in games of chess; Lin Junbi and Xuan Can were both true masters.

Mi Yu truly had questions and asked the Hidden Official directly, “Why not have each continent’s sword cultivators contact their own Sword Immortals? Wouldn’t that be less likely to cause hesitation?”

Chen Ping’an countered, “Deng Liang and the other foreign sword cultivators came to the Sword Qi Great Wall, putting their lives on the line. Now they’re being pulled in to serve as Hidden Official lineage sword cultivators while doing this thankless job, and they shouldn’t be denied the opportunity to earn some goodwill.”

His words were direct.

He laid it out plainly as a business deal.

Lin Junbi smiled knowingly.

The other foreign sword cultivators felt a bit embarrassed, but more importantly, they were grateful, feeling a deeper appreciation for this Hidden Official.

If they could live, who would wish to die? If they could survive and live with a clear conscience, then thinking more about the future path to greatness was only natural.

Mi Yu pondered for a moment, understanding the connections, and helplessly smiled, awkwardly clasping his fists, indicating his understanding and raising no further questions.

The local sword cultivators were responsible for communicating with their own local sword cultivators. However, for the foreign sword cultivators like Lin Junbi, the flying sword communications had hidden nuances and significance. For instance, Lin Junbi would transmit messages to the southern Poso Continent, while the northernmost Aiai Continent’s sword cultivator Deng Liang would cover the northeastern Julu Continent; the other sword cultivators followed suit, all sending flying swords to neighboring continents.

This kind of goodwill was like the ferryboats crossing continents, where the ferry operators made no profit but engaged in the most just business. Such sincere goodwill would naturally last long, allowing for lasting thoughts of each other. As for the local sword cultivators regarding the young sword cultivators who had joined the Hidden Official lineage, they already held them in high regard, so there was no need for Hidden Official Chen Ping’an to go out of his way to make things even better for Deng Liang and Xuan Can.

Lin Junbi was the first to think of it, and the other young foreign sword cultivators quickly realized it. After all, being selected by the Sword Qi Great Wall to become part of the Hidden Official lineage meant, as Chen Ping’an said, while their cultivation levels might not be high, none of them lacked sharp minds.

Thus, there truly was only one who needed to inquire—Mi Yu, the highest in cultivation.

Chen Ping’an picked up a stack of books, over ten in total, all titled simply “Volume A Main Book” and “Volume A Supplementary Book,” and explained, “The next matter is of utmost importance. Listen carefully.”

Chen Ping’an held up the top two books, explaining, “These two books record in detail the names of our sword cultivators in the upper five realms, their life-bound flying swords, and the unique abilities of those flying swords. The main book lists the Sword Immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall, while the supplementary book lists foreign Sword Immortals. Each page records one individual, and the page number will be indicated in the lower right corner. You all must memorize the page numbers and corresponding Sword Immortals thoroughly.”

Then, Chen Ping’an set down these two books and explained the functions of the other books.

The secondary book was responsible for recording all the wild beasts’ upper five realms that had appeared on the battlefield.

On both sides, the main book recorded all the great beasts in the Hall of Heroic Spirits that possessed fourteen thrones, as well as all ascendant and immortal beasts, including those who were sword cultivators at the Yu Pu realm.

The supplementary book recorded all beasts at the Yu Pu realm, excluding sword cultivators.

If names were unknown, then they could arbitrarily assign a name, describing the appearance after transformation, their true forms, key magical treasures, life-bound abilities, and the general faction they belonged to in the wild world, as well as details on who they fought alongside—the more details, the better.

The third book had no supplementary volume.

It recorded all local Earth Immortal sword cultivators, with special emphasis on selecting those whose life-bound flying swords were particularly suited for the battlefield, considering how to pair them in a way that could create effects similar to that of the Earth Immortal couple’s “Drawing the Dragon with a Touch.”

Chen Ping’an also cited several examples, such as the Yuanying sword cultivator Cheng Quan, and the special Earth Immortal sword cultivator Wu Chengpei, who must be treated with special care.

The fourth book recorded the same level of Earth Immortal beasts.

While explaining this last book, Chen Ping’an’s tone was particularly heavy, stating that it was singled out because these beasts from the wild world were the most deserving of death, and they were relatively easier to kill compared to the great beasts. In the past, they had often been overlooked by the Sword Qi Great Wall, either not being taken seriously enough, or due to the need to focus on battles between top-tier forces, leaving them unable to divert their attention. However, once the calculations were made, the killing power of these beasts might not have been apparent at any given moment, but if one were to review the entire course of the war, the longer the battle dragged on, these beasts became a central force causing severe damage to the Sword Qi Great Wall, perhaps even more frightening than certain upper five realms beasts.

In Chen Ping’an’s words, killing these beasts was the most cost-effective. The Sword Immortal seniors wouldn’t need to exert too much effort, yet they could still reap considerable military merit—every bit adds up, and not killing them would be a waste.

Chen Ping’an clearly valued this “fourth book” greatly, holding it for a long time and reluctant to set it down, saying solemnly, “So if we can draft a relatively detailed framework for this fourth book, relying on its incredibly detailed specifics to deduce facts as close to the truth as possible, then we can reopen the main and supplementary books to seek out those Sword Immortal seniors who possess great killing power and strike quickly on the battlefield, to find opportunities to slay the beast cultivators recorded in this book. This, at present, is the most immediate action for our Hidden Official lineage, so I urge you all to consider this carefully. Each name we strike through from the fourth book represents the most tangible military merit for everyone present!”

Xuan Can asked, “What if the senior Sword Immortals have their own reasons and don’t wish to engage in battle? Even after our flying sword messages, it would be useless—what then? On the battlefield, both sides have longstanding grievances. If, for example, one of our Sword Immortals becomes fixated on revenge, insisting on facing their enemy, unwilling to heed our commands, are we to have internal strife?”

Chen Ping’an smiled, “If someone is too proud to move or refuses to leave their post under some pretext, or if what you said were to happen, Xuan Can, you can invoke the identity of a Hidden Official lineage sword cultivator. This is a military order. If that doesn’t work, after two reminders via flying swords, we won’t waste any more words. I will personally seek out Sword Immortals with even greater authority and killing power to request their engagement. If they refuse, then we will simply pursue them!”

The atmosphere grew a bit heavy.

This young Hidden Official was joking, but in truth, this was far from an easy task.

The defection of the previous Hidden Official and the followings of two Sword Immortals, especially the injuries sustained by those on either side, had left the morale at the Sword Qi Great Wall visibly low. Another unexpected incident would undoubtedly add fuel to the fire.

Chen Ping’an set down the book, smiling, “What are you all looking at me for? A Hidden Official of such stature personally running errands and calling out orders—how embarrassing. My own shame is trivial, but I cannot bear to tarnish your reputations. Right, Brother Gu? Isn’t that a fair statement?”

Gu Jianlong nodded vigorously.

Chen Ping’an’s smile faded, “You all probably don’t yet fully grasp the weight of the term ‘Hidden Official lineage.’ Here at the Sword Qi Great Wall, these four characters can determine life and death without needing to reason!”

Chen Ping’an continued, “If you harbor doubts in your hearts, it’s no problem; just wait and see. I’m not afraid to wager the head of a Sword Immortal to prove the truth of this matter. As for all of you, why worry? If the sky falls, just say that our Hidden Official lineage’s twelve members will naturally bear the brunt of it.”

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 738: Settling Accounts Across the World (Part Two)

Chen Ping'an picked up the latest blank ledger, the "Wu Ben," which followed immediately after the "Ding Ben."

The Wu Ben recorded the strategies for sieges in the previous three battles, detailing every aspect meticulously. It included troop distributions, the sixty small battlefields of the barbaric world, the speed of troop redeployments, and whether the siege style remained steady or was frequently adaptable—everything was to be documented.

As a result, this ledger was bound to be thick and heavy, and its content would constantly be supplemented, growing denser by the day.

Next was the Ji Ben. 

This ledger would chronicle all the merits and demerits of the twelve sword cultivators from the Hidden Official lineage in minute detail. 

This was a record of achievements, as well as a book for self-reflection.

The sole author was, of course, the newly appointed Hidden Official, Chen Ping'an. However, only Chen Ping'an had the privilege to peruse it.

Then came the Geng Ben.

This was intended to record the names of all sword cultivators who died in battle or lost their life swords. 

It was destined to be another hefty tome.

Deng Liang asked, “Should we record the sword cultivators who died or lost their swords in the previous two battles right away?”

Chen Ping'an replied straightforwardly, “No need. We can add that later. This one should only be written when we have the time.”

The living were always more important than the dead.

Such was the nature of war.

Deng Liang nodded, showing no dissent, and secretly let out a sigh of relief. 

If Chen Ping'an had answered incorrectly regarding this matter, then the hearts of all the sword cultivators, including Deng Liang himself, would have scattered like ashes.

Everyone was quite intelligent; whether as the new Hidden Official or as the second shopkeeper under the identity of a disciple of the Confucian Sage, if Chen Ping'an could not manage to suppress them and earn their respect in this "small world," then leaving aside other matters, the Ji Ben would become a huge joke. Given that the Hidden Official lineage had just begun to take shape, it would only serve as a burden rather than a benefit.

In this small world, only those with the strongest hearts could command reason.

There was an ancient saying at the Sword Qi Great Wall that seemed quite ridiculous but was, in reality, extremely cruel.

Sword cultivators from the lower five realms would often boast, “I’m better than Zong Yuan.”

It was important to note that this old sword immortal had fought alongside Chen Qingdu for the longest time after Long Jun and Guan Zhao, holding the highest status and was reputed to be the one most likely to break through the “great bottleneck” of ascendant sword cultivators.

During the brutal battle where the demon army flooded the city, it was he alone who wielded his sword to slay two ascendant demons, and with Chen Qingdu's help, they managed to repel the barbaric forces.

According to military merit, Zong Yuan could certainly have his name inscribed, and it would only take two characters. However, being dead meant he could no longer have two characters carved into the Sword Qi Great Wall.

A dead old sword immortal, a great sword immortal, could hardly be seen as formidable if he could not even wield his sword anymore. Not at all.

Chen Ping'an set the blank ledger down.

Geng, then, autumn harvest awaiting the spring.

It was initially a phrase filled with hopeful meaning but had turned into a grand delusion.

Chen Ping'an continued discussing the Xin Ben, the Ren Ben, and finally the Gui Ben.

The Xin Ben.

This would tally the battle losses in the barbaric world.

The Ren Ben.

This would account for all the assets of the Sword Qi Great Wall, including the sword workshop, clothing workshop, and alchemy workshop, with a particular focus on coordinating with the Nalan and Yan families responsible for trade at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

In a war, aside from the consumption of both sides' forces, it was also a battle over the intangible foundations, celestial coins, and precious materials.

The Gui Ben.

In every battlefield, the twelve members of the Hidden Official lineage could evaluate, deduce, and speculate on the next offensive and defensive battles, freely expressing their thoughts and insights, writing them down at any time to be submitted to Guo Zhujiu, who would compile them for Chen Ping'an.

After placing all the ledgers in order, Chen Ping'an said, “Having discussed the second and third matters, it’s time to address the first. The previous division of responsibilities for Lin Junbi was not an issue before, but given the current situation, we will make some changes. This is also a key principle for our Hidden Official lineage going forward. We can no longer approach battles with the same unchanging strategies as before; we must adapt at all times. Every change must yield the best results through our collective wisdom. Every time we send a message via flying sword, it must benefit the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall!”

Chen Ping'an meticulously delineated the detailed responsibilities of the twelve individuals and emphasized that each sword cultivator must keep an eye on the overall trend of the battlefield, never focusing solely on their small patch of land. To not demand such from the twelve would easily lead to small gains at the cost of significant losses on a larger scale, resulting in a seemingly bizarre yet undeniable account within the Hidden Official lineage—one that would come at the greater cost of unnecessary deaths among hundreds of sword cultivators.

“Heroes slay the enemy, all within the pen.”

Chen Ping'an finally smiled, bending down to pick up a folding fan, opening the jade bamboo fan with a grin, and said cheerfully, “Now, I invite you all to join me in calculating the barbaric world. What skill is there in merely making money? If we’re to earn, let’s earn those heads of great demons!”

Only at this moment did Lin Junbi truly feel admiration for Chen Ping'an.

He truly was the esteemed teacher in name of that Mr. Cui.

A legacy passed down, with achievements to the utmost!

Chen Ping'an closed the fan and smiled at Pang Yuanji, calling him by name, “Pang Yuanji, remember to write on the Yi Ben that ‘Xiao Xian, also known as Zhengyun, a bottleneck sword cultivator of the ascendant realm, with an unclear life sword’—make sure this does not end up in the Jia Ben. If you have any leads on this person's life sword, you can certainly add that in the book, just for reference. I can then record a merit for you in the Ji Ben.”

Pang Yuanji's face turned pale as he nodded silently.

The previous Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall was named Xiao Xian.

This was a name many young sword cultivators at the Sword Qi Great Wall had long forgotten.

They had grown accustomed to referring to her simply as the Hidden Official.

Chen Ping'an narrowed his eyes and asked, “You nodded but said nothing. Forgive my dullness; I cannot tell whether you know anything about this person’s life sword.”

Pang Yuanji shook his head, “I do not know.”

Chen Ping'an chuckled, “It’s fine. The great war is prolonged, and that person should not act for now. If you happen to forget and later remember, there will still be a merit to be had.”

Their exchange left Sword Immortal Mi Yu, along with the other sword cultivators who had initially kept their distance, feeling a chill run down their spines.

Chen Ping'an looked around, lightly shaking the folding fan, his hair fluttering, “I already know your names, origins, and realms. However, I have an unusual request: please tell me your greatest strengths and weaknesses. This is a small matter; everyone should focus on their important tasks first. When I ask, just share your thoughts with me. I hope you all can be open and honest; this matter is no trifling matter.”

Lin Junbi was somewhat puzzled.

Chen Ping'an's actions certainly weren’t a likable gesture.

However, Lin Junbi quickly understood.

Chen Ping'an needed to grasp the hearts of all members of the Hidden Official lineage as quickly as possible.

If the standoff between the Sword Qi Great Wall and the barbaric world was the largest battlefield, then the Hidden Official lineage and all the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall would be the second. Within the Hidden Official lineage itself, the twelve individuals formed the third battlefield. And seemingly the smallest battlefield—where hearts fluctuated—was significantly impactful; any ripple of intention could greatly affect the dynamics of the first two battlefields due to the weight of their positions.

As the Hidden Official, Chen Ping'an could certainly rely on the subsequent actions of the twelve to gauge their character traits little by little. However, that would be too slow; a delay in strategy for the Hidden Official lineage would lead to a lag in battlefield responses. But with this measure in place, regardless of how the twelve answered, it would serve as a proof, allowing the meticulous Chen Ping'an to make further judgments.

After a moment, everyone provided their answers. Chen Ping'an remained impassive, choosing not to record them directly in the Ji Ben but instead wrote them on a piece of paper, which he tucked into the Ji Ben.

Yu Jianfu approached, pausing for a moment before asking, “Can I help?”

No one turned to look at the noblewoman from the Central Land, and even Lin Junbi dared only to glance slightly, keeping an eye on this potentially significant inquiry.

Chen Ping'an shook his head, “No.”

Yu Jianfu didn’t linger and quietly moved to a distant, secluded spot on the wall to sit alone and drink.

Chen Ping'an turned to Mi Yu, “Sword Immortal Mi Yu, I need you to outline a sword formation within a three-mile radius to serve as a restricted area. Then, recruit a group of young sword cultivators. Their realms can be low, even from the lower five realms; three to five will suffice. Their only responsibility is to inform all passing sword cultivators of the new regulations here. All extraneous personnel are not allowed to come close, and sword immortals are no exception.”

At this point, Chen Ping'an smiled and said, “Sword Immortal Mi Yu, you have the highest realm among us, so you will have to take on the role of the villain. If any conflict arises, just draw your sword; if you can’t handle it, I’ll personally reason with the sword immortals.”

Mi Yu felt slightly reassured and accepted the order, rising to carry out the task.

The rules of the Hidden Official lineage, whether previously slack or strictly adhered to, would only become more unyielding under Chen Ping'an's leadership. It was certain that the Sword Qi Great Wall would soon learn this.

Chen Ping'an closed the folding fan gently, placed it on the table, and then removed the jade token labeled "Hidden Official," placing it beside the fan. He then began drafting the primary and secondary volumes of the Jia Ben, a series of names already clear in his mind, allowing him to write quickly.

Named after the Tian Gan, he designated both the Jia Ben and Yi Ben with their respective secondary volumes.

Perfectly, there were twelve volumes.

Now, the Hidden Official lineage also amounted to exactly twelve individuals.

Chen Ping'an hoped that after the great war, everyone could each take away a volume.

If they were all still alive, that is.

Suddenly, Xuan Can spoke solemnly, “Great Sword Immortal Yue Qing is currently wielding tremendous sword energy, but it’s affecting the overall sword formation. The nearby two sword immortals can only follow suit. Although the cooperation within the small range of sword immortals is evident, several earth immortals and other mid-five-realm sword cultivators are significantly slowed in their strikes, resulting in greater losses of their life swords.”

Soon, two other sword cultivators nodded, each affirming, “Indeed.” “That’s true.”

Chen Ping'an cast a glance at the drawing and continued to focus on writing in the Jia Ben, saying nonchalantly, “Flying sword message to Yue Qing.”

Wang Xinshui quickly sensed the urgency and controlled a flying sword to concisely explain the situation, glancing at the defense map each sword immortal held. The flying sword vanished in an instant, heading toward Great Sword Immortal Yue Qing, and the young sword cultivator began to sweat nervously, ultimately feeling apprehensive. Although Wang Xinshui was one of the talented sword cultivators in the Sword Qi Great Wall's history, commanding a peak sword immortal was akin to instructing them on how to wield their sword; how could he feel at ease?

In a moment, Chen Ping'an lifted his head while continuing to write, his gaze sharp as he said, “Wang Xinshui, send another flying sword message to Yue Qing. Don’t bother with reasoning; directly tell him that if he doesn’t change his sword, he should roll off the city wall. Before leaving the wall, remember to complain to the old sword immortal!”

Wang Xinshui trembled as he sent the second flying sword message.

Not only that, but Chen Ping'an also seemed to remember something, cursing under his breath, and directly used his own flying sword to send a message to the old sword immortal.

Then, he instructed Guo Zhujiu to send a flying sword message to the jade purity realm sword immortal Wu Chengpei, inquiring about the progress of refining the “Sweet Rain” sword, and then said to everyone, “These matters are your responsibilities; I don’t want to remind you a second time.”

Moments later, not only did Great Sword Immortal Yue Qing retract his sword slightly, but this restricted area also welcomed an unexpected guest.

It seemed that Chen Ping'an's flying sword message had led the old sword immortal to personally issue orders, bringing in a significant figure to prevent such incidents from occurring; otherwise, it wouldn’t have taken two flying sword messages to achieve the desired effect.

The Old Deaf Man.

Mi Yu naturally did not dare to stop him and led this ancient being, one of the peak ten, toward the Hidden Official’s side to discuss matters.

Only to find that Chen Ping'an had already fixed his gaze on the ground beneath himself and the Old Deaf Man.

Mi Yu felt a chill.

Chen Ping'an raised his gaze and told the Old Deaf Man, “Change it; I don’t trust you.”

The Old Deaf Man paused, scratching his head, seemingly unperturbed, and immediately turned to leave, disappearing in an instant.

Before long, he was replaced by another individual—the female sword immortal, Lu Zhi.

Chen Ping'an said, “Lu Zhi, be careful to guard our sword cultivators here from surprise attacks by great demons. If anyone dies, I will hold you accountable!”

Lu Zhi nodded and headed toward the northern city wall to command the battlefield, speaking plainly, “I will not give the Hidden Official any chance for accountability.”

Lin Junbi glanced at Chen Ping'an, who seemed unwilling to even acknowledge Lu Zhi’s words, feeling a rush of admiration.

Chen Ping'an set down his pen, stood up, and went around the desk to crouch over the drawing, “I am even more worried about you all. I will keep an eye on you for half an hour, so I will only give you half an hour to meet my expectations. If anyone fails to meet my standards, you will still be sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage, but you must pass on those tasks that require thought to others. If others can’t do it, then I will personally take over. I simply do not believe that this small group of the most intelligent people in the world can’t measure up to a mere lower five-realm Qi practitioner! If in the end, aside from Chen Ping'an, everyone else in the Hidden Official lineage is deemed useless, I believe the gossip that spreads will not be pleasant.”

All the sword cultivators grew increasingly tense, feeling as if they were facing an enemy even more daunting than being on the battlefield.

Mi Yu's feelings were mixed.

This young man was truly terrifying.

Half an hour later, Chen Ping'an evaluated each of the eleven individuals, standing up with the closed folding fan tapping against his palm, smiling, “Very good, your skills in countering are exceptional. It turns out I am the one who’s idle. Especially you, Pang Yuanji, and Lin Junbi, Guo Zhujiu, in this half hour, you have nearly no flaws; you have made me pick at straws.
