When the two swords clashed, a deafening explosion of sword light erupted before Chen Ping'an, creating a blinding display of brilliant colors. The splattered "Burning Flower" and "Sky Light" instantly shredded the robe from the clothing shop into pieces, and the flying sword "Burning Flower" entered the golden Sword Lock Talisman, causing it to develop cracks of ash, interlacing in all directions, clearly threatening to break through the talisman with a single push.

With the talisman’s assistance in stalling the flying sword's attack somewhat, Chen Ping'an summoned a movement talisman and retreated ten or so zhang.

All Chen Ping'an could do was cast another talisman to escape.

Two jade purity realm sword immortals' life-protecting flying swords were nearly shadowing each other, but "Sky Full of Haze" was to save a life, while "Burning Flower" sought to take one.

"Burning Flower" aimed to achieve the utmost speed, plunging an inch into Chen Ping'an's heart.

This was the deadly strike of a sword immortal at close range.

What was even more ruthless was that Lie Ji not only did not retract his flying sword but rather shattered his own life-protecting sword, risking his own foundational path.

Mi Yu's sword struck down on Lie Ji’s shoulder, slicing through his resilient body in half.

As Lie Ji's soul left his body, he abandoned his true form and aimed to use his sword shop's long sword to decapitate the new Hidden Official.

Simultaneously, after the explosion of his life-protecting flying sword within Chen Ping'an, Lie Ji's soul was also affected by his own technique. The relatively weaker soul of Yuan You seemed to bathe in the glow of Lie Ji's last sword, as man and sword, path and life, vanished into thin air together.

Mi Yu withdrew his life-protecting flying sword, holding his long sword without sheathing it for a long time.

Because Mi Yu knew that he had been severely harmed by this deranged Lie Ji.

From this moment on, whether he would be thrown into the old deaf man's prison still depended on whether his brother Mi Hu's immortal realm was sufficient to protect him.

Lu Zhi hurriedly arrived on his sword, his face ashen. Without even glancing at the dazed Mi Yu, he gritted his teeth and said, "You are truly a waste!"

Lu Zhi immediately formed sword seals, attempting to gather the remnants of the young Hidden Official's soul, seeking any possible chance for Chen Ping'an.

But it was all in vain.

Lie Ji's strike had been too decisive.

Lu Zhi turned his gaze toward the distant thatched cottage, mentally inquiring the Grand Sword Immortal.

Chen Qingdu said, "Let the troubled seedlings choose three sword cultivators to join him in entering the Hidden Official's line."

Lu Zhi furiously retorted, "Just like that?!"

Chen Qingdu replied, "You, Lu Zhi, have the nerve to ask me?"

Lu Zhi snapped, "Am I supposed to accompany Chen Ping'an everywhere? What about the safety of the other sword cultivators in the Hidden Official's line? How should Mi Yu be handled? Executed?!"

Chen Qingdu said, "We’ll talk about that later."

Lu Zhi suppressed the killing intent in his heart and brought Mi Yu back to the horse-walking path where the Hidden Official's line had gathered.

Upon seeing those younger disciples, Lu Zhi hesitated for a moment, an unprecedented act, before finally saying, "The Hidden Official was killed by the traitor Lie Ji, and Lie Ji is dead as well. Mi Yu is under suspicion and is to be detained temporarily. Troubled Seedling will bring three people into the Hidden Official's line. You must leave the city walls immediately and relocate to the summer retreat."

Guo Zhujiu laughed heartily, "Great Sword Immortal Lu, you certainly know how to tell jokes."

Lin Junbi and the others also appeared skeptical, exchanging glances.

Lu Zhi sighed, "That’s how it is. Leave the city walls and take care of yourselves."

With that, Lu Zhi departed.

Guo Zhujiu playfully asked, "Mi Jianxian, now that Lu Zhi has left, you shouldn't keep joking. Or else I might get angry…"

Though the girl smiled, tears were already welling up in her eyes. As she spoke, her expression tightened, and she found herself unable to utter another word.

Lin Junbi's emotions were extraordinarily complex.

This Hidden Official position was indeed not easy to hold.

Lie Ji, a jade purity realm sword immortal, was actually quite low on the roster in the original documents, only a few pages away from Mi Yu.

Yet precisely because of this, Lie Ji became the unexpected variable.

As for why Lie Ji acted this way, who could tell?

The historical grievances of the Sword Qi Great Wall were far too many, and almost none of the stories of sword immortals ended happily.

Dong Budu's face turned pale, clearly unable to accept this inexplicable outcome.

Guo Jianlong and Wang Xinshui clenched their fists, utterly unable to accept this matter.

Xuan Shen and other sword cultivators also fell silent, disheartened.

Soon, a young-looking sword immortal stepped forward, just over a hundred years old, a jade purity realm cultivator, praised as having the most stable cultivation in the past three thousand years of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

This person was Qiu Miao.

He had followed A Liang into the depths of the barbaric world.

Beside Qiu Miao was a Golden Core realm female sword cultivator, naturally charming, named Luo Zhenyi. She was around the same age as Qiu Miao and incredibly beautiful, beloved by many unattached sword immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Additionally, there was a young Golden Core realm sword cultivator, Xu Ning, who possessed two life-protecting flying swords, "White Practice" and "Mountain Color," which complemented each other.

There was also a Dragon Gate realm young sword cultivator, Chang Taiqing.

Compared to the dazzling peaks of Qi Shou and Gao Ye, the sword cultivators under Qiu Miao’s leadership, who spent their days in the large characters at the southern wall, had extraordinary composure, even the young sword cultivators appearing like ancient Buddhist monks or Daoist sages, their sword hearts dry and withered.

Qiu Miao said, "Mi Yu can stay by my side. The rest will move to the summer retreat together. Zhenyi, Ning, Taiqing, you three assist."

Mi Yu smiled bitterly.

Qiu Miao's meaning was simple: staying by his side meant Mi Yu could do nothing he wanted.

The first batch of sword cultivators from the Hidden Official's line, including Lin Junbi, silently began to relocate. There was no animosity toward the later sword cultivators, but there was also no goodwill.

In the end, they had unknowingly grown accustomed to Chen Ping'an's presence.

Only Guo Zhujiu remained behind, sitting dazedly, saying, "I won’t leave; I’ll wait for my master."

Qiu Miao replied, "That's fine. Whenever you feel you can’t wait any longer, go to the summer retreat to work."

Qiu Miao led the group, taking to the skies on their swords, heading toward the important location west of the city.

Only Guo Zhujiu was left behind, sitting alone at the desk.

All the sword cultivators landed on the plaza outside the summer retreat’s hall.

Qiu Miao paused for a moment.

No wonder he had not been immediately appointed as the new Hidden Official.

Qiu Miao did not care about this; in fact, whether he became the Hidden Official sword cultivator or stayed at the city walls to kill enemies, it made no difference to Qiu Miao, as it was all about cultivation.

The three sword cultivators, including Luo Zhenyi, were surprised.

As for Mi Yu, he was nearly moved to tears.

Lin Junbi sighed in relief.

That’s good.

Now, with this Hidden Official, they were all on the same rope, sharing honor and disgrace.

Compared to the unknown Qiu Miao, Lin Junbi preferred to work with this fellow before her.

It turned out that at the entrance to the hall, a young man in a blue robe with sleeves draped smiled at everyone.

His face was pale, yet his eyes sparkled.

Chen Ping'an waved to Mi Yu, "Come walk with me."

Then Chen Ping'an looked to Qiu Miao, "In the future, when I'm not around, I’ll trouble you four to listen to Lin Junbi’s opinions."

Qiu Miao nodded, "No problem."

Chen Ping'an turned to Guo Jianlong.

Guo Jianlong immediately understood, praising Qiu Miao, "Sword Immortal Qiu Miao, so grand and magnificent, can be testified by the sun and moon!"

Luo Zhenyi furrowed her brow.

Chen Ping'an had already taken Mi Yu into a side corridor, strolling toward another place.

The group entered the hall and soon discovered that all the secret records from the winter residence had already been moved here. The hall, aside from the entrance, now had three walls lined with bookshelves, orderly arranged. Many secret record books had labels attached, making it easy for everyone to pull and reference them. It was evident that this was the handiwork of the Hidden Official, written in a neat and precise small script.

Chen Ping'an remained silent.

Mi Yu felt a surge of emotions and also said nothing.

Chen Ping'an took out his sword nurturing gourd and retrieved a jug of bamboo sea cave wine, handing it to Mi Yu.

Mi Yu bitterly remarked, "I fear this wine."

Chen Ping'an laughed, "There are a thousand kinds of drinkers, but only wine is faultless. But it’s fine to drink. If you have questions, just ask."

Mi Yu inquired, "What happened? Who is the Hidden Official up there on the city walls?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "It's a high-quality substitute talisman, plus a puppetry technique, a truly solid golden body warrior’s physique. With the help of the Grand Sword Immortal to shield some things, it’s rather discreet. But if it were only that, it certainly wouldn’t fool you, Mi Yu, which means it probably wouldn't fool Lie Ji either. So, I attached a part of my soul to the talisman puppet. Up there on the city walls, 'I' must carefully control every step and breath, and right now, I'm quite injured, and it's not an act. However, paying this little price unearthed an unexpected traitor, and he was a sword immortal, so it’s worth it. In fact, the person I wanted to fish out wasn’t initially Lie Ji; there was someone else. As for who, you’ve been following me closely, there are traces to follow, but I estimate you’ve forgotten."

Mi Yu tentatively asked, "What you said earlier about 'in case,' was that a setup to lure out a big fish like Yang Zhi or Huang Luan? Were you anticipating this ambush from the start?"

Chen Ping'an laughed, "Our sword cultivators can send messages to the wild world in secret; naturally, the other side can also send messages back to the Sword Qi Great Wall. As for why Lie Ji betrayed us, whether it’s due to more resentment towards the Haoran world or a greater grievance against the Grand Sword Immortal, or even if he bears hatred for the entire Sword Qi Great Wall, there must be reasons. Otherwise, he wouldn’t have been so decisive in his attack; however, the intricacies within this, I’m not interested. In any case, Lie Ji is dead."

Chen Ping'an emphasized, "People like him should die sooner rather than later. Otherwise, he might truly drag one or two great sword immortals down with him at a critical moment."

Mi Yu halted, his face extremely grim. "I was pulled into the Hidden Official's line just for this day, for this matter?!"

Chen Ping'an also stopped, nodding and speaking frankly, "Not only to pull you into the fold but also to invite Lu Zhi. It’s essentially the same. Truth and falsehood, reality and illusion; without this strategy, how could I deceive a scheming sword immortal? With a sword immortal harboring betrayal in his heart, their minds become exceptionally sharp. Lu Zhi is protecting all of us in the Hidden Official’s line. Unless a sword immortal at the immortal realm comes near me for a close-range strike, there’s no opportunity. Otherwise, anyone attempting to attack would be deluding themselves. With this premise, when I leave Lu Zhi’s side, it creates the illusion of missing out on a rare opportunity."

At this point, Chen Ping'an leaned against the corridor pillar, shaking the sword nurturing gourd in his hand, smiling broadly, "It’s a great opportunity; it would be a pity to miss it. We could try it out."

"Lu Zhi's protection and vigilance are merely a façade for others to see. The Hidden Official is exceptionally secure, with no life-threatening worries. Once I leave Lu Zhi’s side, the absence of a jade purity realm Mi Yu beside me becomes a necessary hint. Otherwise, the assassin would worry I’m too confident and suspect there’s a plot at play. Not carrying a sword of celestial-grade quality and not wearing a celestial-grade robe, is also a reasonable approach. Thus, without the robe, and without a reliable sword immortal like Mi Yu to guard me, the Hidden Official’s true reliance becomes solely on being within the Sword Qi Great Wall and his own golden body warrior physique."

Mi Yu gulped down a mouthful of wine, still remaining silent.

Chen Ping'an said, "Once the Hidden Official dies, it’s only natural for morale to wane, and my sword formation will be affected. Therefore, we can fish even better now. Compared to killing a sword immortal, this is the outcome I desire most."

Mi Yu stared blankly at this young man.

Chen Ping'an laughed, "In fact, I've thought of a lot, and most of it truly is just thinking, without any real use."

Mi Yu had never been good at pondering such grand matters. Even regarding his stagnation in cultivation, his brother Mi Hu had been anxious for many years, but Mi Yu himself had always been more open-minded. Thus, he only asked the question he most wanted to know, "If you hold a grudge against someone from the Sword Qi Great Wall, wouldn't you not even know how they died in the end?"

Chen Ping'an was taken aback for a moment, then thought seriously for a while before nodding, "I should be able to do that, but I’ve never thought about it. Because for me, it’s not worth the loss. A piece of Dao heart is hard to come by; having been poor since childhood, I’ve grown accustomed to cherishing rare things."

Mi Yu's gaze suddenly sharpened. "For example, the Qi family, who made things difficult for the Ning family back in the day?! Do you hate them? Truly not a bit of personal interest? In that thirteen-driven dispute, after you became the Hidden Official, you’ve surely seen all the archived records. You must have found traces of key words spoken by certain sword immortals at specific times; you know much more about the filthy inside story!"

Chen Ping'an smiled, "Mi Brother, you guess."

Chen Ping'an handed over the sword nurturing gourd, but Mi Yu’s wine jug remained still. Chen Ping'an looked helpless and said, "In any case, I'm not the kind of person who holds grudges, on my conscience."

Mi Yu seemed even more dispirited than Chen Ping'an, who had suffered soul damage. His spirit was utterly drained, and he casually asked, "That girl Guo Zhujiu is still up there on the city walls. When will you notify her to come back?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "Wait a little longer."

Mi Yu shook his head, "Calculating and scheming, you even won’t let a little girl off. That Guo Zhujiu is your disciple! Even if you have good intentions, I still find it quite strange, Chen Ping'an. Aren’t you exhausted? Not a shred of guilt?"

Chen Ping'an countered, "Is it enough to only seek to be guiltless to oneself? Do you think Lie Ji was guiltless? A dignified sword immortal, he even sacrificed his own life. What kind of grievances and guilt must he have harbored?"

Mi Yu had no retort.

Chen Ping'an looked up at the southern city wall, laughing, "Burning Flower, Burning Flower, what a fine name—‘Mountain Green and Flower Ready to Burn.’ Sword immortals are indeed skilled at naming their life-protecting flying swords."

The two returned to the hall of the summer retreat.

Mi Yu took his seat.

Chen Ping'an did not sit down but instead settled on the steps outside the door.

Chen Ping'an merely said, "Aside from the Hidden Official line’s flying swords, no one is allowed to leave the summer retreat even a step. No private meetings with outsiders are permitted. If anyone is found, they will be executed for treason. Moreover, our Hidden Official line’s message-carrying flying swords, Qiu Miao and the four of them, along with Lin Junbi and the twelve others, must all know the contents of the messages, line by line, word by word, and Mi Yu Jianxian must record them."

Xu Ning looked up at the figure outside the door, asking, "If you don’t trust us, why pull us into the Hidden Official line?"

Chen Ping'an, holding the sword nurturing gourd in one hand and a folding fan in the other, said, "Before you speak to me, first respectfully address me as Hidden Official."

Xu Ning really did add "Hidden Official" before repeating that sentence.

Only then did Chen Ping'an smile and say something incredibly frank: "If I can't even trust myself, how can I trust you?"

Xu Ning fell silent, while Luo Zhenyi and Chang Taiqing suddenly raised their heads, expressions full of anger.

Xuan Shen and Cao Jun, who deeply revered the Hidden Official, being outsiders among the sword cultivators, were even more direct than Guo Jianlong and Wang Xinshui. The two young people did not conceal their allegiance.

Qiu Miao said, "Less talk among the crowd. If there’s nothing to do, return early. If there’s work, let’s get to it. Since the four of us have become sword cultivators of the Hidden Official line, everything will follow the rules."

Chen Ping'an turned his head and smiled, "If I were to die, Qiu Miao sword immortal, you and Junbi would indeed be the best candidates for the Hidden Official."

Lin Junbi feigned deafness.

Qiu Miao acted as though he had heard nothing.

In the night, a message-carrying flying sword flew toward the city wall, after which appeared a heartbroken young girl who slowly flew over, her face sorrowful, constantly wiping her tears.

After gracefully landing, her movements were still a bit unsteady.

Upon seeing her master, who had already risen, she immediately beamed.

Chen Ping'an gently smiled, "You’ve come a bit late."

Guo Zhujiu sheathed her sword, standing in front of Chen Ping'an, excitedly bouncing in place with her arms swaying, her eyes sparkling, "Master, let me tell you! Earlier, I was the only one who believed my master wouldn’t die. I just didn’t expect you to be so powerful, not only alive and well but you even managed to fool me! I couldn’t even break through my small brain to think that you were already in the summer retreat. Unbelievable, truly incredible…"

"I said as long as my master is here, you don’t have to think about life and death. It should always be like this; I’m willing to believe in my master."

Chen Ping'an chuckled, reaching into his belongings to pull out a small bamboo box, "This is a reward for you. If it’s not too heavy, carry it. But you mustn't show off to others."

Guo Zhujiu lifted the small bamboo box, softly asking, "Master, what’s this bamboo box? Did it get some spirit and come to find you? Fine, when my elder sister gave me this bamboo box, it transformed into a spirit. Later, Master, you can make a regular box without legs and gift it to my elder sister. This one that has grown into a small bamboo box will belong to me."

Chen Ping'an shook his head, laughing, "You can negotiate with Pei Qian later; Master won’t show favoritism."

Chen Ping'an ruffled Guo Zhujiu’s hair, "Off you go; don’t delay important matters."

Guo Zhujiu bounced up the steps and then suddenly turned around, jumping backward, facing the hall, standing still for a moment before finally turning and stepping forward.

Chen Ping'an did not follow into the hall but continued strolling through the summer retreat.

Every place he walked was a small world.

Chen Ping'an plucked a blue talisman from his belongings, gently shaking it, saying, "The Grand Sword Immortal won’t let you go back empty-handed. In the near future, any sword immortal attempting to spy on the summer retreat will be killed directly. Those willing to take such risks are not patient enough; they won’t hold much value for us at the Sword Qi Great Wall."

After pausing for a moment, Chen Ping'an added, "If such a contribution comes knocking, it would best be placed on the shoulders of the head of our Hidden Official line, Sword Immortal Mi Yu."

Even though Chen Ping'an was speaking in his own small world, to Chen Qingdu, it was as insubstantial as paper.

Though Chen Qingdu neither agreed nor refused, the meaning was quite clear: having chosen you, Chen Ping'an, as the Hidden Official, feel free to make your own moves.

This old great sword immortal changed the topic, asking again, "Have you really thought this through? If it is indeed you, will you not regret it? Will you not clarify things with Ning Yao first?"

Chen Ping'an did not answer, also changing the topic, "How is my senior brother doing?"

Chen Qingdu replied that he was doing fine.

Chen Ping'an then put away the talisman, hiding it in his sleeve. He switched to a different talisman, gently twisting it and silently reciting the incantation, instantly arriving at the other winter residence.

In the summer retreat, there was a towering ancient tree, the green tree bringing coolness in autumn.

The standout feature of this residence was a scepter inscribed with poetic verses, shaped like a fish tail yet resembling a fungus.

Chen Ping'an walked alone through the massive courtyard.

Both residences were quite simplistic inside, lacking any unnecessary embellishments.

Chen Ping'an planned to familiarize himself with this environment first.

Before leaving this silent residence and returning to the summer retreat, Chen Ping'an murmured to himself, "I’m ready. I’m coming."

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 742: A Gentle Breeze Under the Soft Moon (Part 1)

The Hanging Mountain originally had only one grand gate leading to the Sword Qi Great Wall, but now a larger entrance had been opened, leaving the old gate much less bustling.

To put it in the words of the sword-wielding man, it was a case of "loving the new and hating the old," which had truly hurt people's hearts.

An exceptionally senior little Taoist boy remained seated, engrossed in a book. He was reading a collection of miscellaneous writings by a disheartened scholar. With a casual gesture, he conjured a handful of silvery moonlight to envelop himself and the book, illuminating the pages like fireflies in the night.

Last time, he had been thoroughly disgusted by that white-clad youth whose head had been caught in a door and then kicked by a donkey. What could have been a beautiful tale of talented scholars and fair maidens in the Pinewood Collection had been twisted by that boy into a censored version of a romantic novel. As a result, he had spent several days unable to recover, feeling demotivated to read anything, and was left with no choice but to abandon this rare pleasure and simply daydream.

However, after enduring a month without reading, boredom had driven him to pick up a stack of books, diving headfirst into them day and night, utterly mesmerized.

Though the little Taoist boy was a being of divine nature, he read slowly and meticulously. Even with an exceptional memory, he frequently flipped back to earlier pages just to take another glance.

On the other side of the gate, the sword-wielding man, holding his long sword, wandered over to the little Taoist boy. Realizing this could be considered slacking off, he quickly returned, resting the sword against a pillar before grabbing a jug of wine and returning to squat beside the little boy, leaning in to read along. The little Taoist boy preferred to enjoy his reading alone and disliked the smell of alcohol, so he turned away, and the man followed suit, understanding just how bored a sword cultivator could be after years of solitude. They settled into this routine.

The man pointed to a line in the book, saying, “This scholar in the book has some skill, ‘The mountains are clear, the waters are beautiful, the essence of heaven and earth all belongs to the beauty. We men come to this world merely to ruin the mountains and rivers and betray the beauties.’ This line is wonderfully written. It deserves to be highlighted and memorized.”

The little Taoist boy had grown accustomed to the man’s rambling and continued flipping through his book, while the man babbled away without bothering about the boy’s reading pace.

After finishing a book, the man sighed, “Boring, without a hint of spice.”

The little Taoist boy put down his book and picked up another—this one was an adventure novel about dark nights and high winds, depicting martial artists leaping across rooftops. Whenever the man found something exciting, he would take a swig of wine, but his eyes remained glued to the pages, not missing a single word. He clicked his tongue in admiration, “As expected of that little heavenly genius chosen by the heavens, he picks up the unparalleled martial arts that would take others a lifetime to comprehend in just one night. I truly envy him. What a pity the incantation for this technique was written so vaguely; otherwise, I could give it a try…”

“See? I told you, this scruffy old man who loves to spout nonsense is definitely a hidden master! How about that? I was right, right? The old man really looks upon our little genius with admiration. Wow, what a grand gesture! Not only did he use a lifetime’s worth of internal energy to help him open up his meridians, but he also thoroughly cleansed his marrow. Goodness, if he returns to the martial world, wouldn’t he be invincible?”

The book was only halfway through when the little Taoist boy, with a serious tone, interjected, “Clearly, he is not invincible yet, even with a sudden windfall of a lifetime's worth of internal energy added to his own twenty years of training, he only has eighty years of internal energy. There’s a foreshadowing in the story; a notorious demon who has stirred up a bloodbath in the martial world has already cultivated for a hundred years, his internal energy is pure and unfathomable—he cannot be defeated.”

The man stroked his chin, finding it reasonable, “Then he still lacks a weapon that can cut through steel like mud. But I doubt he’ll get his hands on one too quickly; after all, the story is only halfway through.”

The little Taoist boy turned the page slowly, rarely agreeing with the man, “What’s the rush? He’ll definitely get one, otherwise, how could he even fight?”

The man took a hearty swig of wine, “A childhood sweetheart, a righteous female hero encountered in the martial world, a demonic beauty with whom he has a love-hate relationship—none can be missing!”

It was likely that the author, who was simply thinking about earning a bit of money for food and ink, could never imagine that there were two readers so immersed in the story.

Moreover, both readers were “shallow” in their understanding, yet they had genuine affection for the tale.

One was a master whose name was taboo across the land, seeking to learn from the ancient true immortals how to manipulate the elements, grasp the yin and yang, move mountains, and part seas, to breathe in harmony with the universe.

The other was a grand sword immortal from the Sword Qi Great Wall, who had participated in the fierce battles of the Thirteen Struggles and had formed bonds with many heroes, including a female sword immortal.

The little Taoist boy, hailing from an illustrious family and possessing a prestigious lineage, had left his hometown in the Celestial Realm to toughen himself and sharpen his Dao heart.

In contrast, the man could be considered a prisoner among prisoners, forced to guard the gate behind them year after year.

The little Taoist boy closed his book, prompting the man to ask in irritation, “What’s the matter?”

The little Taoist boy replied, “Let’s take it slow; this book is quite good. Read it more carefully.”

The book contained a scene that didn’t describe mountains or immortals but focused on the people of the martial world. In just a few strokes, it allowed the little Taoist boy, who had never truly wandered the martial world, to visualize the narrative.

After the rain, the sky cleared, mist rising from the water, hazy and ethereal. In the heart of the lake was a colorful boat, where a hero stood at the bow, cutting through the water. As it approached the pavilion, the reeds along the path rustled, while inside the pavilion, a guest in white brewed wine, waiting to resolve life and death over a drunken duel.

The man sighed, reclining back, casually asking, “Jiang Daojun, what kind of place is the Celestial Realm?”

The little Taoist boy answered, “It has its customs and rules, similar to this vast world of righteousness.”

The man inquired, “Has Daoist Lao Er gathered five hundred spirit officials yet?”

The little Taoist boy didn’t think this was any secret, “Probably still early. Changing shells and continuing to establish the Daoist temple isn’t easy.”

The man rested his hands behind his head in a comfortable position, crossing his legs, “Everyone is busy.”

The little Taoist boy laughed, “We’re not busy.”

The man gazed at the bright moon, “But we’re still burning the midnight oil.”

A-Liang had once left behind a saying at the Sword Qi Great Wall: those who cannot stay up late will never cultivate any great path.

As for how to stay up late?

The laborious practice of refining Qi and swords is fundamental.

Drinking is the middle ground; even if one runs out of money for wine, the moonlight pouring into the cup costs nothing, and the cup never runs dry.

As for what is above?

Gamblers and drunks, all men, shared a knowing smile.

The little Taoist boy found it odd and turned to the man, “Zhang Lu, are you really this lackluster? The situation at the Sword Qi Great Wall is tense; if you insist on returning to the city wall, Chen Qing wouldn’t stop you, would he?”

The man named Zhang Lu closed his eyes to rest, saying, “I’m just tired.”

The little Taoist boy laughed, “With that mindset, it’ll be hard for you to improve further.”

Zhang Lu softly replied, “Whatever.”

The little Taoist boy waved away the moonlight that resembled a desk lamp, looking up at the sky, “The true flavor of the world can only be tasted by the tranquil.”

“Did your master teach you that?”

“I read it in miscellaneous writings.”

“Jiang Yunsheng, you say when a man sees insult, he draws his sword and stands up to fight, but forgets life and death—is that good?”

“I don’t know, don’t care to think about it.”

“There’s no banquet that doesn’t end, I’ll think of you in the future, and I’ll find you in your hometown to have fun.”

“A big man saying this to another big man, who are you trying to disgust?!” 

“You just look like a child; you’re not that big yet.”

“Zhang Lu, are you looking for a beating?!”

The man turned on his side and fell fast asleep.

If in the vast world of righteousness, even a grand sword immortal in a dire state wouldn’t end up with such a meager existence.

The little Taoist boy continued reading.

Pity the sword immortal Shao Yunyan.

Business, earning silver, never stops day or night.

Every piece of celestial money is praised as the most refined essence of spiritual energy in the world, but whether a single clean piece exists is hard to say.

A massive ferry unloaded goods and exchanged supplies for the Sword Qi Great Wall before departing from the Hanging Mountain dock.

This was a cross-regional ferry from the Southwest Fuyun Continent, specifically from the Mountain Water Cave’s major sect. The ferry had a very rustic name—Basin.

It was said that the founder of the Mountain Water Cave started from humble beginnings in the marketplace, but after making his fortune, he spent his life distancing himself from the past and living on the mountain like a feudal lord. The only time he revealed his true self was when naming the cross-regional ferry—the Basin.

A ferry overseer, a Nascent Soul cultivator, stood on the observation deck of the ferry, silently calculating. This round trip to the Hanging Mountain could at least yield seventy grain rain coins, and with the major dynasties in Fuyun Continent embroiled in chaos, if everything went smoothly and the right buyers were found, doubling the profits was not out of the question.

Meanwhile, because of several newly emerged celestial treasures, there were already more than three semi-celestial weapons on the mountain, leading to bloody conflicts, and many earth immortals had perished. Numerous old tortoises from the upper five realms were also gradually surfacing. If not for the constraints of the Confucian Academy, these old immortals would not remain in the shadows. Otherwise, they wouldn’t be merely puppets pulling strings in such a harmonious manner.

Regardless of the mountains and the plains, such exhausting conflicts were beneficial for the top-tier commercial sects like the Mountain Water Cave.

The Qionglin Sect was wealthy due to the influx of sword cultivators from the Northern Julu Continent, leading to rapid turnover of celestial sects. Once the tide turned, celestial money naturally flowed like water.

Calculating and counting, every bead that rolled was money.

As for the Liu family of the Aiai Continent, they were unique; they could deal with anyone. Many transactions had moved beyond the realm of mere finance; paying money earned them the rise and fall of dynasties, the replacement of powerful families in the celestial realm.

The most frightening part was that the Liu family's principle in any transaction was to ensure the other party could profit first. Even more terrifying was that this principle became an unbreakable family rule, passed down through generations.

The old cultivator returned from this trip to the Hanging Mountain with considerable gains. As the overseer of the Mountain Water Cave's cross-regional ferry, he had received guidance from the founder. Earlier, he had booked several top-tier rooms at the Lingzhi Pavilion and planned to exchange insights with fellow cultivators from Fuyun and Jinjia continents, aiming to join forces for profit. In total, eight cross-regional ferries were to be involved, focusing on profits; otherwise, they would merely give the Sword Qi Great Wall’s Yan family and Nalan family the chance to compare prices and lower them.

This was merely the first matter, with hardly any dissent. The Mountain Water Cave was financially robust and determined to push this initiative, willing to guarantee that after the next transaction, everyone would profit and be happy, proving the feasibility of this method. In the future, they would follow this pattern for the Hanging Mountain. However, if someone ended up in the red, the Mountain Water Cave would compensate them.

The second matter was the current battle at the Sword Qi Great Wall, which was incredibly difficult and required substantial supplies. The Mountain Water Cave took the lead, proposing a plan to collaboratively build several new ferries, hire the old ancestors to help open one or two smoother new routes, eliminate roadblocks, and assist in manning the ferries. Previously, they hadn’t acted because of limited funds, but with the change in circumstances, now that they had sufficient grain rain coins, even if these old ancestors looked down on it, they all had sects, lineages, and families to care for. As long as their respective sect leaders made a case to them with reason and sentiment, there was still hope to persuade these old seniors to step into the mundane.

The third matter was trickier; the two Nascent Soul sword cultivators, Yan Ming and Nalan Caihuan, had gone to the city wall, leaving family affairs to the younger generations. Although they were far from as shrewd as the two financial masters of the Sword Qi Great Wall, the trouble was that this group of people would cling to prices and stubbornly stick to rules. If they refused, both sides would be at a standstill. While everyone knew the Sword Qi Great Wall could not outlast the cross-regional ferry, the longer they stayed at the Hanging Mountain, the more celestial money would flow away, which was no small amount. Thus, not only the Mountain Water Cave, but all cross-regional ferries hoped to break the deadlock.

Historically, during the Great War at the Sword Qi Great Wall, the Nalan family had not hesitated to threaten several cross-regional ferries that insisted on high prices, threatening them to either sell or leave.

Just when these ferry overseers were about to bow their heads and concede, a sudden turn of events occurred. An obscure young man aboard a ferry from Fuyun managed to unite and persuade all ferry overseers from the Seven Continents' sects, declaring that they would withdraw from the Hanging Mountain without profit, as if they were going on a leisurely outing, docking at the Rain Dragon Sect's affiliated island dock, leaving only a message for the Sword Qi Great Wall: they would not earn this money.

This young man, who gained fame and ultimately helped all ferries make a fortune, was none other than the founder of the Mountain Water Cave. At that time, he was merely a Sea Observation Realm cultivator but managed to persuade all the seasoned merchants, earning immense respect. Just thirty years later, he had established his own faction along with cross-regional ferries.

The Nalan family had considered targeting the two cross-regional ferries from the Mountain Water Cave, but time and again, they had handled them effortlessly. Over time, what else could be done? Business continued.

Later, the Yan family emerged, with the patriarch Yan Ming being more amicable than the forthright traders of the Nalan family. He was more like a shrewd businessman, diligently helping the Sword Qi Great Wall save unnecessary expenses, allowing all cross-regional ferries to earn profits, creating a mutually beneficial relationship. After Nalan Caihuan took over the family's financial power, the relationship with the various ferries was also not bad. With both Yan Ming and Nalan Caihuan taking charge of commerce, the relationship between both sides was generally one of mutual non-interference, though there would occasionally be minor conflicts of interest.

An old cultivator’s direct disciple arrived at the observation deck, hesitating to speak.

The old Nascent Soul smiled, “Just say what you want to say.”

The young man asked, “Master, in the past, our Mountain Water Cave ferries agreed with Sword Qi Great Wall to allow credit; after the war, we would settle the debts at the agreed interest, paying less if returned early and more if late. Why does the old ancestor want us to partner with the other ferries to reject this matter?”

The old man gently replied, “Although the Sword Qi Great Wall keeps a tight lid on information, preventing anyone from approaching the city wall—even old acquaintances like me, who used to stay at the sword immortal’s residence for days—this time, once we entered the Sword Qi Great Wall, we couldn't even get into the city, only negotiating business with members of the two families in the mansions between the city and the mirage. The more they conceal, the more it proves that the demon tribe is coming in full force, and this battle at the Sword Qi Great Wall will be brutal. You tell me, how solid are the Yan and Nalan families?”

The young man chuckled, “Yan Ming and Nalan Caihuan, both sword immortals, are surely astute. Their accumulated wealth, whether their own or helping the Sword Qi Great Wall, must be considerable.”

The old man nodded, smiling, “So, this time, we can help the Mountain Water Cave earn a lot more. Not only do we intend to dig out their wealth completely, but we also want to empty their alchemy workshops. As for not allowing credit, we’ll be serious about it—this is no joke—but in reality, it doesn’t have to be taken seriously. How we don't take it seriously would depend on the sincerity of Yan Ming and Nalan Caihuan.”

The young man cautiously said, “The sword immortals have quite good tempers; we mustn’t push them into a corner.”

The old man scoffed, “Nalan family has that old ancestor Nalan Shao'wei, one of the top ten sword immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall. If we were in our Fuyun Continent, who would dare breathe loudly in front of such an old monster? Nalan Shao'wei has a good temper? Not at all. But when it comes to us, what can he do if he has a bad temper? The sword immortal’s killing power is immense, and he enjoys killing? Let him do as he pleases; do they dare?

Next, we will also persuade the old ancestors of other ferries to come out of their seclusion. Thus, celestial money truly is the strongest fist in the world.”

The young man genuinely wanted to ask why they couldn't earn a little less money and didn't always have to squeeze the Sword Qi Great Wall for every last coin, as it seemed unnecessary.

The old man seemed to see through his disciple's thoughts and laughed, “You, your cultivation is fine, but in business, you are utterly clueless and lack wisdom! If you can clearly earn money, yet think about earning less, do you really think you can earn big bucks in this lifetime? As long as you think like that, you’ll never become a person like our old ancestor. Don’t even dream of it; you’re not worthy of even carrying his shoes.”

Finally, the old man said, “You should mind your own business and live well; that’s already impressive. When you become a more important figure in the Mountain Water Cave than me one day, then you’ll have the qualification to talk about earning less. But I can assure you, when that day comes, you’ll want to earn even more than I do. Looking back on today’s thoughts, you’ll find them ridiculous! Why?”

The old man answered himself, “Because you’ll be sitting on the seat of the Mountain Water Cave’s ancestral hall.”

Fu Ke, the youngest Golden Core Earth Immortal in the history of the Rain Dragon Sect, left the ancestral mountain of the sect today to visit a vassal island and meet a friend.

The Rain Dragon Sect itself did not possess cross-regional ferries, as it was unnecessary; with over twenty vassal islands, each with its own docks, and a multitude of sects affiliated with the Rain Dragon Sect, including inner and outer disciples and miscellaneous workers, there were tens of thousands of people.

The vast majority of cross-regional ferries from the Northern Julu Continent and some from the Southern Posa Continent needed to stop here midway.

Fu Ke did not bring a companion; he steered his talisman boat alone to a place called Jade Island. The island was home to celestial trees, precious as jade, sought after by many cross-regional ferries. After making a fortune at the Hanging Mountain, he didn’t lack for this expense, and besides, upon returning home, he would still earn money and enhance his status.

Jade Island was located in the northeast of the Rain Dragon Sect, so in earlier years, one could often see the old rain-dispensing dragons traveling between Jiao Long Ditch and the Southern Posa Continent. If lucky, one might even see a weary dragon struggling to return to the sea. The Rain Dragon Sect had always treated these dragons, following their nature to bring clouds and rain, with kindness. Whenever an exhausted dragon surfaced, unable to return to its lair, a great cultivator would help it navigate the waters back to Jiao Long Ditch.

However, in recent years, such sightings had become rare due to a sword immortal of high skill and poor temper who, seeking fame, had indiscriminately destroyed much of the dragons’ nests. Some long-time residents of Jade Island commented that this sword immortal, despite his prowess, lacked understanding of human interactions, embodying the classic case of virtue not matching position.

Fu Ke was perhaps the most qualified to speak on these rumors, but he chose not to spoil the excitement for his own people.

Fu Ke's talisman boat didn’t head directly to his friend’s private residence, instead landing respectfully at the mountain gate on Jade Island, then slowly making his way. As he walked, he greeted those he encountered. Anyone who exchanged words with Fu Ke, even just casual pleasantries, felt both surprised and honored.

To Fu Ke, this was a minor affair that served two purposes: it helped deepen his approachable image and gave his friend a bit of face. On the mountain and in the plains, it was almost the same; face could be exchanged for money.

Fu Ke’s friend, Yu Fujing, was a fifth realm cultivator with a bit of fame in the Baoping Continent. He and Fu Ke had a long-standing friendship, starting from similar beginnings in their early years. Who would have thought that Fu Ke, who seemed to be at the end of his rope, would eventually find such great fortune in trying to see the Hanging Mountain? Instead of merely seeing the Hanging Mountain, he ended up at the Rain Dragon Sect, climbing the ranks to become a favored son-in-law of the sect, with two heavenly maidens falling for him one after another.

Such a profound opportunity was truly enviable, and his romantic fortune was even more so, enough to make others green with envy.

This news quickly spread back to Baoping Continent with the return of the ferry from Laolong City to Guihua Island, and Fu Ke became a figure admired by many cultivators, making even the immortal masters jealous.

Thus, Yu Fujing had come hoping for luck, initially just wishing to squeeze out a few celestial coins from his good friend Fu Ke, perhaps just a few small grains, to help him out.

Little did he expect that Fu Ke would indeed show loyalty. After Yu Fujing cautiously left the ferry and ventured toward the Rain Dragon Sect, he dared not step onto the island but only reported his name, saying he knew Fu Ke, even feeling too embarrassed to say he was Fu Ke's friend.

Fu Ke, unable to delay any longer due to the sect’s rules that prevented him from bringing Yu Fujing onto the island, settled Yu Fujing on Jade Island, assuring him to rest easy and not rush back to Baoping Continent. After Fu Ke left, Yu Fujing felt both fortunate and regretful. He was thankful that Fu Ke had not explicitly stated anything. The next day, however, the law-keeper cultivator from Jade Island’s ancestral hall personally came to inquire if he wished to become an inner disciple of Jade Island. Though not a direct descendant of the ancestral hall, this alone made Yu Fujing tearfully grateful. 

While Jade Island was a vassal of the Rain Dragon Sect, it was still guarded by a Nascent Soul old immortal! What kind of celestial mansion would that be in his hometown of Baoping Continent?

Moreover, the law-keeper cultivator was a Golden Core Earth Immortal. For someone like Yu Fujing, a fifth realm wild cultivator, even dreaming of the slightest smile or polite word from a Golden Core Earth Immortal was beyond what he could hope for.

After that, Yu Fujing began his stable practice on Jade Island as a registered cultivator, receiving the celestial master’s techniques. Though his aptitude was average and his progress was slow, he still received special attention from the ancestral hall cultivators.

Fu Ke’s visit to Jade Island was evidently to see his friend Yu Fujing.

Having already learned the news from his sect, Yu Fujing hurriedly left his dwelling. He thought about the futility of cultivating Qi when there was no extraordinary fate or significant celestial money to invest; just sitting there hoping was akin to waiting for death.

However, Yu Fujing suddenly paused at the door, hesitating for a long time before finally opening it. After a brief wait, he spotted Fu Ke, who was saying farewell to the old ancestor of Jade Island.

Yu Fujing quickened his pace, hoping to at least share a few words with the Nascent Soul immortal. The island’s master, the old Nascent Soul, indeed stopped.

Yu Fujing rushed forward and playfully slapped Fu Ke’s shoulder, jokingly scolding him for forgetting his brothers now that he had a wife. Fu Ke smiled and said nothing.

Yu Fujing then respectfully bowed to the old ancestor.

The old Nascent Soul exchanged a few courteous words with Yu Fujing, mostly about diligent cultivation and the hope for the Dao, while Yu Fujing listened intently. After the old Nascent Soul departed with a smile, Yu Fujing pulled Fu Ke into his modest private residence—though small, it was still a private dwelling. Jade Island had strict rules, and aside from the promising young talents destined to become pillars of the ancestral hall, Yu Fujing was the only fifth realm cultivator with a private residence.

Yu Fujing invited Fu Ke to drink.

Fu Ke took out three jugs of celestial wine brewed by the Rain Dragon Sect, giving one to Yu Fujing and keeping one for himself while leaving the last one for his master. Fu Ke smiled, saying his master loved good wine and that he would bring some back for him later.

Yu Fujing gave a thumbs up, “So righteous.”

Fu Ke grinned, “Wine is fine to drink, but remember not to get drunk; this wine is potent. If you like it, I’ll make sure to have someone deliver it to Jade Island even if I can’t come myself.”

Yu Fujing teased, “Isn’t that a bit lofty? Fu Ke, have you looked down on your fifth realm friend since becoming an Earth Immortal?”

Fu Ke sighed, “What nonsense! I’m just at a small bottleneck and need to enter seclusion for a while; I can’t get away.”

Yu Fujing took a sip of wine and propped his foot up on a chair, looking outside, sighing, “I never would have thought I’d be sitting here with you drinking this ridiculously expensive celestial wine.”

Fu Ke chuckled, “Such is the unpredictability of the Dao. Cheers!”

Yu Fujing drank quickly, and Fu Ke couldn’t stop him.

While Yu Fujing had once been filled with gratitude for Fu Ke, as Fu Ke climbed higher and higher, he came to see Fu Ke as almost perfect, and thus thoughts began to creep in.

There were profits to be made.

Fu Ke had left behind a troublesome past, as if he had never had that mountain-down relationship, soaring to heights and marrying beauties, becoming a direct descendant of the Rain Dragon Sect, seemingly completely forgetting those he had left behind.

Yu Fujing, of course, didn’t dare threaten Fu Ke, who was both a friend and an Earth Immortal.

Thus, during today’s drinking gathering, Yu Fujing spoke casually, almost letting something slip. A seemingly light remark was woven into their reminiscing.

Fu Ke set down the wine jug.

Yu Fujing slapped himself, instantly regretting, “What am I saying! Fu Ke, don’t think too much about it; I swear I won’t mention this to outsiders!”

Fu Ke chuckled.

Then, Yu Fujing fell silent.

Fu Ke picked up the wine jug and continued to drink slowly, staring at the door, muttering to himself, “Yu Fujing, you come looking for me to gamble on wealth, and I leave the Rain Dragon Sect to row a boat to see you, giving you a fortune you’ve never dared to dream of. If you behave well and know your place, perhaps there will still be some chance for you to become my right-hand man. After all, realm is realm, and intellect is intellect. I’ve always known you are a clever man; if you choose to squander your fortune, then I can’t be blamed for severing our brotherly ties.”

“You are merely a fifth realm cultivator who has never seen the view from the mountain peak, while I have seen it with my own eyes. Face and reputation are things I desire as long as it’s possible. But when two harms must be weighed, I find you to be an insatiable wolf. Rather than keep you around to bring misfortune upon myself, it’s better to resolve things early. The reason I keep you here is to remind myself, every time I see you, of my humble beginnings, to cherish every celestial coin I possess and every flattering smile I receive, as well as every word of praise.”

Fu Ke’s expression fell, “Do you really think your death is such a big deal? I won’t do anything; once I step out, I won’t say a word, and just like that, I’ll return to the Rain Dragon Sect. Everything on Jade Island will be handled seamlessly, and I’ll genuinely thank you for helping Jade Island connect with me through this hidden relationship. That’s what a wise man should do. Yu Fujing, you still lack vision; it’s no wonder you’re courting death.”

Fu Ke stood up, wiped his hands, and glanced back at Yu Fujing’s lifeless form, “I told you, drink well and say less nonsense, but you didn’t listen.”

Fu Ke truly left Jade Island, heading toward the mountain gate, then summoned his talisman boat to return to the Rain Dragon Sect.

As Fu Ke lay on the talisman boat with his eyes closed, he pondered future matters—like first becoming a Nascent Soul, then advancing to the upper five realms, eventually becoming the sect leader of the Rain Dragon Sect, claiming one of the four private residences of the Hanging Mountain, the Water Crystal Palace, as his private property, returning home in finery to that little corner of Baoping Continent, collecting those celestial maidens he had once regarded as divine, getting a few to serve him tea and water, like the one from Zhengyang Mountain, Su Jia, oh no, she had already fallen from the heights of the phoenix to become a muddy chicken, so she could be disregarded. Despite her beauty, what use was that? The world had no shortage of beautiful women.

What it lacked was someone like Fu Ke, who was destined to reach the peak.

Fu Ke raised a hand, gently clenched his fist, smiling, “I wonder if the female sword immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall might have a chance to be hidden away in my golden house; I’ve heard that Luo Zhenyi and Situ Weiran are both young, beautiful, capable fighters—prime candidates to become female sword immortals! If the Sword Qi Great Wall were to collapse, might I seize this opportunity?”

As for what would happen if the Sword Qi Great Wall fell into chaos, there would be those high and mighty Confucian sages to clean up the mess; what need would there be for Fu Ke and the Rain Dragon Sect to lend a hand?

Not to mention the Central Divine Continent; even closer, there was the current Confucian sage, Chen Chunan, standing on the city wall.

Moreover, this was merely a contingency. The sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall were truly interesting; in the world of righteousness, every Qi refiner feared death, yet those at the Sword Qi Great Wall seemed to fear life, engaging in acts that sought death.

With this thought, Fu Ke opened his eyes and silently reflected, “It’s a pity the beasts in the Savage World are too useless.”

A bird flew past the talisman boat, and Fu Ke glanced at it, laughing heartily.

The poets say that the rower and the waterbird share a dream.

We, the celestial guests, should share our dreams with the flying birds amid the white clouds.

Luhua Island could only be a neighbor to the Rain Dragon Sect, known for its strong-handed actions, not a vassal. Without some skill, that would be impossible.

In the last thousand years, the Rain Dragon Sect had indeed suffered losses at the hands of that sword immortal, but as for the other passing cultivators, even Earth Immortals, and those of the upper five realms, they had all been dealt with by the Rain Dragon Sect without protest. In any case, the outcomes were generally not good. Moreover, the Rain Dragon Sect was too far from the mainland, isolated in the sea, and far from the emperor’s reach, making its rules more effective than those of the Confucian Academy.

Luhua Island not being swallowed by the Rain Dragon Sect wasn’t due to the strength of its own cultivators. Rather, Luhua Island had an ancient ruin known as the “Creation Cave,” said to be guarded by an unknown Daoist high immortal who monopolized fortune, forbidding others from touching it. However, regarding this old legend, even the highest-ranking cultivators of Luhua Island could no longer ascertain its truth, as it was far too ancient. Those brave enough to explore the place never returned, gradually extinguishing such thoughts. Celestial opportunities might be precious, but one couldn’t risk their life for them. Besides, Luhua Island harbored no ambitions, and the Rain Dragon Sect had not swallowed this place, which said enough.

Luhua Island was only a distant neighbor of the most southwestern vassal island of the Rain Dragon Sect.

The cultivators of Luhua Island were numerous, but their wealth was limited, which could be blamed on the unwillingness of the Tongye Continent to deal with other continents. They were very reluctant to establish any cross-regional ferries. Although the route from Tongye Continent to Hanging Mountain was fraught with dangers compared to those of Laolong City, the major sects of Tongye and Yuguizong were capable of developing routes, which wouldn’t be too difficult or lose money. However, the celestial forces in Tongye Continent were primarily gigantic beings, renowned for their ease of life in the vast world of righteousness. Unlike other continents, where celestial mansions and masters could be found in almost every nation and region, it was different.

As the head of the Jiang family put it, “I could sneeze or pass gas and still make money. Why would I bother running to Hanging Mountain for a few coins?”

“You can insult me, Jiang Shangzhen, for being lowly, but you absolutely cannot insult my ability to make money. Whoever dares behave heroically, I'll bury them with money.”

But if Tongye Continent truly established a few cross-regional ferries and selected a transfer dock, Luhua Island would be the first choice.

Luhua Island was too isolated from the world; everyone simply followed their paths in cultivation. As for making money, there were those pearl-collecting cultivators who went to sea.

Thus, the cultivators here were more interested in gathering tales of extraordinary people from outside to share, otherwise, who were they practicing for? Luhua Island could not compare to the Rain Dragon Sect, which had never produced any astonishingly talented cultivators.

Today, there was a dispute that was hardly surprising.

Two groups of cultivators with average aptitude, boys and girls, found themselves divided into two factions.

Originally, they were arguing about whether a talented sword cultivator from the Rain Dragon Sect could rival the top genius of the Sword Qi Great Wall. The so-called genius was one who became a Golden Core sword cultivator before the age of one hundred.

Some insisted it was incomparable, while others claimed they were certainly not far off.

Before they knew it, the argument had shifted to just what kind of place the Sword Qi Great Wall was.

Some claimed that every hero and bold figure could be found there, insisting it was the densest gathering of sword immortals in the world. It was said that merely going out to buy a jug of wine would allow one to encounter many such figures. A place like that—if one never went to experience it, nor enjoyed a drink there, it would be a shame for their identity as a cultivator.

The essence of argument since ancient times is to declare everything the other side says wrong, even if it is right, and so soon someone said that sword cultivators from the Sword Qi Great Wall were all foolish, never doing business. Almost every cross-regional ferry was able to make a fortune, and it was exactly because of the Rain Dragon Sect that it had become so wealthy, indirectly profiting from the Sword Qi Great Wall.

A young man laughed coldly, declaring that when he grew up, he too would go to Hanging Mountain to earn the Sword Qi Great Wall’s celestial money, taking all those so-called sword immortals’ money without leaving a single snowflake coin behind.

A passing old cultivator cursed them for being nothing but bickering children and told them to go practice instead.

The younger generation not only ignored his advice, but they insisted on having the esteemed elder judge their argument.

The old man was known for his countless stories on Luhua Island, and he had no air about him, able to chat with anyone. When in a good mood, he would even treat them to wine, regardless of whether they were mere kids.

The elder was a Golden Core Earth Immortal, with a seat in the ancestral hall and a lavish private residence on the island. He had traveled far and wide, visiting places like the Southern Posa Continent, Baoping Continent’s Laolong City, and the Northern Julu Continent’s Bone Marsh, seeing much and experiencing a variety of events.

Thus, the younger generations loved to listen to the old immortal’s jokes.

When he was tipsy, he could recount all sorts of fascinating tales from around the vast world of righteousness. Whether it was about customs on the Day of Beginning of Spring or how the courtesans in brothels would invite boys in open-crotch pants to dance to ward off evil, or how the Confucian Academy did not endorse the burning of paper money, while both Buddhism and Daoism also did not recognize this custom as their own, leading to years of uproar, leaving the children of Luhua Island dreaming of adventures.

The elder loved to tell stories about Jiang Shangzhen, often saying he shared a table with the renowned figure from Tongye Continent.

No one believed him, of course.

Today, the old man was dragged by the younger generation and wouldn’t be allowed to leave until he mixed in some praise for the talented sword cultivator of the Rain Dragon Sect and some good words about the Sword Qi Great Wall, finally granting him a moment of peace.

The elder walked down the mountain along a wide path, ancient trees towering on both sides, lush greenery surrounding him. The elder, with nothing to do, fell back into his old habit, quietly counting the steps until he reached the edge of Luhua Island, where the waves rolled endlessly. Feeling quite well, the elder had made quite a bit of money at Miliu Cliff in recent years, earning a good sum of small summer coins. What’s more, he felt that the money was earned with a clear conscience. Occasionally, in the dead of night, he would even consider sending some celestial coins to the Sword Qi Great Wall, but just thinking about such a joke made him laugh heartily. What was he, Song Sui, to send money to the Sword Qi Great Wall? Did he know any sword immortals?

The old man scratched his head, feeling a bit melancholy. If he could truly say he had shared a drink with Jiang Shangzhen, how good that would be.

In the future, when boasting to the kids, he could thump his chest with pride.

The old man looked back up the mountain, hoping for a life of peace, with only minor troubles and no great worries.

The old man regained his senses, chuckling to himself, shaking his head before climbing back up the mountain, counting the steps once more, his pace leisurely and unhurried.

He nostalgically recalled the days when a rosy-cheeked girl would walk beside him. He wasn’t handsome, and she wasn’t particularly beautiful either, but they liked each other. As cultivators, a few steps were nothing, and they would naturally not tire. Yet she always insisted on taking breaks, and he would sit with her on the steps, gazing into the distance, watching the moon rise over the sea.

The old man halted his steps and turned to gaze at the moon on the sea.

The people of today have seen the moons of the past; the current moon has cast its light on old friends—everyone has seen it.

Suddenly, the old man pressed his hand to his forehead, stabilizing his mind, opening his eyes wide, concentrating on the moonlight on the steps, feeling something strange for just a moment. But as he looked around, the world was silent, with only the occasional whisper of pine flowers falling to the ground.

The old man’s mind was sharp. Although he had never truly shared a drink with Jiang Shangzhen, having traveled across continents and witnessed extraordinary beings, he did not think this was trivial. Immediately, he summoned the wind and flew to the top of an ancient pine, still finding no trace. The protective mountain formation showed no signs of disturbance. Finally, he gazed toward a solitary peak marked as a forbidden zone on Luhua Island—the once-famous Creation Cave, which had gradually faded into obscurity.

The old man self-deprecatingly said, “If the old immortal inside truly emerges, that would be a good thing.”

The vast sea stretched beyond, even broader than the nine continents. Throughout history, many immortals quietly departed the land to choose a location of good fortune in the sea, hiding away to cultivate, either breaking through in silence or quietly dissipating, all without anyone knowing.

**(End of Chapter)**

 ### Chapter 743: Gentle Winds and Soft Moons (Part Two)

The Jade Seal Sect (Yugui Zong) is located at the southern tip of the Tung Leaf Continent (Tongye Zhou). The peaks rise in layers, deep and serene, infused with abundant spiritual energy, making it an exceptional place for cultivation. Among its many mountains, the Divine Seal Peak (Shenzhuan Feng) is renowned for its towering beauty that seems to touch the heavens. 

With the rise of many talented individuals in the Jade Seal Sect, there has never been a worry about a lack of successors. The only concern has been how the ancestral hall can avoid favoritism among generations of geniuses. From the founding ancestor, Xun Yuan, to the relatively younger Jiang Shangzhen, and finally to the most outstanding talent of the current generation, Wei Ying, the sect has always been rich in exceptional individuals. 

There are also other talented cultivators of similar standing to Jiang Shangzhen and Wei Ying. If not for the overshadowing brilliance of these two, their own fame would have flourished significantly in other sects. 

On a mountain called Nine Strategies Peak (Jiu Yi Feng), the pavilions stretch continuously, surrounded by ethereal mist and celestial birds soaring above, it is an enchanting place that rivals even small heavenly realms. This peak, which draws spiritual energy from all the mountains and streams outside the Jade Seal Sect’s ancestral mountain, is particularly special. Throughout its history, every sect leader has cultivated here, including Xun Yuan, who only moved out after becoming sect leader.

It is said that when Jiang Shangzhen was at the brink of attaining the Golden Core realm, he found Nine Strategies Peak within reach, only to realize that he could not settle there, as if a cooked duck had suddenly flown away, leaving him with nothing but the frustration of being unable to claim it. Frustrated, he left Tung Leaf Continent grandly, heading directly to North Julu Continent (Beijulu Zhou) to stir up trouble, tarnishing the reputation of the Jade Seal Sect throughout that region.

After Xun Yuan moved out of Nine Strategies Peak and before Wei Ying ascended, the peak remained unclaimed due to Jiang Shangzhen's inability to become its master. Everyone understood that whoever could achieve the Golden Core here would undoubtedly be the next sect leader.

Wei Ying was brought to the Jade Seal Sect while still in swaddling clothes. By the time he was nineteen, he moved to Nine Strategies Peak amidst much expectation and support. From then on, he often found himself standing atop Nine Strategies Peak, gazing up at Divine Seal Peak, never hiding the admiration in his eyes. 

After all, this would be his next place of cultivation. As long as he refrained from unnecessary actions and focused on his training, it would eventually belong to him. There was no need for secrecy.

Today, Wei Ying stood on the corridor of a rooftop, looking up at a specific spot on Divine Seal Peak, which felt different from earlier. Beside him stood a tall young man, unlike his father. This young man had an ordinary appearance, with light brows and a somewhat effeminate name, yet he possessed narrow, elongated eyes, giving him a semblance of his father.

Jiang Heng.

However, in the ancestral records of the Jade Seal Sect and the Jiang family genealogy, he was officially listed as Jiang Beihai. Yet, those familiar with him still preferred to call him Jiang Heng. 

Whether one could refer to Jiang Beihai as Jiang Heng was a subtle sign of success among the younger generation of the Jade Seal Sect. After all, both names belonged to the only son of Jiang Shangzhen. If Wei Ying was the indisputable next sect leader of the Jade Seal Sect, then Jiang Heng, while not as prominent, should still inherit the next fortune of the cloud cave.

However, in recent years, there had been whispers that Jiang Shangzhen, under the alias Zhou Fei, had fathered another son. This news had troubled Jiang Heng for quite some time, but he could only endure it in silence, even suppressing any thoughts of sending someone to infiltrate the cloud cave and eliminate that brother. 

The reason was simple: Jiang Heng feared his father, Jiang Shangzhen, more than anyone else.

The terrifying nature of Jiang Shangzhen was well-known among the people of Tung Leaf Continent. But Jiang Heng's fear of his father ran deeper. Jiang Heng's mother, a direct descendant of a highly esteemed ancestor of the Jade Seal Sect, had always known that Jiang Shangzhen had never truly loved her. 

Yet, when alone with young Jiang Heng, she would still show sincere happiness, sharing her heartfelt thoughts with him, telling her child how grateful she was just to be by his father's side. 

As she lay on the brink of death, Jiang Shangzhen sat beside her sickbed, his expression gentle as he held the frail woman's hand without saying a word. Instead, it was Jiang Heng's mother who tightly grasped Jiang Shangzhen's hand, smiling as she spoke words that left young Jiang Heng feeling as if he had fallen into an icy abyss, “That woman, I secretly met her once. She’s already gray-haired, and even when young, she wasn't particularly beautiful. Jiang Heng, with your name, I guessed your thoughts and fulfilled your wish. Yet, you didn’t even say thank you. I’ve spent all these years only feeling angry about this.” 

Jiang Shangzhen gently patted her hand, smiling softly as he said, “Did you know, while you were secretly watching her, I was secretly watching you? You looked so innocent and lovable, like you had won at everything back then. You were incredibly beautiful.” 

She nodded and smiled before leaving this world.

Jiang Heng, sitting on a chair by the bedside, wept quietly.

Then Jiang Shangzhen turned his head and laughed, “Crying your mother to death, and now you want to cry your father to death? That’s not what a filial son does.” 

The child was so frightened that he immediately sat up straight and remained still.

Jiang Shangzhen then said something that Jiang Heng could only remember but never understood, “If you can’t be yourself, you first have to learn to deceive yourself. Being Jiang Shangzhen's son isn’t easy.” 

Despite the deep-rooted fear of his father, Jiang Heng lived quite well in the Jade Seal Sect. In fact, apart from Wei Ying, there were only one or two others who could match the young master Jiang Heng.

At this moment, Jiang Heng followed Wei Ying's gaze towards Divine Seal Peak and asked with a smile, “Are you still so fixated on that Sui girl?”

Wei Ying shook his head, “It’s not about being fixated; I just can’t forget her. What angers me most is that she would rather die than come visit Nine Strategies Peak.” 

Leaning against the railing, Wei Ying stopped looking at Divine Seal Peak and turned to Jiang Heng, smiling softly, “Women’s thoughts, Jiang Uncle knows best.” 

Jiang Heng leaned on the railing, unwilling to discuss this topic. His name had become a source of amusement for many elders in the Jade Seal Sect. 

Adding to his woes was the matter of the cloud cave, where those with seats in the ancestral hall would never outsmart his father. So they took pleasure in venting their frustrations on Jiang Heng. 

After all, those elders understood clearly that Jiang Shangzhen had never given Jiang Heng any hope, let alone expectations.

Jiang Heng changed the subject, “Looking at the aura from Divine Seal Peak, the old sect leader is surely on the verge of breaking into the Ascension realm.” 

Wei Ying nodded with a smile, “So my desire to become the next sect leader feels even more distant. Thankfully, only one sect leader can exist in the Jade Seal Sect, but Tung Leaf Continent can have two to three Ascended beings. I wonder which fortunate soul will become the third. I think that Huang Ting from Taiping Mountain and that child who left the Fuji Sect for the academy have a relatively higher chance.” 

Jiang Heng genuinely admired Wei Ying for his ability to talk about anything, even daring to speak freely. This was not something that developed only after moving into Nine Strategies Peak; he had been like this since the beginning of his cultivation. 

Jiang Shangzhen never hid his fondness for Wei Ying, claiming his own son wasn't much of a son at all, but thankfully there was a Wei Ying who resembled him living on Nine Strategies Peak.

Currently, the Jade Seal Sect was flourishing and not limited to just one continent. 

Not only was the old sect leader Xun Yuan about to ascend to the Ascension realm, but the lower sect, the True Realm Sect, had already firmly established itself in the Baping Continent (Baoping Zhou). 

Also, the Tung Leaf Sect, Taiping Mountain, and Fuji Sect had all suffered significant losses, and within the sect, the talk had begun that as long as the Jade Seal Sect desired to move northward, even if the three sects formed an alliance, they could not stop us. The entire continent, both above and below the mountains, would belong to us, surpassing even the Great Li Dynasty of the Baping Continent, which claims the entirety of its territory.

The Jade Seal Sect had gone from being the second in Tung Leaf Continent thousands of years ago to becoming the ruling force without any effort, and it seemed that for the next several thousand years, the sect could continue to do nothing and still hold on to its position of power.

It was likely that the old sect leader Xun Yuan could smile in his dreams. 

Indeed, the Tung Leaf Sect had suffered an unimaginable amount of misfortune, and it was not surprising that others would revel in their downfall. 

First, the Ascended Ancestor Du Mao died mysteriously, and not only that, but it also implicated a small heavenly realm. Du Mao couldn’t even leave behind all the fragments of his Glazed Golden Body after his death, and with the sword cultivator’s meticulous strikes, the impact was profound, shattering the hearts of almost all the Tung Leaf Sect’s cultivators.

Then came Jiang Shangzhen’s grand banquet on the sea of clouds, right on the edge of the Tung Leaf Sect’s territory. If Du Mao, the founding ancestor, had been alive, he wouldn’t have needed to personally intervene. Jiang Shangzhen would have been forced to retreat in embarrassment.

Afterward, there was a defection from an elder of the fifth realm, who took the sect’s treasures and defected to the Jade Seal Sect. He accompanied Jiang Shangzhen to the Baping Continent to select a location for a lower sect and expand their territory. However, there had been no news of this person in recent years; it was said he had gone into seclusion.

Suddenly, Wei Ying said, “Earlier, we talked about Huang Ting. In my opinion, her fortune is quite unfortunate, being trapped in one continent. If the sword cultivators of Tung Leaf Continent shed their narrow-mindedness and were willing to travel along the Sword Qi Great Wall, even if Tung Leaf Continent cannot become North Julu Continent, they should have already attracted one or two Ascended sword cultivators early on. If I had the final say, starting today, I would send sword cultivators to the Upside-Down Mountain. The deeper the mountain, the heavier the mist; each descent would at least yield some dew, and with the efforts of the ants, the sword path’s fortune in Tung Leaf Continent would accumulate year after year, naturally becoming abundant. Of course, these wandering sword cultivators must remain unaware, because only with sincere hearts can things come to fruition.” 

Wei Ying sighed, “If she stays in the Jade Seal Sect, I would gladly help her compete with Huang Ting in the sword path.” 

Jiang Heng did not know whether the concept of fortune was something Wei Ying had come up with himself or if it was revealed by the old sect leader. However, Jiang Heng would not ask. Knowing the matter, what was the point of asking further?

As for how that mysterious woman came to the Jade Seal Sect and why Wei Ying held her in such high regard, Jiang Heng did not care. 

Finally, Wei Ying slowly said, “After the worst comes the best; when the moon is full, it begins to wane. Don’t overlook that.” 

Jiang Heng looked into the distance, lazily smiling, “I’m just someone who eats and waits to die. All the grand endeavors are left to you, Brother Ying.” 

“An old horse at the edge of the field, unties the reins and wishes to sleep; it has no strength left to withstand the whip.” 

Wei Ying chuckled, straining his eyes to look far ahead, “What a gloomy sight, with thousands of graves.” 

Hearing such strange words, Jiang Heng merely registered them subconsciously. 

His thoughts drifted far away, recalling years past when he traveled to Upside-Down Mountain, the Osmanthus Isle, Lady Gui, and the clouds above the Old Dragon City. 

During that trip, Jiang Heng had originally intended to secure the first intercontinental ferry in Tung Leaf Continent as a new source of income for the Jiang family. Though the profits were modest, it would have drawn the attention of that elusive man shrouded in mystery. 

However, nothing went as planned. Not only did that secret endeavor fail, but upon returning from Upside-Down Mountain to the Jade Seal Sect, he was met with the shocking rumor that after his return from a trip, he inexplicably gained a brother?

Today, Jiang Heng returned on the wind from Nine Strategies Peak to his residence, still the old house where his mother had lived. 

Jiang Heng sat on the threshold of a room, turning to look into the empty interior, choking back tears as he murmured, “Mother, Father lied to you. At that time, Father was still in the cloud cave. How could he possibly have seen you? Do you really know...?” 

Finally, Jiang Heng raised his head and whispered, “Mother, you are so intelligent and refined, how could you not know? You’ve always been like that, caring most for that cold-hearted scoundrel. Mother, wait for me. One day, I will make him apologize to you in person. I promise, from that day on, I won’t be Jiang Heng anymore; I will be Jiang Beihai...” 

Suddenly, a familiar voice, which struck fear deep within Jiang Heng, rang out not far away, “Good son, saying such things about your father is quite unfilial; you might just die from it.” 

Jiang Heng tensed up, stiffly turning to see the man with a smiling face. 

That man sighed, “I finally returned home, and I’m met with complaints from my eldest son. If I were truly cold-hearted and heartless, wouldn’t I have been blasted to pieces by your words?” 

Jiang Heng swayed on his feet, pale as a ghost. 

The man looked at Jiang Heng, then nodded with a smile, “You may be a bit foolish; after all, you take after your mother. But at least you’re still a person. Following her is actually a good thing. Foolish people have their own blessings, which is nice. However, family rules still need to be upheld. Today, I won’t hold it against you.
