Growing up, I, as your father, never taught you anything, nor can I scold you for anything. But from now on, remember this: A father may be unkind, but a son must be filial. Strive for brotherly friendship and let no one cause me worry.” 

With his mind in a muddle, Jiang Heng could only nod stiffly. 

Jiang Shangzhen turned and left, clicking his tongue, “How did I end up with such an ugly son? It’s truly distressing to look at you. You’re doing a disservice to your parents. Next time you see me, lower your head when you speak.” 

Only then did Jiang Heng dare to wipe the sweat and tears from his face, feeling as if he had walked through the gates of hell.

The words of that man today, if overheard by outsiders, would likely evoke pity for Jiang Heng’s plight, but in reality, they were far kinder than what he had said in the past.

After Jiang Shangzhen left the residence, he went directly to Divine Seal Peak’s ancestral hall to welcome the old sect leader out of seclusion, who had successfully reached the Ascension realm.

Regardless of his realm or status, Wei Ying should have a place in this ancestral hall, and it would surely not be a lowly one. However, Nine Strategies Peak was too unique, and thus it lacked seating.

The rigid rules passed down by the ancestors left no room for discussion. After all, in the realm of immortals, ancestral laws have always trumped everything.

Upon entering, Jiang Shangzhen, slightly affected by Jiang Heng’s earlier antics, felt his mood improve as he enjoyed the expressions of the old masters who looked as though they had eaten something unpleasant.

He noticed a female cultivator sitting near the entrance, well-preserved and equally beautiful. Jiang Shangzhen immediately moved closer, smiling brightly, “Sister Liu, it’s quite windy here; be careful not to catch a chill. It’s been a few days since we last met, and you look so thin; it pains my heart. Can’t afford to buy meat? Can’t you find me for money? Don’t sit here; come, come, come, sit on my lap.” 

The woman glared at him coldly.

Jiang Shangzhen sighed dramatically, his face full of sorrow, and walked away.

Everyone seated in the ancestral hall knew that she was one of those who wished to skin Jiang Shangzhen alive.

Of course, most of the chair owners felt similarly towards him.

Yet, Jiang Shangzhen continued to live well, wandering around as if he were carrying a dung pit. He was happy, but everyone else found it repulsive.

After Jiang Shangzhen settled down, he leaned back in his chair, exhaling deeply, “It really is more comfortable at home; even squatting feels more at ease.” 

An elder sitting opposite him, responsible for the rules, said coldly, “Jiang Shangzhen, keep your mouth clean!” 

Jiang Shangzhen paused, “Who are you? Are you my father? Who are you to teach me? If I acknowledge you as my father today, will you give me that celestial weapon? I’ll kneel right here and call you father. If we acknowledge each other as father and son, your precious daughter and lovely granddaughter, how would they still like me? It’s a win-win. If I were you, I wouldn’t hesitate to recognize me as your son; you could even consider recognizing me as your father!” 

The elder closed his eyes to meditate. 

It was impossible to openly confront Jiang Shangzhen with violence; shouting wouldn’t work either. 

In fact, they had already faced off once at Jiang’s cloud cave. 

The outcome had not been good for either side.

That time, sect leader Xun Yuan had been extraordinarily furious.

Near the center, a wave rippled, and an old man stepped out; it was Xun Yuan, who had just broken through, smiling, “Alright, in all the ancestral halls of sects in the world, none can match the chaotic atmosphere of our Jade Seal Sect.” 

Jiang Shangzhen widened his eyes, “Old Xun, by the looks of it, you’ve broken through two realms?” 

Since there were no outsiders, Xun Yuan immediately cursed, “Stay away from me.” 

Jiang Shangzhen lifted his backside, the legs of his chair wobbling as he shuffled back. 

Xun Yuan straightened his expression, “Let’s get to business. First, the preparations for the sect ceremony are halted. Second, let’s discuss the candidates for the new sect leader of the Jade Seal Sect. In the vast world, this is not considered a rule nor an exception. So don’t look like you’ve seen a ghost. If you’re warm-hearted, be warm-hearted; if you’re envious, be envious. Just learn from that Wei Ying; there’s nothing to be embarrassed about.” 

Jiang Shangzhen moved his chair back to its original position and said seriously, “I can immediately resign from the position of the True Realm Sect leader and take on a heavier burden. As for Wei Ying, he can take my former position; young people still need more experience.” 

All the elders and high-ranking officials in the ancestral hall thought that either Jiang Shangzhen was Xun Yuan’s illegitimate son or that Xun Yuan had indeed broken through and lost his mind.

Because Xun Yuan nodded, “That’s acceptable.” 

Fortunately, Xun Yuan’s next words were somewhat reassuring. 

The old man turned and fixed his gaze on the now-standing Jiang Shangzhen, speaking solemnly, “Once you take my seat, you won’t just be Jiang Shangzhen, the head of the Jiang family.” 

Jiang Shangzhen promptly sat back down. 

Xun Yuan’s expression darkened, “Stand up! If, back then, you had wanted to go to Nine Strategies Peak and I hadn’t agreed, you’d have to roll to another peak. Today, I want you to be this sect leader; you must accept it and become the leader of the Jade Seal Sect!” 

Jiang Shangzhen slowly stood and bowed, “Jiang Shangzhen finally says these four words: ‘I will obey the law’.” 

Xun Yuan smiled, “Let me sit in this chair for a little while longer.” 

After the old man sat down, he gazed at the clouds and mountains outside the door, suddenly reminded of an ancient poem.

The clouds have no heart as they rise from the ravine; the birds weary from flight know to return. Return, return. The trees are lush, and the spring flows gently, return, return. 

But what truly made the old man remember this poem was not the beautiful words that even the immortals atop the mountains would envy but just the first three words.

“My family is poor.”

If there were a bored immortal who decided to set out from Luohua Island across the sea, they would land near the Fuji Sect. 

The ancestral mountain of the Fuji Sect is called Chui Chang, which is shrouded in clouds all year round. 

In the past, it was as renowned as Taiping Mountain, located in the central part of Tung Leaf Continent, roughly positioned in the west and east, opposite the Tung Leaf Sect and the Jade Seal Sect.

The Fuji Sect excels in “Immortal Questions and Answers, Bestowing Truth to All”, yet even though it’s a Taoist sect, it does not belong to the three veins of the Baiyu Capital in the Qingming World, similar to the Longhu Mountain in the Central Plains or the Daxuandu Temple in the Qingming World.

Before the catastrophic events that almost devastated the entire Tung Leaf Continent, not discussing their true foundations, merely in terms of influence, the Fuji Sect still had the upper hand over Taiping Mountain. The two sects had harbored longstanding grievances. After two great calamities, one severely injuring the Fuji Sect and the other wounding Taiping Mountain, the two sects, having gone through hardships together, naturally set aside their past grievances and became allies, with both sect cultivators heading down the mountain to fight side by side for many years, their relationship greatly improved.

Tonight, a pair of young men and women ascended the long-sealed Fuji Sect. 

Before the sealing, the Fuji Sect had moved the bustling Huan Tian Street down the mountain. This vibrant street had evidently become a place of sorrow for the sect leader, Ji Hai, because every glance would remind him of the companion who had built this street with his own hands. 

On Huan Tian Street, a young man dressed in scholar’s robes bought a few trinkets, avoiding any priced over ten snowflake coins. 

Beside him was an incredibly beautiful swordswoman, but no one dared to cause trouble, and for a simple reason: that sword had the style of Taiping Mountain’s sword. 

And there was only one such stunning Taiping Mountain female immortal: the Yuan Ying sword immortal, Huang Ting, renowned across the continent for her exceptional fortune. 

It’s known that even the likes of He Xiaoliang from the God Gua Sect in the Baping Continent and the current head of the Qingliang Sect in North Julu, had only been referred to as “the second Huang Ting” in terms of fortune.

Beside Huang Ting, the disheveled scholar was none other than Zhong Kui, who had lost his identity as a Confucian gentleman. 

As a steward, Chen Ping’an had learned from Zhong Kui early on. 

Zhong Kui sidled up, smiling, “I’m not quite human or ghost, and though I’ve lost my identity as a Confucian disciple, I still don’t have the standing to learn Ji Hai’s unique techniques. Relying solely on my teacher’s connections might not be enough, but since I’m a close friend of Chen Ping’an, and your relationship with him is good, we’re practically family. You can't not help me out a little.” 

Huang Ting had just returned from her travels in North Julu not long ago. Unable to break through her Yuan Ying bottleneck in one go, she returned to Taiping Mountain and claimed to be in seclusion, but in truth, she was just too lazy to see anyone. 

On her way south, when passing through the Baping Continent, she even made a special trip to the Great Li Dynasty to see that ugly little girl, wondering how her swordsmanship and knife techniques were coming along. To her surprise, the little girl was not on the mountain, but two dubious characters had eagerly tried to keep her there. The older one seemed to want to deceive her into becoming a guardian, while the other was practically drooling, resembling a street rogue. 

Huang Ting had no mood to joke with Zhong Kui. This time coming down the mountain was due to the sect leader pushing her to go, so she had to accompany Zhong Kui to Chui Chang Mountain, thus she spoke seriously, “I have a secret letter from the sect leader that should help. As for the rest, I won’t bother. If Ji Hai doesn’t agree, I can’t help you; you’re on your own.” 

Zhong Kui was filled with worries. 

Huang Ting couldn’t understand why he hadn’t been serious about things earlier, and why he was only taking them seriously upon arriving at Chui Chang Mountain.

Earlier, back in Huan Tian Street at the foot of the mountain, this former Confucian gentleman, Zhong Kui, was haggling fiercely over prices, showing no hint of shame. Huang Ting, who had been through the streets below more often, felt embarrassed in comparison. 

But Zhong Kui had one admirable quality: he could take a joke; even if he rubbed salt in his own wounds, he wouldn’t mind. 

As he tugged at his collar and shook his sleeves, Zhong Kui said, “When a scholar’s interests are compromised, yet he can still maintain a sense of calmness, that’s a small accomplishment in self-cultivation. If you can’t do that, it’s just a matter of pretense. Right now, I’m embodying the true essence of grandeur. Back in the day, that Chen Ping’an kid was absolutely awestruck by my magnificent aura, idolizing me to the point where he wanted to be my disciple. I didn’t agree because I thought he lacked the depth to write poetry.” 

Huang Ting remarked, “I’m not blind; I can see that.” 

Zhong Kui looked westward towards Chui Chang Mountain, which faced the sea. 

He muttered to himself, “I really want to see the Sword Qi Great Wall. But my teacher won’t let me.” 

Huang Ting glanced at Zhong Kui. 

Zhong Kui forced a wry smile, “I’m not you; I’m a sword cultivator, and everything is guided by the heart. But scholars have many rules.” 

Huang Ting laughed, “You’ve lost your title of gentleman and your identity as a Confucian disciple, yet you still cling to your identity as a scholar. Hmm, you really are holding on tightly.” 

Zhong Kui had one wonderful trait: he could take a joke, even when salt was rubbed in his wounds. 

Zhong Kui tugged at his collar, shook his sleeves, and said, “When a scholar’s interests are compromised, yet he can still maintain a sense of calmness, that’s a small accomplishment in self-cultivation. Huang Ting remarked, “I’m not blind; I can see that.” 

Zhong Kui looked westward towards Chui Chang Mountain, which faced the sea.

 ### Chapter 744: Gentle Winds and Soft Moonlight (Part Three)

Ever since Du Mao's rise, the Tongye Sect had never found itself in such a precarious situation. If it weren't for the sect master sacrificing his path to ascendancy and breaking through his bottleneck using unorthodox methods to become a sword cultivator at the Immortal Realm, along with the protective mountain array "Wutong Heavenly Umbrella" still in place, the past few years for Tongye Sect would have been even more unbearable.

The Ancestor of Law, unexpectedly carrying a precious treasure, defected, causing instability within their ranks. The offerings scattered, and despite the vast territory of Tongye Sect still existing, they simply lacked personnel.

It wasn't that Tongye Sect had no potential cultivators; on the contrary, there were many promising seedlings with excellent qualifications. However, most had yet to truly mature.

In the thousands of years prior, Tongye Sect had acted with arrogance, expecting that all their actions were justified. Other immortal forces, from top to bottom, had grown accustomed to it, even going so far as to actively assist Tongye Sect in accumulating resources in exchange for a bit of goodwill—perhaps a local Earth Immortal from Tongye Sect visiting, making an appearance at a mountain ceremony to lend support, or young disciples of Tongye Sect going down the mountain for trials, bringing along their own sect members for some roughhousing. As long as they didn't accidentally break the Bridge of Longevity, it would suffice. In the unfortunate event of a mishap, Tongye Sect would be willing to offer some form of compensation later, thus preserving a semblance of face for those sects. 

During the peak ceremonies, as long as a place was secured, they wouldn't expect to be on the ancestral mountain, just a distant view of the prominent figures of Tongye Sect from another peak would serve as a practical banner of their influence.

Yet, what had once been a familiar state of affairs for both the sect and outsiders had now become one of the most criticized aspects of Tongye Sect. Not only was it criticized, but many underhanded actions had escalated. Some sects further from Tongye but with sufficient depth of cultivation were on the verge of openly undermining Tongye Sect, quickly devouring many of its lower-ranking offerings.

Thus, even though the sect master had ascended to the Immortal Realm, he still felt utterly exhausted. 

The once-subservient mountain deities, previously groveling at their feet, had begun to secretly forge alliances, daring to negotiate with Tongye Sect.

Many of the lower kingdoms that would have once presented their potential disciples to Tongye Sect were now harboring different intentions, opting to divert their paths, bringing their children first to the Fuyi Sect or Taiping Mountain, to see if the immortal masters there would take a liking to them.

In all fairness, Tongye Sect had not been devoid of merit; they had indeed performed many actions that could not be criticized. They had extended kindness time and again, showering blessings like rain that nurtured the land for thousands of miles, and such praise was not merely flattery.

Unfortunately, the current cultivators of Tongye Sect were reluctant to mention these past deeds.

A man in a purple robe stood by a river within the sect's territory, a place that had previously hosted the fleeting presence of sword immortals. 

Initially, he would have been furious at another's sword strike, but as time passed and various unforeseen changes arose—seemingly without warning—he had come to realize that the roots of disaster had already begun to spread.

Tongye Continent had relied too heavily on the cultivation level of the revitalizing ancestor. 

The ancestor had been overly fond of using his prowess to suppress others, leading to a culture of imitation within the sect that permeated both upper and lower ranks.

A stable society, in essence, was not a bad thing; it fostered a competitive spirit, a flourishing of great sects.

Issues arising from outside the mountains could often be resolved by cutting down the problem swiftly. If that failed, the name "Tongye Sect" could be invoked for resolution. If all else failed, they could return to the sect and request the intervention of senior elders—three strikes, and it would rarely go wrong. Those who were uncooperative would lose their heads, while those who were more agreeable would apologize and bow at the mountain gate.

It wasn't that Tongye Continent had been without its unique aspects for thousands of years; rather, these embellishments seemed unable to withstand significant upheaval.

Once the revitalizing ancestor departed, coupled with Du Mao's ruthless actions to obliterate a minor cave heaven for survival, it was not just the ungrateful offerings who felt the strain; even the sect master found himself disheartened.

Even if he switched roles, he believed he would make the same choice as Du Mao.

At that moment, a timid young woman approached him.

The man turned and smiled, asking, “How has his sword heart recovered?”

This acknowledged sword genius of Tongye Sect had received a long sword personally bestowed by Ancestor Du Mao, yet ended up almost shattering his sword heart due to a few casual words.

The young woman, who had only just shed her youthful naivety, replied happily, “Reporting to the sect master, senior brother’s sword heart is nearly restored. Once it is fully recovered, he is hopeful of breaking through immediately.”

Though the man was exhausted and had lost all possibilities for his own path, seeing the young faces of those who would become the pillars of Tongye Sect’s next revival reignited a flicker of hope within him.

He smiled gently, “You all have worked hard these past few years. Many responsibilities that should belong to your seniors have fallen onto your shoulders.”

This girl, once deemed too timid by the Ancestor Hall, had surprisingly become more resilient in this harsh reality, a quality uncommon in the young of Tongye Sect in the past—a result of the sect's previous smooth sailing.

She shook her head vigorously, gathering her courage to declare, “Reporting to the sect master, practicing both cultivation and inner strength is wonderful! It’s not difficult at all, so please don’t worry!”

The purple-robed sword immortal smiled lightly; it was indeed good that she could speak her mind so openly.

As he prepared to leave on his sword, he turned to her and said, “Our Tongye Sect has hope. I believe in you, and you must also believe in yourselves.”

Once the sect master’s figure had faded from view, the young woman sat by the river, lost in thought.

She wondered how that most unreasonable sword immortal would negotiate with the wild world once he reached the Sword Qi Great Wall.

She tossed a small stone into the river, secretly cursing that man.

---

**Baoping Continent, Old Dragon City.**

In the prince’s residence, Song Jixin, also known as Prince Song Mu of the Great Li Dynasty, felt overwhelmed today and sought solace in a quiet corner, lying on a long bench in a corridor.

All sorts of characters from different walks of life were clamoring to enter the prince’s residence. 

Song Jixin felt increasingly that he lacked trustworthy and capable people around him.

As long as someone had a good head on their shoulders and sufficient cultivation, he didn’t mind their background—provided they were chosen by him.

Otherwise, hints from the Fu family, implications from the Jiang family in Yunlin, and the actions of various figures from Zhengyang Mountain and Qingfeng City made Song Jixin feel irritated.

The key was that many qualified individuals who could enter the residence still warranted his attention.

Previously, he hadn’t thought it difficult to speak straightforwardly with people or to converse with ghosts. Now, he didn’t find it too hard, but he felt exhausted.

Ultimately, despite having been a prince for several years, Song Jixin still didn’t feel like a true prince ruling over half a continent.

Even though Nascent Soul cultivators and those at the Fifth Stage treated him with respect, and powerful military officers of the Great Li Dynasty or noble offspring from the south visiting Old Dragon City weighed their words and tones when speaking to him, Song Jixin still felt out of place.

It was like a dream.

The thing that troubled him the most, however, was a seemingly trivial matter.

His long-time maid, Zhi Gui, had begun to feel increasingly distant.

Song Jixin felt he could no longer understand her.

In fact, Zhi Gui hadn’t said anything unreasonable, not even a glance out of place.

Yet, Song Jixin could sense the strange atmosphere between the prince’s residence and the Fu family in Old Dragon City.

He didn’t want to ask her; he wanted her to tell him herself.

Neither of them took the initiative—he didn’t ask, she didn’t say.

Lying on the long bench, Song Jixin resolved to think of nothing and take a short nap, murmuring, “Could this be what they call a superficial harmony with a deep division? No way.”

Suddenly, he sat up straight.

Because a man in a white robe had taken a seat beside him.

His royal uncle, Song Changjing.

And the Ten-Stage Martial Artist, Song Changjing!

Song Changjing, with an indifferent expression, said, “Are you already feeling overwhelmed?”

Song Jixin nodded, “Every matter is time-consuming, and while I can’t guarantee they’re done perfectly, there certainly won’t be any major mistakes. You can rest assured, Uncle. If I deserve rebuke, I will listen intently and correct my mistakes.”

Song Changjing sneered, “If scolding you were effective, I could just berate you to death.”

Song Jixin felt a suffocating pressure, struggling to breathe.

Yet, in reality, Song Changjing had not made any aggressive moves; he merely spoke harshly.

Song Changjing continued, “Ma Ku Xuan from Zhenwu Mountain will be coming here to work in the future.”

Song Jixin’s face darkened.

That troublemaker from Xinghua Alley!

It was rare for him to harbor such animosity toward someone.

Song Changjing stood to leave, glancing at Song Jixin, “I can promise you one thing—if you ever wish to kill Ma Ku Xuan, just let me know. But it’s only one chance. Many requests, I may not agree to, such as killing His Majesty the Emperor and letting you sit on the Dragon Throne. As for whether you want to waste this chance on Ma Ku Xuan, that’s up to you.”

Song Jixin rose as well, “I’ll remember that.”

---

Outside Old Dragon City, the Dragon Ascending Platform by the sea had become a forbidden zone by the order of Prince Song Mu himself.

As such, very few could ascend to enjoy the view. If one were a Qi Cultivator, they needed to be at least at the Nascent Soul stage.

Strangely, the person who visited the platform most often was actually a maid from the prince’s residence.

However, she was of exceptional beauty. It was said she was an ordinary girl, yet she outshone even accomplished female cultivators, exuding an ethereal charm.

Today, she stood alone on the highest point of the Dragon Ascending Platform.

Surveying her surroundings, she detected no prying eyes.

The former Golden Core offering from the Fu family, who had previously resided near the Dragon Ascending Platform, had already moved elsewhere.

Now in Old Dragon City, if even she could not sense any signs, it was certain that no one was employing any extraordinary techniques to observe the mountains and rivers.

Her golden eyes shimmered with fluctuating light.

She wore a dragon robe refined from all the clouds of the Fu family.

In this Baoping Continent, she was not someone who could be easily killed; rather, she could choose to kill whoever she wished!

Yet, that petty degree of cultivation still felt meaningless.

Even with Fan Junmao, who had become the Mountain Lord of Nanyue, she still felt bound.

And Fan Junmao’s rate of breaking through would be swift thereafter.

Zhi Gui lowered her head, a four-legged snake with horns sprouting from its forehead lay obediently at her feet.

She lifted her foot and stomped down heavily; the poor little snake had no courage to flee and could only thrash its tail in a show of helplessness, causing the entire Dragon Ascending Platform to tremble.

“You think wagging your tail will save you? You’re worse off than that mud-legged fool who hides to cry!” 

With added force, she pressed down until the creature sank into the ground.

Zhi Gui withdrew her foot and turned, staring blankly toward the distant southern horizon, a vague sky beyond.

The person who could once control her had died. A truly pathetic death.

The other person, who could also manage her, had never known the truth—how ridiculous.

---

**Under the Night Sky.**

On a vessel from the Fan family in Old Dragon City, on Guihua Island, Madam Gui and her only disciple, Jin Su, sat together in a serene residence.

Jin Su laughed, “Master, it’s not the Mid-Autumn Festival, so why are we eating mooncakes?”

Holding a mooncake in one hand and a delicate gesture in the other, Madam Gui chewed slowly, replying gently, “Just because I want to.”

Jin Su displayed some playful charm only in her master’s presence, stretching her legs, interlocking her fingers, and yawning widely while gazing up at the tall ancient osmanthus tree on the island, which seemed to cradle the moon.

Madam Gui took a gentle bite of the mooncake and teased, “You still prefer Sun Jiashu over Fan Er, don’t you?”

Jin Su’s face flushed slightly as she protested, “Master, that’s quite inappropriate! It’s really out of season!”

Madam Gui chuckled, “Alright, I’ll admit my fault.”

Jin Su continued to gaze at the stunning scenery where the moon and osmanthus tree embraced, casually asking, “Master, I’ve heard every world has its moon. The wild world has three moons, plus so many blessed lands and caves. Which one is the real moon? Or are they all real? Can everyone everywhere look up at the same moon?”

Madam Gui smiled, “Perhaps the true moon resides in one’s heart.”

---

Under the moon, Jin Su felt a sudden wistfulness, “If it could always be like this, that would be wonderful.”

Madam Gui smiled, “The moon waxes and wanes, and ultimately, it’s merely the moon in people’s eyes, not the same in their hearts. There’s never a definite answer as to which one is better.”

The elegant Madam Gui, whose beauty was not absolute but whose demeanor was graceful, looked up at the moon.

Having grown accustomed to observing humanity from the moon, gazing down at it from afar wasn’t too bad either.

The reopening of the shipping routes in Qingluan Kingdom had finally achieved its goal, and all the various departments and officials involved were pleased.

Initially, no one had high hopes for the project; it was difficult and involved offending many people, which could lead to endless troubles. A misstep could leave a stain on one’s official robe that couldn’t be washed away.

At first, only two officials were sent from the Ministry of Revenue and the Ministry of Works, along with the governor of the state where the shipping route was located.

The highest-ranking among them was merely these three.

Additionally, there was Liu Qingfeng, who had been “promoted” from a county magistrate to a shipping assistant official.

However, as unexpected smooth sailing continued, the hats of the officials overseeing the project grew larger, with deputy ministers from the Ministry of Revenue and the Ministry of Works scrambling to leave the capital to endure hardships in that place known for its swarms of insects and leeches. Eventually, the Minister of Works personally led the charge, reportedly taking charge of everything himself. After much hardship, the shipping route finally opened, and upon returning to the capital, the virtuous minister brought back only a single umbrella for the people.

His Majesty the Emperor was delighted, promoting several officials. Those who already held significant ranks received gifts from the emperor.

Of course, except for Liu Qingfeng, who had wisely stayed in the background and hadn’t benefited much. In fact, the three officials who had initially worked alongside him felt somewhat awkward. However, after spending a long time together with Liu Qingfeng, they ultimately found some leftover flavor in their interactions and didn’t mention anything untoward in their reports. As for why Liu Qingfeng acted this way, even after the three were promoted, they still couldn’t figure it out.

Logically speaking, an official who had been excluded from the family tree and whose reputation had sunk to the bottom should have gained something for their concrete contributions. Why would they refuse what should be theirs? Most people would clamor for what they didn’t deserve. Yet, Liu Qingfeng, who seemed to have become as thin as a peasant after the ordeal, didn't seem to care. Moreover, regarding the shipping matter, he was the sole mastermind behind every detail and trend, yet he ended up being the one who gained the least in terms of rank, merely being transferred from a shipping assistant official to a county governor’s assistant.

Today, Liu Qingfeng was on his way to a remote county in the Qingluan Kingdom for his new appointment, riding in a horse-drawn carriage driven by Wang Yifu, a former county constable.

Liu Su, who had been Liu Qingfeng’s steward since childhood, sat beside the burly man, while the master sat in the back of the carriage reading. The bumpy road was taxing on the eyes, but Liu Su couldn’t help but lift the curtain to remind his master. However, Liu Qingfeng always said he would only read for a while, and eventually, Liu Su gave up.

Throughout the journey, his master didn’t read any sage texts but instead flipped through and organized all the official routes of Qingluan Kingdom, even collecting a large stack of geographical maps. He would also extract all records related to roads from the messy local chronicles, tracing and recording everything, regardless of whether the roads were still in use or had been abandoned.

Liu Su felt he would probably never understand what his master was thinking.

Liu Su had a good relationship with Wang Yifu, both having once served as influential county constables, yet he was still willing to accompany his master to face the hardships of the shipping canal, not gaining any promotions but valuing loyalty.

Thus, Liu Su still preferred to call Wang Yifu “County Constable Wang.”

Wang Yifu didn’t comment on it.

Liu Su, who had been Liu Qingfeng’s steward since he left Shiziyuan, had traveled around for studies, then rushed to the capital for exams, and eventually arrived at the county office.

Now still in his youth, though he was no longer as young as before.

The boy felt a bit melancholic today, particularly because his master, still quite young and far from forty, had already begun to show signs of gray.

What saddened Liu Su even more was that his master’s current appearance bore little resemblance to the elegant scholar of years past.

At dusk, the carriage arrived at a relay station. After submitting the official documents, the three of them rested there for the night. The station's clerks failed to recognize the Liu family man as an official. Instead, it was the quiet carriage driver who seemed more official.

Feeling that Liu Qingfeng’s status was neither too high nor too low, the station provided two rooms for them, neither too good nor too bad.

After dinner, Liu Qingfeng began to light a lamp to read, taking out ink and brushes.

Wang Yifu sat beside him, smiling, “Liu, no matter what, even if it’s just to protect your eyes while reading, you should give cultivation a try. You don’t need to save this little bit of celestial currency for the Great Li; after all, the Great Li court will only earn more.”

Liu Qingfeng put down his book, shaking his head, “Let’s skip it. I know my own aptitude for cultivation.”

This was the second time Wang Yifu had said this, and since Liu Qingfeng still refused, Wang Yifu didn’t push it further.

Liu Qingfeng rarely opened the book but, unable to resist the urge to keep reading, eventually closed it, wiping his brow. “How about a drink?”

Wang Yifu was pleasantly surprised, laughing, “In terms of knowledge and governance, a hundred of me wouldn’t compare to one Liu. But when it comes to drinking, it’s the other way around.”

Liu Qingfeng smiled ruefully, “You’re already cursing before drinking.”

Wang Yifu was once a pivotal general from the furthest north of the Baoping Continent, a pillar of the nation.

The Great Li Dynasty had initially only been a vassal of the Lu Dynasty!

Liu Su brought over a bowl of cheap local wine, which was affordable and not too bad in taste.

Liu Su poured wine for both, then looked at the two masters sitting still, puzzled, “Aren’t we drinking? There are no side dishes unless I dare to call on those officials at the relay station who look at me askance.”

Liu Qingfeng laughed, “True hospitality means not seating anyone until the host arrives. If you don’t sit down, neither Wang nor I would dare touch our bowls.”

Liu Su laughed heartily and plopped down. 

His master had a surprisingly entertaining side when it came to jokes.

Unfortunately, such moments were rare.

Liu Su had a weak constitution regarding alcohol and didn’t love drinking, so he had to keep an eye on his master. If Wang Yifu pressured him to drink too much, Liu Su would have to intervene.

Fortunately, Liu Qingfeng drank slowly, and Wang Yifu never insisted, giving the youth some relief.

In his excitement, Liu Su ended up drinking a bit too much.

Wang Yifu put down his bowl, “Liu, I’ve always been curious about your views on the mountains.”

Liu Qingfeng took a sip of wine, slowly replying, “How I view the mountains isn’t very significant. The line between the mountains and the plains isn’t as vast as we imagine. Those below are short-lived, while those above live much longer.”

Wang Yifu asked, “What about the immortal techniques? Don’t you discuss those? Isn’t the difference in lifespan more apparent?”

Liu Qingfeng shook his head and smiled, “I’m a scholar. When confronted with soldiers on the battlefield, if I were struck down by a sword, Wang, do you think the disparity is that great?”

Wang Yifu nodded, “So in your eyes, those who cultivate in the mountains are merely a bit stronger, that’s all?”

Liu Qingfeng ceased drinking, “Rich people in the mountains, especially those who are wealthy enough to rival nations, and the so-called enlightened ones among them, both receive the great blessings of heaven and earth, living without worry and having enough food for several lifetimes. They should think about opening their wallets to give back a little, maintaining reciprocity, and ensuring a steady flow. It’s not that I expect everyone to emulate the moral saints; it’s simply that doing so is a way to send out small coins and welcome in large ones, ultimately a matter of profit and gaining more benefits.”

Liu Qingfeng continued, “Indulgence towards those who break the rules is the greatest harm to those who adhere to them.”

At this point, he turned to the now half-drunken youth, Liu Su, and smiled, “So how do we determine that the rules we set are certainly good and right?”

“Master, you think about it yourself. I don’t want to; I can’t figure it out either,” Liu Su replied, shaking his head and grinning, “But you should think less, otherwise, I’ll be exhausted too.”

Liu Qingfeng waved his hand, exasperated, “Just keep drinking, and don’t think about anything.”

Wang Yifu raised his bowl, toasting Liu Qingfeng.

Liu Qingfeng also lifted his bowl, “I’ll drink within my limits; there’s no need for pleasantries with County Constable Wang.”

Eventually, Liu Su ended up sprawled on the table, sound asleep.

Wang Yifu rarely enjoyed such a long chat with Liu Qingfeng, feeling remarkably at ease.

Liu Qingfeng spoke of what Wang Yifu considered grand matters and achievements with a calm demeanor. However, when discussing a trivial matter Wang had never considered, Liu Qingfeng surprisingly took a deep gulp of wine, truly drowning his sorrows.

“The disappearance of dialects across Baoping Continent is painful. Many larger and smaller dialects, even fragmented literary lines, have a chance for remediation as long as the books are still in circulation. But once those dialects tied to numerous customs vanish, they are gone for good.”

Liu Qingfeng stared blankly out the window.

The window was closed, and the scholar could not see the moonlight outside.

He had no idea if it was brighter than yesterday or dimmer than tomorrow.

---

Xu Yuanxia returned to her hometown and opened a martial arts school. However, this schoolmaster preferred to shut the door and secretly write, only to be found by the servants cleaning the rooms, turning her into a minor joke.

Although the big-bearded man was rather old, his appearance was hardly impressive. However, there were still many young women willing to marry him.

After all, he looked like someone who wasn’t short of money, and the key was that this older man was well-connected, able to chat with local gangs, county officials, and the children of noble families in the same city.

An old bachelor, as long as he had a full wallet, would have a hard time remaining single.

In the deep mountains surrounding the city, a group of celestial beings occupied a secluded mountain peak, which swiftly became shrouded in mist.

Soon, the common folk flocked there, some bowing and praying for a connection with the immortals, while others sought assistance in dispelling disasters, only to be turned away.

Then, one day, a celestial being wandered down the mountain and took a liking to a potential cultivator—a common girl from the county city. She was unwilling at first, intent on marrying her childhood sweetheart and leading a stable life. The young man she fancied happened to be studying martial arts in Xu Yuanxia's school, currently a temporary outer disciple.

What left Xu Yuanxia both amused and exasperated was that she had managed to persuade the group of Qi practitioners using reason and her dagger, successfully convincing them not to resort to force but to conduct a mutually agreeable transaction. Those cultivators, though not highly ranked, were reasonable, and they agreed peacefully.

However, Xu Yuanxia’s school soon attracted a large crowd of relatives from the girl’s parents, causing chaos and despair, particularly an elderly woman who fainted from crying, nearly unable to catch her breath.

Eventually, the girl changed her mind, whether persuaded by her parents or otherwise, and agreed to go to the mountain to practice immortal arts.

Xu Yuanxia found herself caught in the middle.

Yet, having roamed the martial world for a long time, she didn’t feel particularly upset.

That pair had promised each other sweet nothings under the willows, and both seemed to have envisioned a bright future.

One would become a heroic figure in the martial world, opening a school of their own, while the other would learn immortal arts on the mountain, perhaps even supporting one another in the future.

Yet, less than a year later, she came to visit less frequently.

A year later, she completely stopped coming. Even when the young man sought her out, he couldn’t reach the mountain or see her.

The once teetotaling youth started to drink in solitude.

Xu Yuanxia could only sigh.

That girl was indeed born with potential; once following her master and senior brothers, she had already learned to ride the wind above the county city.

Aspiring to explore famous mountains and learn the ways of alchemy.

One time, as the evening glow lit the sky, the young man looked up, tears streaming down his face.

Xu Yuanxia had no way to console him.

That night, Xu Yuanxia lay on the roof, drinking alone.

She found herself missing her two younger friends from the martial world.

Zhang Shanfeng, who was both foolish and clever.

Chen Ping’an, who was eternally deep in thought.

She wondered how much wine she would need to consume the next time they all gathered.

The world felt strange in every corner, and Xu Yuanxia only hoped that her two friends would traverse mountains and rivers without any obstacles.

The big-bearded man tilted his head, stroking his chin, truthfully thinking that after he shaved, he was the most handsome among the three.

---

**In a Lane of Shujian Lake.**

Living door to door were two individuals, one big and one small: a young man and a snot-nosed child squatting in a courtyard, roasting corn, breaking it in half, and the young man handing the child one half.

The child, feeling indignant, refused to take it, “Why should I eat the smaller half, Gu? You’re older; can’t you let me have the bigger one? Do you still want to be my brother-in-law?!”

Gu Can laughed, “In my life, I’ve never eaten the smaller half of anything; it’s always the bigger one. We’re familiar, but I can’t make an exception.”

The child glanced at Gu Can, seeing he wasn’t joking, decided to back down. After all, the corn belonged to Gu Can, and he hadn’t spent a single coin on it. The child nibbling on the corn mumbled, “You’re so rich, yet you still eat roasted corn?”

Gu Can nodded, “Of course I eat. When I’m starving, I’d even eat dirt.”

The child rolled his eyes, “All talk; no girl will like you.”

What the child didn’t know was that this seemingly decent young man, barely good enough for his sister, had once been the notorious Gu Da Demon of Shujian Lake. After a period of quiet, he soon became an influential figure in the area, navigating relationships and connections smoothly, all while remaining behind the scenes.

Once the true Jiang Zhenjun, Liu Zhimao, had completed his retreat, he had fully recognized Gu Can as his only direct disciple, leaving behind the foundational “True Scripture of River Crossing” for him.

Senior sister Tian Hujun had come to see Gu Can as her last lifeline.

The young general who had once been responsible for guarding Yunlou City had since left, but the new Great Li martial general was clearly the friend of Gu Can, who would toast and drink with him, treating him even more respectfully than he did with the previous general. Gu Can understood that this was a friend, yet not quite, but it didn’t really matter.

The new emperor of the Shihou Kingdom, Han Jingling, the youngest ceremonial minister Huang He, and many young “old friends” from Shujian Lake had all come to seek out Gu Can privately.

What mattered most was the unexpected guest who had come knocking.

Gu Can had recognized the visitor’s identity at a glance, even if the other had used some illusions.

Gu Can did not pretend to be ignorant; he directly bowed and greeted, “Greetings, Sect Master Jiang.”

Jiang Shangzhen was quite pleased and not only entered but also drank with Gu Can, creating a private space while treating Gu Can as an insider, freely sharing some shocking words.

He complained that he felt too constrained in his current role, and that the location of Yuguizong’s old sect master was terribly misguided, as any other location would have sufficed. Why did it have to be here, making it impossible for him to sleep?

Gu Can simply listened, holding his cup without drinking.

This gesture was simple: it was Gu Can, situated in Shujian Lake, who would be the person Jiang Shangzhen deemed proper.

As for how Gu Can felt at the moment, what he sought in his heart, or what his future intentions were, none of that was important.

Thus, Jiang Shangzhen merely visited, shared a few drinks, and then left.

Gu Can, regarding these matters, never concealed anything from Zeng Ye and Ma Duyi, but Zeng Ye and Ma Duyi were initially quite worried that Gu Can would revert to the previous Gu Can from Qingxia Island, rather than the one who had traversed thousands of mountains and rivers alongside Chen Ping’an.

Fortunately, Gu Can did not give them any cause for concern. Aside from the endless extraordinary social gatherings and drinking bouts, he still allocated at least six months every year to travel with Zeng Ye and Ma Duyi around the mountains and rivers near Shujian Lake.

During this time, apart from enjoying the scenic landscapes, they also encountered many unexpected conflicts, one of which was a horrific tragedy.

Gu Can did not resort to his previous ways of avoiding trouble or brushing it off with a laugh. This time, he wielded the ordinary sword at his waist and, with a single stroke, killed twelve Qi practitioners, each with a single strike. Among them was even a Dragon Gate cultivator that both Zeng Ye and Ma Duyi greatly feared, yet before Gu Can, who was not even a proper sword cultivator, they couldn’t even muster any counterattack.

That time, even Zeng Ye and Ma Duyi felt a sense of satisfaction; those cultivators deserved to die.

In the end, with his back to them, sword in hand, Gu Can took his time to sheathe his sword, gently shaking off the blood from the blade.

When Gu Can turned around, having already sheathed his sword, he smiled, “Let’s go. The heavens nourish life, and the earth will take care of the dead; no need to worry.”

Now, Gu Can’s holdings were considerable; aside from the Qingxia Island that Liu Zhimao had fought to reclaim, he also owned several other islands, so he rarely returned to this small alley but made it a point to stay a night whenever he returned from his travels or found a moment of leisure.

Today, there was plenty of corn, and although he could only eat half of the smaller one each time, the child still managed to fill his belly.

Gu Can pondered a matter.

He had carefully placed two pieces in Zhengyang Mountain and Qingfeng City, not knowing when he could trigger those lines of connection.

Since there was no rush, he would take it slow.

The child burped in satisfaction and then sat down on the ground, looking at the man named Gu beside him, asking, “Who else is so easy to talk to that you can eat the bigger halves of corn?”

Gu Can glanced at him.

The child suddenly felt a bit scared.

Gu Can laughed and pointed at the child’s face, “Wipe your nose.”

The child immediately sniffed, not even needing to use his sleeve or the back of his hand.

Gu Can thought for a moment and said, “It seems to me that it will be hard for me to return to the way things used to be with that person. But it’s fine; as long as I don’t make any major mistakes—none at all—he will always keep me in mind. How many good friends in this world drift apart without any fuss? It's not that they fall out; they simply grow distant. I feel more at ease now that we’re this way, neither too close nor too far.”

Gu Can looked at the timid child sitting on the ground, smiling, “What do you think, little snot-nosed worm?”

The child, for some reason, felt that the current Gu Can was unrecognizable, so he no longer dared to act as before, saying softly, “Whatever you say is fine. I’m young and don’t understand; I’ll listen to you.”

Gu Can chuckled, “Quite smart, but still not as good as me.”

Now, the child was no longer afraid, rolling his eyes, “I’m smart? Go ask about my teacher’s ruler!”

Gu Can nodded, “That’s quite reasonable.”

Suddenly, Gu Can stood up and told the child, “Go sit in my room for a while, but remember not to rummage through anything.”

The child, confused, still obediently went to Gu Can’s room, standing on tiptoes by the windowsill, worried that Gu Can might have something to do.

So indeed, he was a clever child.

There is a kind of cleverness that is innate.

Gu Can looked toward the door and said, “It’s fine if you won’t come in; I’ll just see you when I go out.”

A timid and weak scholar peeked out, introducing himself, “My name is Liu Chicheng, from Baishan Kingdom, not far from Guanhushu Academy. I was originally traveling to Shujian Lake, but ended up here out of confusion. It’s all a misunderstanding; I’m not a thief, but a genuine scholar with a name!”

Gu Can squinted, clasping his hands in greeting, “Since there’s no need for juniors to go out, please step in, senior.”

The scholar’s demeanor instantly changed, and he strode across the threshold.

“Liu Chicheng” exclaimed in astonishment, “Such a formidable young person!”

Gu Can rose with a smile, “As long as you don’t think, ‘This boy cannot be kept,’ we’re good.”

Upon hearing this, Liu Chicheng burst into laughter, “Interesting, interesting! By the way, I originally came to retrieve the ‘True Scripture of River Crossing’ because I was worried it might fall into the wrong hands. I didn’t expect this to be a heaven-sent opportunity. Little boy, you seem young but have quite a high cultivation level; what’s your name?”

Gu Can, with a strange expression, recalled something, “Senior, are you looking to take on disciples again?”

Liu Chicheng’s expression shifted slightly, feeling a bit awkward, and sighed, “This situation is quite embarrassing.”

Gu Can replied, “I respectfully request you to speak properly and discuss matters thoroughly.”

At this point, Gu Can paused for a moment, locking eyes with the undoubtedly high-ranking “scholar,” no longer displaying any fear, “Otherwise, senior, you might find yourself momentarily pleased but ultimately disappointed.”

Liu Chicheng nodded, “That makes sense.”

Then Liu Chicheng laughed, “You shouldn’t stay in this small pond; you should go to Baidi City in the Central Divine Continent.”

---

The power of the Great Li Dynasty was on the rise.

Recently, in the old Zhongyue territory of Great Li, a continuous light rain fell, becoming quite bothersome.

The original five sacred mountains of Great Li had now been reduced to mere mountain deities, and with the new North Sacred Mountain, they were about to select three peaks as the mountains of the Crown Prince, further worrying certain mountain deities.

Previously, the entire Baoping Continent had not had such concerns. In the mighty Central Divine Continent, history had seen similar actions, but the results had not been significant, even leading to long-lasting repercussions. This endeavor was costly and labor-intensive, often unappreciated, and could easily lead to unforeseen troubles. A slight misstep could leave a stain on one’s official robe that couldn't be washed away.

The reasoning was simple: these subordinate mountain ranges were often extremely far from the grand mountains and were not adjacent to them. The old mountain gods were already nominally dependent on the grand mountain deity, which diminished their stature. Once they became the mountains of the Crown Prince, the regulations and constraints would increase manifold. The mountain deities could come and go as they pleased, and the grand mountain deity could swiftly arrive at their own peak. According to the rites established by the Confucian sages, only the Ministry of Rites could assess and evaluate the merits and demerits of local mountain deities.

Although the Minister of Rites and the deputy ministers were careful not to neglect this matter—after all, it was a national affair regarding worship and war—most of the specific tasks were handled by the small clerks of the shrine, particularly by a low-ranking yet powerful clerk.

Moreover, the mountain deities and the grand mountains could freely seize the mountain and water fortunes from the smaller mountain shrines. Naturally, the grand mountain deities could also reciprocate by offering resources to the Crown Prince’s mountains. However, even if the mountain deity spoke with confidence, could one truly trust their words?

A young woman in a green dress, holding an oil-paper umbrella, walked along the mountain paths.

Her purpose was to negotiate first. If reasoning failed, then they would eat something.

After all, the entire old Zhongyue region was considered the new territory of Longquan Sword Sect.

On her way north, she casually picked up a little girl and brought her along.

The little girl, born of a charming lineage, cheerfully asked, “Sister Xiu, do you know what our paper umbrella is also called?”

Ruan Xiu, distracted, replied, “I don’t know.”

“Flower Holder. Isn’t it vivid and lovely?”

“I suppose so.”

“Sister Xiu, why do you seem so unenergetic?”

“The snacks are finished, and I’m hungry.”

“That makes sense. Sister Xiu, have you heard that eating yangmei without spitting out the seeds and eating watermelon without spitting out the seeds can help stave off hunger even more?”

Ruan Xiu chuckled and patted the little girl’s head, “You’re quite clever.”

The little girl looked at her muddy shoes, feeling annoyed, “It’s frustrating.”

Ruan Xiu nodded, “Yes, it is quite frustrating.”

The little girl stepped further away and, with determination, began stomping heavily in the mud, asking, “Sister Xiu, do you have someone you like?”

Ruan Xiu smiled, narrowing her eyes, “Yes.”

The little girl turned around, raising the umbrella high and examining Ruan Xiu’s profile for a long time before gently saying, “Sister Xiu, you’re so wonderful. Why doesn’t he accompany you when you go out?”

Ruan Xiu pondered for a moment and replied, “He’s always in my heart.”

The little girl pressed her finger to her cheek, making a face, “Sister Xiu, you’re a woman; don’t you feel shy?”

Ruan Xiu began to brush off the questions of the inquisitive little girl, “Oh, that’s how it is.”

---

**In the capital of the Great Sui Dynasty.**

The girl who year after year wore red clothes or padded red jackets wasn’t at the cliffside academy today but had instead gone to a common orange grove on the outskirts of the capital.

Unfortunately, it wasn’t winter yet; otherwise, the oranges hanging from the trees would look like little girls in red dresses.

Li Baoping had come on a whim, recalling a place she had passed earlier and wanting to take a look. After seeing it, she felt satisfied and turned to return.

On the way, she encountered two people who made her even happier.

One was a little black ball carrying a small bamboo box and holding a walking stick.

The other was a fellow who had been nicknamed “Big White Goose” by the little black ball.

Pei Qian sprinted toward Li Baoping.

Li Baoping rubbed Pei Qian’s head, “You’ve grown a bit taller, haven’t you? Take care; don’t turn from a short winter melon into a tall bamboo pole!”

Pei Qian, who had originally been brimming with excitement, immediately grew anxious.

Li Baoping pinched Pei Qian’s cheeks and laughed, “Just teasing you; why is your little head still so slow?”

Pei Qian had a lot to say to her sister Baoping.

Li Baoping motioned for Pei Qian to calm down and turned to ask, “How’s the little master uncle?”

Cui Dongshan nodded with a smile, “The little master uncle, the teacher, and the master will come back.”

Pei Qian angrily retorted, “Don’t put ‘master’ before ‘teacher’!”

Li Baoping watched the two playfully chasing each other and took a deep breath, rubbing her face vigorously. Unfortunately, the little master uncle wasn’t around.

Otherwise, when winter came, it would snow, and they could all have a snowball fight together.

As she grew up, she realized she had seen the least of the little master uncle, especially since she was part of his group.

On the large tree at the peak of the cliff academy, Cui Dongshan, Li Baoping, and Pei Qian climbed up together, feeling quite familiar.

They sat side by side on a branch. Pei Qian wanted to sit in the middle, but Cui Dongshan couldn’t outmaneuver her. Li Baoping yielded, and Pei Qian got her way, feeling overjoyed.

Li Baoping had already listened to Pei Qian’s stories about the mountains and rivers all the way, and they had just finished talking about taking the ferry from Niujiao Mountain to Old Dragon City.

Cui Dongshan leaned back, holding his head with both hands and swinging his legs.

Under the night sky of Great Sui’s capital, the lights shone brightly.

Perhaps this bustling place in the vast world was much like this.

Gentle winds and soft moonlight.

A prosperous and peaceful era.

Cui Dongshan closed his eyes, unwilling to continue watching.

He had seen far too much.

He only wished that the teacher would return home one day in the beautiful season when the grass grows and the warblers sing.

---

**(End of Chapter)**

 ### Chapter 745: The Mutual Questioning of Swords

Chen Ping'an made a solitary journey to the Sword Qi Great Wall, witnessing the legendary Questioning of Swords firsthand.

Who could possibly engage in a sword challenge with the Sword Qi Great Wall?

It was hard to believe that any sects from the vast realm of Haoran would take it seriously; they would likely laugh it off as a joke.

The Questioning of Swords in the Wilds was undeniably real, starting under a night sky where the moon shone dimly.

From his vantage point on the southern battlefield, Chen Ping'an first saw scattered glimmers of sword light flickering into existence. Gradually, more lights appeared, reminiscent of the lanterns he had seen floating downriver during his travels in the Haoran realm, each a tiny beacon of hope gathered together, sparkling like stars, vying for brilliance against the sun and moon.

Ultimately, numerous personal flying swords traced brilliant arcs as they slowly made their way toward the Sword Qi Great Wall, merging into a dazzling river of stars.

From the castle’s heights, it seemed as if an immortal was gazing down from the heavens at the lights of the world below.

If one ignored the enemy lines and simply focused on the breathtaking scene, it was truly magnificent.

As the Hidden Official, Chen Ping'an did not need to draw his sword, nor could he, for he would soon return to the summer palace on the northern side of the wall.

It was not that Miao and Lin Junbi had failed to perform well; it was simply that Chen Ping'an found it hard to relax. This was a kind of obsession that had its pros and cons, and he felt it wasn't the right time for any changes.

Much like the way he had stubbornly sought external help in the past, he needed to adapt gradually.

Standing atop the castle wall near the thatched cottage, Chen Ping'an sighed, “This mutual questioning of swords has never been seen before, nor will it be again.”

The elder sword immortal chuckled, “It's true that there will be no successors, but as for there being no predecessors, that’s debatable. In the past, when mortal sword cultivators raised their swords to question the heavens, swords fell from the sky like a golden rain. That was even more spectacular. Do you know who presided over the formations and maintained order during that time? There were the Greatest Sage, the Dao Ancestor, the Buddha, and nearly half of the ancestors from the Hundred Schools of Thought. Each one selfless, each one honored death.”

Chen Ping'an recalled his earlier journey with Cui Dongshan, where the white-clad youth had rambled on about many strange tales.

Chen Ping'an whispered, “It is said that at that time, there was no concept of the Three Teachings or the Hundred Schools. Each school of thought was just a nascent form, whether we sword cultivators or those practicing Qi, or the dragons of the four seas, all fought side by side as allies. Even the Wilds paused their conflicts with humanity then, not offering help, but neither hindering us.”

Chen Qingdu nodded, a rare look of nostalgia crossing his face. “I, the Dragon Lord, and those long-forgotten sword cultivators of the past, one after another, ascended after drawing their swords.”

Chen Ping'an squatted down, touching the cool surface of the Sword Qi Great Wall, looking up at the southern battlefield. “Elder Sword Immortal, at that time, everyone was struggling for survival; otherwise, they wouldn’t have lived. I don’t mean to belittle your accomplishments, nor would I dare or wish to. Now, after ten thousand years, I have traversed the Three Continents and seen many different worlds; I can say that overall, the Haoran realm is still good, stable. Elder Sword Immortal, you all are like the elders of a large family. You can see clearly the rights and wrongs of our younger generation. In fact, you’ve been quite forgiving. But I still hope you won’t be disappointed; if you lose all hope, we will have far fewer opportunities to realize our mistakes and correct them.”

Chen Qingdu remained silent.

Chen Ping'an hesitated, wanting to say more.

Chen Qingdu smiled, “Since you are now the Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall, you should have the courage to speak frankly.”

Chen Ping'an pressed his palm against the ground and said, “I still believe the world is getting better, step by step. I have faith in that. Elder Sword Immortal, please don’t think that these ten thousand years have been filled with only solitude. Behind you, the Haoran realm has remained stable for ten thousand years, with smoke curling from the kitchens below and the celestial aura lingering above the mountains. Generally, everyone has their hopes and dreams. Even I, as a child, feared nothing and thought I would die, yet I later became an apprentice at the Dragon Kiln and started thinking about earning and saving money, wanting to live well, didn’t I? The thoughts of people over there may be as tangled as wild grass, but they still need soil to take root and sprout, right? As long as there’s soil, countless possibilities will emerge.”

Chen Ping'an looked up and said, “Elder Sword Immortal, do what you think is right. But please don’t be disappointed, don’t be sad, alright?”

The elder squatted down, placing his hand on the young man's head, chuckling, “Young people are just young people, having seen little of the world. Even having experienced the sword technique I taught you, you still don’t know the true heart of a sword cultivator.”

The elder withdrew his hand. “Sword cultivators of my age have all endured and persevered through the deepest despair and the harshest trials. Criminals? In the beginning, who among the mortals on this earth wasn’t a criminal, living day to day? So, there’s no need to speak of great disappointment. Sure, there may be some, but it’s definitely not as thorough as you think. Over the past ten thousand years, what I’ve seen more is a flicker of hope here, a glimmer of hope over there. From the ashes of hope, next year, a spring grass might sprout. While the Sword Qi Great Wall may not hold such a scene, even from the castle wall, I can still catch the scent of spring grass from the Haoran realm every year.”

Chen Ping'an was momentarily stunned and couldn’t help but laugh, “I never expected Elder Sword Immortal to say such things; it’s quite... poetic!”

Chen Qingdu chuckled, “Let me tell you two interesting little things, but remember not to be too eager to reveal heavenly secrets.”

Chen Ping'an straightened, “Elder Sword Immortal, please go ahead.”

However, Chen Qingdu changed his mind, shaking his head, “We’ll talk about it later.”

As Chen Ping'an was about to take his leave, Chen Qingdu suddenly said, “In the Liujin realm, sword cultivators carry two personal flying swords. Reaching the peak of the seventh realm, they are merely pure martial artists. That’s still not enough.”

Chen Ping'an sighed, “Elder Sword Immortal, please don’t be too demanding of me. Among my peers, I’m already quite remarkable. In the path of martial arts, at least I can still catch a glimpse of Cao Ci’s figure. As a lower five realms qi practitioner, to earn a chance for you to draw your sword as the Hidden Official, I wouldn’t dare to claim great merit, but I think my hard work isn’t excessive, right? Moreover, I see no harm in the Liujin realm; it’s about accumulating virtue and luck, and if I’m not careful…”

Chen Qingdu cut off Chen Ping'an’s whimsical thoughts, shaking his head, “You don’t have the fate to comprehend the mysteries of the ‘Preserving People’s Realm’ and shouldn’t expect to ascend to the upper five realms in one fell swoop.”

Chen Ping'an forced a smile, “Elder Sword Immortal, can’t you wait until I reach the fourth realm before saying this?”

Chen Qingdu replied, “Have you thought about who will take the last of the three sword cultivator slots?”

Chen Ping'an shook his head, “I can’t think of anyone at the moment.”

Chen Qingdu waved his hand dismissively, “If you can’t figure out something so trivial, what use is there for you as the Hidden Official? Go to the summer palace and use your brain more. Strive to ascend to the qi practitioner’s cave dwelling realm and the martial artist’s far-traveling realm sooner.”

After bidding farewell, Chen Ping'an asked one matter, which Chen Qingdu agreed to.

It concerned the matter of leaving the castle to kill demons; Chen Qingdu said it was fine. As long as the sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage were willing and it didn’t interfere with important matters, it was acceptable.

As Chen Ping'an summoned his talisman boat, he glanced at the thatched cottage. His senior brother was still in seclusion recovering from injuries; Xiao Shen’s punch had indeed been ruthless. Elder Sword Immortal had said that if it were someone like Yue Qing, they would have been dead by now, and even Lu Zhi and Nalan Shaowei would have fallen in rank.

Just as Chen Ping'an’s talisman boat left the northern castle wall, someone landed on the ferry, riding the wind.

“Are you leaving?” Chen Ping'an asked.

Liu Xianyang nodded, “I expect to depart in a couple of days. The coastal defense of Nanposha Continent has already been put on the agenda, and there are a ton of matters to attend to.”

Chen Ping'an brought up an earlier topic, “Regarding the sword questioning at Zhengyang Mountain, you must wait for me and be extremely careful.”

Liu Xianyang frowned, “If you haven’t seen my sword technique, that’s one thing. But is it really necessary to be so cautious when dealing with a single Zhengyang Mountain?”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “Absolutely. Trust me.”

Liu Xianyang asked, “Is a single Li Tuanjing enough to suppress Zhengyang Mountain for hundreds of years to warrant such seriousness from us?”

Chen Ping'an replied, “Liu Xianyang, the earlier conflict between Fenglei Garden and Zhengyang Mountain is nothing compared to what lies ahead in our questioning of swords at Zhengyang Mountain. Aside from Zhengyang Mountain’s long-hidden foundation, we must also consider the broader context. Both Zhengyang Mountain and the Xu family of Qingfeng City are undoubtedly candidates for sect status in Baoping Continent. In particular, Zhengyang Mountain will likely divide the majority of the swordsmanship fortune of the Zhu Ying Dynasty. This is something even the Longquan Sword Sect cannot achieve. No matter how much the Dali Song Emperor reveres Master Ruan, he absolutely won’t allow the Longquan Sword Sect to dominate; it’s been arranged that the old Zhongyue region is under Longquan’s territory. Aside from Master Ruan’s sect having too few members to grow, this move by the Dali Song Emperor also allows Zhengyang Mountain to seize the opportunity to recruit sword cultivators from the Zhu Ying Dynasty. Once they join a sect, Zhengyang Mountain will be tied to the fate of the Dali Song dynasty. Is this still the same kind of rivalry that Li Tuanjing and the Zhengyang Mountain sword cultivators had in the past?”

Chen Ping'an sighed, shaking his head. “I can’t say more. Just know that Zhengyang Mountain is a crucial part of a significant layout for the Dali Dynasty; it’s indispensable. When the time comes for you and me to question swords, what we’ll truly be confronting is not just the mountain itself but the protective array of Zhengyang Mountain and those elder sword cultivators.”

Liu Xianyang stared blankly at Chen Ping'an.

“Is there something wrong?” Chen Ping'an asked.

Liu Xianyang laughed, “Did you misunderstand? Who said that a question of swords has to be resolved in one go? If I poke them in the backside with my sword today and sense trouble, I can run away, then come back tomorrow and stab them again. Isn’t that also a questioning of swords? Must it be as you say, to kill them in one blow, shattering their sword heart and their spirit in one go? Chen Ping'an, now that you are among the mountain folk, have you become so concerned about face? Have you forgotten how you and I have never been those types of people who care about appearances? I, Liu Xianyang, am not someone whose nature you’re unaware of. My speech may not be in line, but my actions are still reliable.”

Liu Xianyang’s smile faded, “Whatever you do, don’t just think about being flawless; is it really just about being flawless? If you’re mistaken, it’s merely something you didn’t anticipate, yet you’re doing what’s best. I’m the kind of person who is half confused and half clever, not seeking perfection. If I can deal with myself, I can handle opponents too. Life can be lived chaotically or with meticulousness; both ways are valid. You should learn how to make the difficult days more bearable. I’m not saying you’re wrong; I’m just saying that while you may be right more often than I, every person needs to take a break and catch their breath occasionally. This is not something that’s often discussed in books, but I figured it out long ago, just never had the chance to tell you.”

Chen Ping'an stood there for a moment, taken aback.

Liu Xianyang chuckled, “You’re no longer a little snot-nosed kid; you’re still Liu Da Ye after all.”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “I understand.”

Liu Xianyang shook his head, “It’s not just about understanding; you need to remember.”

Chen Ping'an smiled, “You’re in charge.”

The two sat facing each other in the talisman boat.

Life is full of separations.

Only lamenting the spring wind and autumn flowers, the coming and going is truly easy. I wish for the spring flowers and autumn moon to reunite without difficulty.

After a moment of silence, Liu Xianyang blinked, “Is there none?”

Chen Ping'an looked confused.

Liu Xianyang glanced around, ensuring no one was watching, then extended a finger to poke.

Chen Ping'an swiftly slapped Liu Xianyang's hand away and lowered his voice, “Are you trying to get us killed? Don’t involve me!”

Liu Xianyang was taken aback, “We haven’t even held hands yet? I’m not well-read and have been honest since childhood; don’t trick me.”

Chen Ping'an felt like he had been struck by lightning.

Liu Xianyang looked sorrowful, “You’re worse off than I am; it’s not just being single, it’s worse than being single.”

Chen Ping'an laughed, “You should find my future sister-in-law before saying that.”

Liu Xianyang shook his head, leaning back and lying down in the ferry, “It’s hard to find a woman who doesn’t covet my looks.”

The talisman boat hovered at the entrance of the summer palace.

Following the rules of the Hidden Official lineage, no outsiders were allowed to enter the palace without permission.

The two descended gracefully. Chen Ping'an stowed his talisman boat into his sleeve, while Liu Xianyang did not immediately take off.

Standing before Chen Ping'an, Liu Xianyang adjusted his collar, patted his shoulder, and nodded, saying, “I’m leaving. When I’m not around, don’t just take care of others; remember to take care of yourself.”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “You take care too.”

As Liu Xianyang was about to turn, Chen Ping'an tossed him a unique seal, smiling, “This is one of a kind; remember to keep it safe. You might sell it for a fortune someday.”

Liu Xianyang didn’t even glance at it, stowing it away in his sleeve as he rode off into the wind.

Chen Ping'an stood there for a long time, unable to withdraw his gaze.

The doors of the summer palace remained wide open, with no gatekeeper in sight.

Chen Ping'an walked towards the great hall, where Miao was waiting. “Hidden Official, the necessary arrangements have been completed. We just discussed that each time, three people will go to the castle to draw swords. It won’t delay our plans, and observing the battlefield from a distance is not as effective as being there in person to capture the details.”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “Who are the first three?”

Miao stood up, with Mi Yu and Dong Buduo following suit.

Chen Ping'an smiled, “Go ahead, but Mi Sword Immortal should not rush; it should be Deng Liang instead. Remember, do not linger there. After a ten-day period, the next team must include Mi Sword Immortal, Pang Yuanji, and Lin Junbi. Following them will be Song Gaoyuan, Cao Gun, and Xuan Can. Lastly, there will be Gu Jianlong, Wang Xinshui, and Guo Zhujiao, and I might join as well.”

Chen Ping'an had no doubts about Miao and the other three, particularly Miao, who was greatly admired by both Elder Sword Immortal and A Liang as a promising young sword cultivator.

However, he felt some apprehension regarding Luo Zhenyi and the other two, so he placed them behind Deng Liang and Song Gaoyuan. But placing Luo Zhenyi and the others last, even behind Gu Jianlong and his companions, felt excessive. Having Luo Zhenyi and the others together was a kind of supplementary measure.

Therefore, it was reasonable for Luo Zhenyi and the others to harbor some resentment towards him, the Hidden Official, as long as it didn’t interfere with the overall situation, and they did what needed to be done. Chen Ping'an didn’t mind this small grievance. In fact, he felt a strong admiration and longing for these sword cultivators, who were most familiar with the customs of the Wilds, akin to Chen Sanqiu.

However, when it came to specific matters, one should always remain vigilant. Thus, if Luo Zhenyi and the others felt displeased with him, it was of no concern. If he were to be a universally praised good person, he shouldn’t have taken on the role of the Hidden Official.

Miao and the others exited the great hall, soaring away from the summer palace.

Sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage were mostly young yet wise; they all understood that this battle would last a long time, at least three to five years, or even a decade or more—no one could say for sure. The intensity of the conflict would still exceed expectations.

Huang Luan held the fort, with a torrent of magical tools from the demon race and the current Lotus Flower Abbot serving as the backbone of the demon army, leading tens of thousands of demon sword cultivators in questioning swords at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Moreover, after two rounds of battle, millions of demons from the Wilds, under the guidance and coercion of those demon cultivators, would leave their homeland, heading towards the Sword Qi Great Wall. It was said that along the roads leading to the northern battlefield, countless skeletons piled up on either side.

Ants gnawing on an elephant, the demons’ wait-and-see approach has now turned into a burden for the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Once the Questioning of Swords in the Wilds was over, the sword cultivators on the castle wall would have to engage in close combat.

Chen Ping'an didn’t immediately step into the great hall; he took a stroll outside in the plaza.

The Hidden Official lineage had grown accustomed to their Hidden Official acting this way, often found walking alone in the courtyard, drawing circles as he walked.

Pondering some matters, he spoke a few words with the sword cultivators inside the building.

Chen Ping'an recalled a conversation from earlier in the great hall, initiated by Miao and Deng Liang.

Miao had a far-sighted perspective. When the Hidden Official lineage had roughly deduced the next ant siege battle, Miao said that the situation in the Wilds was no simple matter of changing the timing and geography of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Deng Liang made a comparison. He recounted how during his early years as a rogue cultivator traveling in the mountains, he passed by a county town and witnessed a brutal street fight between two sects, resulting in nearly a hundred casualties. The victorious side not only took all the territory but also instilled a great sense of fear in the neighboring counties, quickly infiltrating them. Local officials, the rogue forces, and wealthy merchants all feared those desperate criminals, each with their own schemes, many actively seeking to appease them. Over time, the surrounding county factions lost their momentum and territory was gradually consumed.

At that time, Chen Ping'an had remained silent.

Using this comparison for the Sword Qi Great Wall, the Wilds, and the Haoran realm was somewhat inappropriate. However, the conclusion drawn was correct.

Chen Ping'an had consulted the sages of Confucianism and Buddhism stationed at the castle, and they believed that the Wilds aimed to break through the Sword Qi Great Wall and the Upside-Down Mountain, establishing a foothold in the Haoran realm. They sought to transform the Haoran realm’s territory into that of the Wilds, thereby altering the balance of power between the two realms and seizing advantages—essentially creating opportunities for the peak demons while reducing the need for transcendental forces to dominate. Thus, the more demons that died at the Sword Qi Great Wall, even those who perished in vain, would not die in vain; they would serve a great purpose in the future.

Inside the building, Mi Yu, who had been acting as a gatekeeper, suddenly asked, “Hidden Official, have you become a sword cultivator?”

Chen Ping'an turned to him, asking, “Why do you say that?”

Mi Yu replied, “If you take a chance and consider it a certainty, it often becomes reality.”

Chen Ping'an did not provide an answer, merely smiling, “It’s a pity that Mi Sword Immortal isn’t going to my hometown’s mountain peak to serve as a guardian.”

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 746: The Young Man in the Master Position

A group of over ten people crossed the blazing summer sun of the Sword Qi Great Wall and arrived at the snow-laden slopes of the Inverted Mountain. 

They all cast illusions, choosing the deep midnight of the Inverted Mountain to go directly to one of the four private residences, the Chunfan Pavilion. Among the group were Yan Ming and Nalan Caihuan, the two deities of wealth from the Sword Qi Great Wall. 

Aside from the solitary peak where the Great Heaven Monarch resided, no one noticed the sudden appearance of these crossing dragons. 

The Great Heaven Monarch overlooked the entrance, accompanied by an old master holding a golden dust whisk, who softly inquired, “Master, could this cause any trouble?” 

The Great Heaven Monarch chuckled coldly. “Who would dare to cause trouble? Those merchants blinded by greed? Would they even have the guts?” 

The old master rubbed the golden threads made from the whiskers of a dragon, “If it’s just a show of force, it might not achieve anything.” 

The Great Heaven Monarch turned his gaze to one of the men in the group and nodded. 

The man glanced up at the Great Heaven Monarch at the peak of the solitary mountain and nodded back. 

It seemed the Great Heaven Monarch had only come to meet this person for a moment; after exchanging pleasantries, he turned and left, saying, “After I enter seclusion, you manage things. It’s simple: don’t interfere in anything.”
