Li Cai stood up. “I won’t leave the Upside-down Mountain, but I can send a flying sword message to the Floating Weeds Sword Sect and Taohui Sword Sect, saying that there are some rumors from the Upside-down Mountain suggesting that the two old immortals are colluding with the monsters. By the way, Ku Xia Sword Immortal, aren’t Yu Jianfu and Zhu Mei’s juniors still at the Sword Qi Great Wall? Let them also talk about this matter with the Central Earth Divine Continent so that the two old immortals can clear their names and avoid wronging the good people.”

The Ku Xia sword immortal immediately stood up and said, “No problem. That’s how it should be.” 

Chen Ping’an blinked, filled with confusion, “Do you think I want to become enemies with the mountain behind you? Is it necessary? Not at all; I just don’t like you. Besides a few who are surely doomed, I still have a sense of proportion when I do things. Furthermore, post-event apologies, along with generous compensation, will be provided. In the long run, no one will lose out. Do you really think that I called the sword immortals here just to drink tea with you? Do you think you’re worthy of that?” 

Sun Juyuan also stood up, smiling, “I have some ties with all of you and the sects and ancestors behind you, but there are no personal grievances at all. Therefore, I won’t trouble the Hidden Official with apologies; I can handle that myself.” 

Yan Ming stood up. “As for compensation, my Yan family still has some resources. I, Yan Ming, will handle it until it’s settled.” 

Nalan Caihuan did not move. 

Tonight’s events had exceeded her expectations by far. 

Chen Ping’an shifted his gaze, “Don’t let outsiders see the joke. My face doesn’t matter, but the face of Nalan Shaowei is worth something.” 

Nalan Caihuan had no choice but to slowly stand up. 

Chen Ping’an completely lost his smile, though he still maintained a relaxed posture, his gaze firmly fixed on the business-savvy Yuan Ying sword cultivator. 

Nalan Caihuan steeled herself, remaining silent. 

Chen Ping’an asked, “Is there a mix-up with your seating arrangement? You, Nalan Caihuan, should sit over there.” 

Nalan Caihuan’s eyes flashed with anger, about to speak. 

Sword Immortal Gao Kui stood up, turning to look at Nalan Caihuan. 

Nalan Caihuan had originally been about to call out “Chen Ping’an” but swallowed each word back down one by one. 

This sudden change was increasingly shocking to Wu Qiao and the other “outsiders.” 

This young Hidden Official, who spoke of being small-minded and gaining power, was truly ruthless enough to even kill his own people! 

Whether he was small-minded or not was hard to say. 

This young man’s heart was extremely dark! 

As for that phrase about holding great authority, there was no hint of exaggeration. 

Wu Qiao finally stood up, cupping his fists and saying, “Hidden Official, there’s no need for this. Business is just business; let’s both take a step back and seek a mutually beneficial outcome, aiming for a steady stream of wealth.”

The young Hidden Official merely rested his hand on his chin, gazing out at the heavy snow outside the door. 

Chen Ping’an seemed to be talking to himself, “Do you really believe that the Sword Qi Great Wall has no good relations or ties in the Haoran world? Do you think the Sword Qi Great Wall can exist without these? It’s just that we don’t behave like you, engaging in deceitful dealings, and that became your reason to mistakenly think that sword immortals are brainless. Do you know why you’re still standing here, alive, and not dead?” 

Chen Ping’an posed the question to himself, “That’s because over the nearly ten thousand long years, since the first cross-continent ferry arrived at the Upside-down Mountain, from that ferry called ‘Zhen Shui,’ if I remember correctly, the second ferry was from Fuyang Continent’s now-defunct sect, Yun Duy Mountain, called ‘Fu Yang,’ and the third was from the now-nonexistent Tong Ye Continent with the ‘Tong San’ ferry that capsized in a maritime disaster, killing everyone aboard. When the news reached the Sword Qi Great Wall, the sword immortals could only silently draw their swords to pay homage. This matter is far too distant, and many of the local sword immortals from the Sword Qi Great Wall may not be aware of it.”

Chen Ping’an straightened his posture.

“In those early years, almost all ferries heading to the Upside-down Mountain were not for profit but were essentially giving money to the Sword Qi Great Wall. Even though circumstances have changed over time, we at the Sword Qi Great Wall have always remembered your ferries across the eight continents and never forgot. Do you now understand why Nalan Shaowei was so furious but still didn’t draw his sword when he reached the Rain Dragon Sect’s territory? Now you know the reason, right? It wasn’t because that old ancestor from the Mountain and Water Cave was particularly clever, nor was it because he was adept at forming alliances; with a single sword strike, he could wipe them out without a trace.”

“You all are here to earn money, but in the end, the materials from each ferry are continuously sent to the Upside-down Mountain and then transferred to the Sword Qi Great Wall. Without you, the Sword Qi Great Wall would have long been unable to hold its ground, and we acknowledge that.”

Chen Ping’an stood up suddenly, laughing, and stretched out his hands, pressing them down several times, “Everyone sit; what are you all standing around for? When I say I’ll kill, I truly mean it! Is there any point in having a conversation? Do you really believe it?” 

The young Hidden Official smiled cheerfully, “Jiang shipmaster, sit. Liu Shen, you sit too. Everyone, let’s sit and talk. Harmony brings wealth; we are all merchants, not suited for fighting and killing.” 

Mi Yu remained standing. 

Thus, no one dared to sit down. 

Xie Songhua, Pu He, and Xie Zhi, among others from the Haoran world, still had evident killing intent. 

Chen Ping’an walked to Nalan Caihuan’s chair, reached out with two fingers, and gently pressed down on the shoulder of the young female Yuan Ying sword cultivator, smiling as he reminded her, “You should take the lead and sit down, or else you’ll die. There are many overly adventurous businesses in your hands, and the records of the Hidden Official lineage are all meticulously noted. So you are still too foolish; do you really think your ancestor’s business acumen surpasses yours? You are tens of thousands of miles apart from the old sword immortal. Nalan Shaowei has already saved your life once; he can’t do it a second time.”

Nalan Caihuan felt struck by lightning; her mind blanked, and her face lost color as she slowly sat down. 

Then the young Hidden Official rested his arms on the high back of Nalan Caihuan’s chair, looking at the ferry stewards across from him, his expression filled with helplessness, “I’ve treated you with respect, pressured you with force, enlightened you with reason, and moved you with emotion. As a small Hidden Official, I have done everything I could tonight, so why is it that no one is willing to give me a bit of face? Hmm?!”

Thus, everyone sat down. 

This young Hidden Official, who had sprung up from nowhere, was devious and ruthless, his mind twisted! 

Chen Ping’an returned to his original position but did not sit down, slowly saying, “I cannot guarantee that you will earn more money than before, but I can guarantee that you will earn a lot of money. This can be trusted. If you don’t believe it, it doesn’t matter; in the future, those increasingly thick account books on your desks won’t lie.” 

Mi Yu stood up, shaking his sleeves, producing volumes of books that hovered in front of each ferry steward. 

Chen Ping’an continued, “All the materials needed by the Sword Qi Great Wall will be on the list, sorted and priced according to Tian Gan. The specifics for discounts will depend on how capable you are at digging into the earth in the Haoran world. For those ferry stewards who couldn’t attend tonight’s meeting, please help spread the word. Many materials that were previously accepted will not be received at all in the future, but certain materials will be welcomed at the Sword Qi Great Wall at even higher prices. Each continent has its strengths.”

“Promising credit to the Sword Qi Great Wall while refusing us credit is a matter of friendship and connections, while the latter is the duty of a businessman to pursue wealth. You can always discuss this with me privately; whether it’s extending credit in exchange for benefits elsewhere, that can also be negotiated.”

All the ferry stewards began to carefully browse through the volumes. 

At this point, Chen Ping’an smiled at Bai Xi, the Yuan Ying cultivator from the Mountain and Water Cave, “Isn’t it surprising? One of your schemes was apparently to unload and reload before arriving at the Upside-down Mountain, aiming for a ferry that specializes in a few types of materials to seek a high price, avoiding mutual price pressure and selling cheaply to the Sword Qi Great Wall. Isn’t it just what the Sword Qi Great Wall is already helping you accomplish? Old Immortal Bai Xi, ask yourself, hasn’t the Sword Qi Great Wall always been straightforward in dealings with you? Why do you still act secretly without gaining anything? What’s the point? As for who leaked your intentions, there’s no need to investigate. With Fuyang Continent’s rich resources and the capabilities of the Mountain and Water Cave, you’ll be too busy making money in the future to bother with such trivial matters.”

The Aiai Continent cultivators, upon reaching a certain point, were stunned for a moment; the Sword Qi Great Wall was actually going to buy large amounts of snowflake coins in the future?! 

The steward from Dragon City’s Fu family, upon turning to a page, also found it interesting because the price of Yungenshi, a specialty from Yunxia Mountain, which had already been contracted with the Fu family, would go up! 

Even the ferry stewards from Beiju Lu Continent, who were least inclined to earn big money, were left speechless, realizing they would have to sit down and have a good discussion with the Skeleton Marsh’s Pi Ma Sect upon their return to their continent. 

Finally, Chen Ping’an said, “The next batch of money will be yours to earn freely. If anyone decides to stop their cross-continent ferry here and refuses to make this divine money, acting like a child throwing a tantrum and engaging in a conflict of wills, that’s fine; the rivers will remain green and the waters will flow, and this friendship will slowly be calculated. Moreover, aside from public matters, you ferry stewards should also think about your paths. For those who wish to acquire pill workshop items or certain fairy treasures, we at the Sword Qi Great Wall will record them one by one. As long as it’s feasible, we’ll help you exchange goods. If you need to supplement some divine coins, we will, of course, be straightforward with you. During this period, I guarantee that the Sword Qi Great Wall will not earn an extra snowflake coin from anyone. Consider it a small benefit I’m extending to all of you.” 

Jiang Gaotai discreetly flipped through the thick volume, asking via thought, “Hidden Official, are you truly not killing anyone and just doing business?”

Chen Ping’an smiled and said, “It all depends on the result, not the process. Shouldn’t I be thanking you? The day we no longer do business, we will settle the accounts then. But you can rest assured; for every completed business deal, the prices will stay there. Not only is it mutual consent, but it also counts as a bit of your goodwill, so there’s hope for reconciliation. Beyond that, the world is vast. Whether we meet again in this lifetime is uncertain.”

Jiang Gaotai was skeptical. 

Chen Ping’an either replied to some quiet inquiries from others or initiated conversations with them. 

“Your young city lord Fu Nanhua, what realm is he currently at?” 

“Lady Liu, I spoke hastily earlier. Your left and right arms, your junior sister, truly holds great respect for you.” 

“Don’t hold a grudge against our sword immortal Mi Yu; how could he bear to kill you? Of course, it was just for show for this Hidden Official. If you’re hurt by this, it will only cause him more pain. Unrequited love is a great regret in the world.” 

The young Hidden Official, who was still filled with youthful vigor, spoke casually, as if exchanging pleasantries with acquaintances. 

However, those words fell into the hearts of each ferry steward, making them chew on every word carefully, fearing they might miss some hidden meaning. 

Because even though no one had communicated directly, they all shared the same trepidation regarding one thing. 

This young man, at some earlier moment, had genuinely wanted to kill everyone present in the hall opposite the sword immortals. 

It might indeed be true, or it could be false. 

But what if it were true? 

Chen Ping’an continued to rest his chin on his hand, gazing out at the heavy snow. 

At this moment, that ferry belonging to Liu Xianyue should be nearing South Powsa Continent. 

And on that ferry, which had long departed from the Upside-down Mountain, 

Liu Xianyue was inside, reading by lamplight, with a seal resting on the table. 

The inscription read: “First Seal of Great Sword Immortal Chen Ping’an, retained by Brother Liu Xianyue.” 

The text inscribed read: “Moving Mountains and Draining Seas.” 

Liu Xianyue glanced at the seal and smiled knowingly. 

What a kid; he should learn to brag like himself. 

At the Upside-down Mountain, within the hall of the Spring Banner Pavilion, heavy snow fell upon the world outside. 

Mi Yu quietly asked, “Hidden Official, will it really end like this?” 

Chen Ping’an countered, “Did I say it was over?” 

Mi Yu replied, “It seems you did.” 

Chen Ping’an said, “I often don’t believe my own words.” 

Mi Yu immediately understood, saying, “Got it!” 

Chen Ping’an shot a sidelong glance at the big sword immortal Mi Yu. 

Mi Yu then directed his gaze toward the idle Shao Yunyan by the door, asking, “Sword Immortal Shao, do you have any good tea or wine at your place? It’s rather inappropriate for the Hidden Official to sit here like this.” 

Shao Yunyan smiled but remained silent, making no move. 

Mi Yu then pulled out a jar of fairy wine and presented it to the Hidden Official. 

He stood up to serve the wine, placed it on the table, and gracefully turned around to take his seat. 

Everything flowed naturally, without a hint of awkwardness. 

The owner of the Spring Banner Pavilion at the door felt embarrassed for this Jade Purity realm sword immortal. 

At that moment, Mi Yu was undoubtedly unaware that he would soon become the number one lackey of the Hidden Official, destined for that role. Such is fate. 

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 748: The Sun Sets, The Moon Rises

In a moment, the only sound in the room was the rustling of pages. Each shipowner, skilled in business and accounting, was deep in their calculations, as was their forte and a part of their craft. 

With the hidden lord's permission, the Sword Immortals had departed for the most part. Li Cai, Ku Xia, Yuan Qingshu, Xie Zhi, Song Ping, and Pu He had all returned to the Sword Qi Great Wall. Only Mi Yu and Gao Kui remained. 

Shao Yunyan continued to sit by the entrance. A dignified Sword Immortal guarding his own territory was indeed a rare sight. 

Xie Songhua needed to personally "escort" a ship across the Aihai Continent to leave the Upside Down Mountain, so she naturally would not leave Chunfan Studio just yet. 

Could the words of a Sword Immortal be merely for scaring people? 

Yan Ming and Nalan Caihuan also needed to stay. In the future, specific trade dealings would still require these two, alongside Shao Yunyan, to coordinate business with the ships of the Eight Continents right here in Chunfan Studio. 

Tonight's transaction at Chunfan Studio was not trivial. 

In the vast territory of the Haoran World, hundreds of dynasties, sects on the mountains, and influential families of immortals would be set in motion due to tonight's dialogue. 

Chen Pingan remained seated in the main position, sipping the wine brought by Mi Yu, not urging any ship owner. He held the wine pot in one hand, while the other gently opened and closed into a fist.

Nalan Caihuan was perhaps the one in the room who harbored the deepest hatred towards Chen Pingan. 

Gao Kui’s purpose for coming here was singular: to kill Nalan Caihuan! 

With such intense hatred, there was often more fear than hate involved. 

Nalan Caihuan's greater fear lay in the words spoken by the young hidden lord, “I can conduct business with these outsiders while pinching their noses, but how can I not tolerate someone from my own side who holds real power? That makes no sense. Nalan Caihuan, I assure you, the Nalan family won't suffer too much loss. If fortune smiles upon us, there might even be profit. As for luck, I can't guarantee anything.” 

Nalan Caihuan had also assured some matters. She felt she had truly come to an understanding with the young hidden lord, exchanging heart-to-heart sentiments. 

However, this not only failed to change her current predicament but instead brought about her greatest fear: Gao Kui still had not left Chunfan Studio and was quietly sitting nearby, drinking not the local brew but the wine from Bamboo Sea Cave.

Nalan Caihuan calmed herself and began to ponder all the details of tonight’s discussions, seeking to understand the young man more thoroughly. 

She had previously had little real interaction with Chen Pingan or the second shopkeeper; they had only discussed matters once after he became the hidden lord, and it hadn’t been particularly pleasant. 

Nalan Caihuan recalled the young hidden lord's closing words, which felt like a final verdict. 

The way scholars meticulously choose their words could be truly terrifying. 

According to the customs of the Haoran World, it should have been “persuading with emotion, explaining with reason,” yet Chen Pingan insisted on saying “explaining with emotion, persuading with reason” instead. 

Emotion referred to the ties of kinship, a sentiment long forgotten by the merchants of the Nine Continents but still cherished by the Sword Qi Great Wall. 

Reason was simpler: it was the Sword Immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall, who could take heads with flying swords. 

Only after that did the most vulgar and materialistic aspect of wealth come into play, where everyone sat down, speaking properly and conducting business fairly. 

Yet before this, Chen Pingan’s most ruthless threat was not the immediate threat of a Sword Immortal killing, but rather a cut that pointed directly at some ship owners' vested interests. 

Disregarding any morality, business rules, or sect relationships, Chen Pingan chose to confront his opponents head-on, such as Wu Qiao, Tang Feiqian, and the reputations of two fifth-level practitioners in the vicinity of the private residence in North Julu Continent's Dili Mountain. 

It was a life worse than death. 

Of course, there was also the life of Dai Hao from the “Southern Ji” Jiang Gao Terrace, and Liu Shen, the manager of the “Rainbow Dress” ship. 

When it came to death, death it would be. 

Don’t talk to me about sect foundations or the consequences of breaking off trade; as long as anyone stands up from their seat, the Sword Qi Great Wall would only target that person before the young hidden lord. 

Many of the proper and prestigious sect masters of the Haoran World, especially the proud offspring of wealthy families, might not be able to come to an agreement on such matters, and it could even lead to a complete falling out. 

However, discussing this with the merchant class present here, who had long ceased to be purely cultivators, was the most effective approach. 

The true turning point in all of this, of course, lay in the documents Mi Yu had produced. 

Without them, no matter how many calculations Chen Pingan made, once dozens of ship owners left Chunfan Studio and Upside Down Mountain, he would only end up dragging the entire Sword Qi Great Wall into resentment, with no benefit to himself. Perhaps the hidden lord could continue to act, but the financial authority of the Sword Qi Great Wall would have to revert to her and Yan Ming. In this process, the Sword Qi Great Wall would suffer the most, inevitably being harshly dealt with by these merchants. 

Nalan Caihuan regained some composure, finally realizing how to interact with the young hidden lord. 

In terms of appearance and demeanor, Nalan Caihuan was indeed a great beauty. 

Thus, Mi Yu cast her a glance. 

Then he shook his head, his eyes filled with a mix of pity and disdain, turning away from Nalan Caihuan and continuing to rest his eyes. 

If Nalan Caihuan could sway a man’s heart purely with her looks, then Mi Yu could surely captivate women just by his appearance. 

Sitting across from them, the resentful and deeply troubled Yuan Ying lady caught sight of this exchange and felt her gloom slightly lifted. 

This heartless man, who should be punished a thousand times over, had not spared her a single glance after uttering that blasphemous statement, repeatedly casting his gaze elsewhere, deliberately avoiding her each time. 

If Mi Yu had no feelings for her, would he be so deliberate? 

Moreover, it was said that Nalan Caihuan had once harbored feelings for Mi Yu, yet she still failed to approach him, unable to become a pair of celestial partners with him in the Sword Qi Great Wall. 

Thinking this way made her feel she had triumphed over Nalan Caihuan. 

Looking at Mi Yu, whose expression was desolate and lonely, she turned her gaze to the beautiful scenery of heavy snow outside, lost in thought. 

Compared to the previous sycophantic demeanor he had when serving wine to the young hidden lord, he was now a different person altogether. 

She felt inexplicably pained; now that they were both fifth-level Sword Immortals, how could Mi Yu still be so humiliated in his homeland? 

Someone like Mi Yu deserved to die! 

But liking him was, after all, still liking him. 

Both were out of her hands, leaving her feeling helpless. 

Chen Pingan rested his chin on one hand, observing the various human emotions unfolding, and upon noticing Mi Yu’s subtle changes, couldn’t help but feel a measure of respect. The lovesick person could only be moved by their affection; Mi Yu, this remarkably talented heartbreaker, if he devoted himself solely to romantic pursuits in cultivation, should have reached the level of ascension by now. He could probably contend with Jiang Shangzhen on the path of enlightenment. 

Chen Pingan intended to find an opportunity to vent the frustrations of these lovesick women by giving Mi Yu a good beating, one he wouldn’t be able to retaliate against. 

Xie Songhua appeared troubled, contemplating the "Southern Ji" Jiang Gao Terrace and the "Rainbow Dress" ship managed by Liu Shen, both of which she couldn’t afford to miss. This female Sword Immortal's gaze flitted restlessly, her bamboo box of sword intent creating ripples that never ceased. 

Now that things at Chunfan Studio were settled, she still had several personal grievances to address. The crew from Aihai Continent was the first to speak up, but when they finally stood to speak, it appeared they were seeking death, and they were the most numerous among the Aihai Continent group. 

Looking at Wei Jin and Yuan Qingshu, and then at the cultivators from Baoping Continent and Nanpusa Continent across from them, weren’t they all showing great respect to the two? 

What? Just because I’m a woman, I’m not a Sword Immortal anymore?! 

Dai Hao, trembling with fear, had no choice but to take the initiative to ask the young man, who was slowly drinking, cautiously inquiring, “Lord Hidden, what about Xie Sword Immortal?” 

Dai Hao didn’t even dare to lift her gaze toward the main seat; she had no choice but to forget about manners for the moment. Otherwise, if she raised her head, Xie Songhua, a terrifying Sword Immortal who could easily take down even a Jade Purity Realm demon, would definitely notice her. 

Chen Pingan smiled, “Do you remember what Xie Sword Immortal said when she first met you all tonight? Think carefully.” 

Among all the ships from Aihai Continent, if anyone was most in need of money, it was Xie Songhua personally escorting their ship. If she did not escort it properly, they could blame her. 

Dai Hao breathed a sigh of relief. “Thank you for the reminder, Lord Hidden.” 

Wei Jin deliberately chose not to join Li Cai and the others, instead opting to leave last on his own. 

Chen Pingan stood up, “I’ll see Wei Sword Immortal off first. Mi Yu, you’re responsible for answering any questions from the guests. Whether deals are struck or not, just note them down. I’ll say this once again, once seated, everyone here is a merchant. When in Rome, do as the Romans do. Whether one earns a lot or a little is up to each individual’s abilities. I’m no exception; tonight at Chunfan Studio, the rules for making money will be even greater than the title of Lord Hidden.” 

Chen Pingan looked toward Liu Shen, the shipowner of the "Rainbow Dress," and then to Liu Yu of the "Fuzhong" ship from Liuxia Continent, smiling as he said, “I’d appreciate it if the two of you could help keep a record of the discussions.” 

Chen Pingan accompanied the Sword Immortal from the Wind and Snow Temple to the entrance of Chunfan Studio. 

Wei Jin said, “I don’t really like to meddle in other people’s affairs, but I have some questions. Can I ask?” 

“There’s nothing you can’t ask, nor anything I can’t answer.” 

Chen Pingan smiled, “I’m very glad to meet a Sword Immortal from Baoping Continent here at the Sword Qi Great Wall, and you’re not at all inferior to other senior Sword Immortals.” 

Chen Pingan continued, “That’s the truth, no matter whether you believe it or not.” 

Wei Jin chuckled, “If you hadn’t said that extra sentence, I would have actually believed you.” 

Chen Pingan said, “Just ask.” 

Wei Jin then asked, “All the outsiders, including Xie Zhi, don’t want to gain anything extra from tonight’s affair. Why did you insist on coming to Chunfan Studio beforehand to conduct a transaction? Isn’t that... overkill? Or rather, it shouldn’t be like that. Let’s change the question: you said you wouldn’t let any Sword Immortal leave the Upside Down Mountain empty-handed, nor would you allow anyone to play the villain in Chunfan Studio, but you didn’t specify what the compensation would be. How can you say for sure that you won’t let the Sword Immortals be disappointed? What exactly do you consider compensation?” 

Chen Pingan hesitated for a moment before slowly replying, “In terms of sentiment, it’s about hoping good people get good rewards. In terms of business, I just don’t want the Sword Qi Great Wall to owe anyone favors anymore. It’s straightforward; we’re doing business with these outsiders in good conscience. As for the compensation you inquired about, it varies from person to person, and I won’t elaborate too much, as it involves the privacy of the Sword Immortals.” 

In addition, Chen Pingan didn’t hold back, “But there is a bottom line I can state clearly: in the future, any outsider Sword Immortal who still has the chance to return home can take at least one potential candidate for a lower fifth-level Sword Immortal from the Sword Qi Great Wall. Those who are unwilling to take anyone will receive other forms of compensation. Those willing to take one or two more, as long as the Sword Qi Great Wall has such promising candidates, may take them as well.” 

Wei Jin could only smile bitterly and shake his head. 

What kind of reasoning was this? 

Outsider Sword Immortals, intercontinental ships, candidates for Sword Immortals that the Sword Qi Great Wall had yet to develop—past, present, and future—all accounted for. 

And if these young and talented Sword Immortal candidates had a chance to flourish in the Haoran World, what kind of scene would that create? 

Moreover, those outsider Sword Immortals who take on the role of teachers, regardless of their individual temperaments, are still brave enough to come to the Sword Qi Great Wall and risk death on the battlements; wouldn’t they be inclined to teach these disciples with great care? 

Once these children grow up and eventually rise across the continents, would they not band together? And those returning Sword Immortals who have left the Sword Qi Great Wall would also likely band together. 

To take it a step further, even if the Sword Qi Great Wall were to fall in the future, wouldn’t their meeting place become another form of the Sword Qi Great Wall? 

Wei Jin smiled. 

He looked forward to that scene. 

This was Wei Jin looking forward, but if he were to look back... 

He couldn’t help but recall the first time they met; Wei Jin remembered that the young man next to him was a clumsy, timid lad back then. 

And that young man had a very clear and bright gaze. 

Wei Jin stopped walking, sighed, and turned to look at Chen Pingan, who habitually rubbed his hands to keep warm. “You, an outsider, why do you bother thinking so far ahead for the Sword Qi Great Wall?” 

Chen Pingan smiled, “I have a wife here; you don’t. How can you compare with me?” 

Wei Jin shook his head, feeling like drinking again, not wanting to discuss this matter. 

Chen Pingan had been straightforward with him regarding his own future plans, and the elder Sword Immortal had been present at the time. 

Wei Jin had no intention of refusing. 

He just hoped he could match up to Xie Songhua from Aihai Continent and establish his own achievements worthy of the "Celestial Platform" at the Sword Qi Great Wall before heading to Fengyao Continent to accomplish that task. 

Wei Jin had no particular attachment to the Wind and Snow Temple; once his master left, he had long since let go of it. However, since his master had entrusted him with the "Celestial Platform," he needed to do something. 

The elderly cultivators of the previous generation valued face, and as a disciple, Wei Jin had to help his master earn it, so he wouldn’t be left silent when visiting the grave in the future. 

Chen Pingan said, “Can I share something I’ve never mentioned to anyone?” 

Wei Jin replied, “If it’s not calculated, I’ll listen.” 

The Wind and Snow Temple’s Wei Jin, with his sword opening the night, was yet to arrive. 

That kind of Sword Immortal bearing. 

Song Yusheng from Shushui Kingdom, facing an army alone, stood against an entire nation. 

That kind of warrior spirit. 

Ding Ying from the Lotus Flower Blessed Land, whose true opponent was the Dao itself. 

That kind of ambition to compete with heaven. 

These were the battles Chen Pingan recalled most vividly. 

Hearing Chen Pingan’s words, Wei Jin chuckled, “What you’re saying doesn’t seem to matter much regarding realms.” 

Chen Pingan nodded, “It doesn’t matter much.” 

Wei Jin left Chunfan Studio. 

Chen Pingan turned back alone, retracing his steps. 

Halfway back, he crouched next to a courtyard, scooped up the snow, rubbed it on his face, took a deep breath, and formed a solid snowball. 

Shao Yunyan stood behind the young hidden lord, chuckling softly, “Sword Immortals kill without shedding blood; tonight, Lord Hidden’s actions are quite similar.” 

Chen Pingan shook his head and smiled, “Not so wonderful. It’s like a family with a thick foundation; the younger generation relies on their elders’ power to act. They have their own abilities, but it’s not as grand as imagined.” 

He casually threw the snowball onto the roof, tightened the golden cord of the jade token at his waist, “If it were Yan Ming or Nalan Caihuan sitting in my position, they could accomplish the same thing. What they lack is not heart and calculation, but simply this jade token.” 

Shao Yunyan shook his head, “I doubt that.” 

Chen Pingan smiled, “If everyone were as perceptive as you, Mr. Shao, knowing the difference between sincere words and polite ones, and being able to hear the unspoken meanings, it would save much effort.” 

Shao Yunyan remarked, “If there really needs to be an apology, it would involve Sun Juyuan and Mi Yu. As for who lays out the money for the compensation, whether it’s Yan Ming, Nalan Caihuan, or myself at Chunfan Studio, the order doesn’t really matter; what Lord Hidden needs to keep in mind is just how far the compensation must go: whether to lose entirely or split it three ways.” 

Chen Pingan replied, “Let’s start by covering half; if that time comes and there’s no improvement in financial operations or unexpected events cause Yan and Nalan families to incur losses, then Mr. Shao will have no choice but to sell off Chunfan Studio cheaply.” 

Shao Yunyan chuckled, “That’s fine. Actually, I’m not afraid of surprises; I’m just afraid of the lack of procedure in doing things.” 

Chen Pingan said, “If we want to prevent those ship owners from leaving Chunfan Studio and still being unable to warm up to one another, we can’t rely on someone like the young man who once disrupted the situation and united the hearts of people into a single cord. To accomplish this, we must first let them feel disheartened and lose complete trust in their former allies, creating a façade of unity while being divided at heart. My earlier somewhat ambiguous and half-truthful words were ultimately not solid facts; those old foxes among them are often the ones who won’t shed tears until they see the coffin; without suffering a stick of hardship, they won’t know the sweetness of a jujube. Therefore, I will be doing some underhanded deeds soon, many of which may require Mr. Shao to lend a hand. During this period, if I need any Sword Immortal’s assistance, just ask.” 

Shao Yunyan humorously inquired, “Lord Hidden, without discussing human sentiments or visions, do you think this style of doing things is deserving of the elder Sword Immortal’s special regard and high expectations?” 

Chen Pingan chuckled, “You shouldn’t speak so frankly, Mr. Shao.” 

Shao Yunyan replied, “Friends should speak without reservation.” 

Chen Pingan scooped up some snow again, lightly clapping his hands, sending snowflakes flying, and slowly said, “Doing things well is always harder than reasoning and being a good person.” 

To outsiders, a person who does not reason at all actually has many justifications supporting this “lack of reason.” A person who enjoys making money and can indeed make money has actually paid many prices they don’t consider costs. 

What? Such people exist? 

Oh, so it’s this kind of person. 

With vision clouded, bumping into obstacles everywhere, one can only leave it to fate. 

With a clear vision, when the world is bright, many unpleasant sights come into view. 

One suffers. 

One is troubled. 

Shao Yunyan declared, “To deny the goodwill of the entire world based on one’s own suffering is not good. To deny the joys and sorrows of others with grand visions is equally not good.” 

Chen Pingan stood up and smiled, “You truly have insight into human hearts, Mr. Shao; you are indeed a learned person.” 

Shao Yunyan chuckled, “Not as much as the Hidden Lord.” 

“Where is that?” 

“Just being polite.” 

They quickly became familiar, sharing warmth and camaraderie. 

“Brother Shao, didn’t you leave a gourd vine behind? I just want to take a look, to see the world; you don’t need to look at me like I’m a thief.” 

“Indeed, not a single gourd for cultivating swords was left behind; they were all taken by that little girl Lu Sui to North Julu Continent. If you don’t believe me, feel free to search; if you find one, I’ll give you another.” 

“Alright, please send me a layout of Chunfan Studio; I might frequent this place in the future, and with such a large estate, I wouldn’t want to get lost.” 

“I don’t think that’s necessary.” 

“Brother Shao, if you keep being so uncooperative, we’ll truly become a laughingstock among the brothers.” 

“Not at all.” 

The ship manager from North Julu Continent had no objections to the extensive inventory and tedious pricing in that hefty book. 

In fact, compared to the meticulous scrutiny of other ship owners and managers, those old practitioners from North Julu Continent flipped through the book casually, either drinking or having tea, each feeling relaxed and at ease. 

They originally didn’t make much money, but now had the opportunity to earn more; what more could they hope for? 

At the Southern Pusa Continent ship, there were minor objections. 

The old shipowners from the Fufeng family and Ding family in the Old Dragon City of Baoping Continent had some small disagreements as well. 

The shipowners from the Central Land, Aihai Continent, and Fengyao Continent had not yet spoken. 

The shipowners from Liuxia and Jinjia Continent were neighboring lands with generally good relations, with many resources and minerals being mutually exchanged for transport to the Upside Down Mountain, so they had been communicating in low voices. 

They planned to wait for Wu Qiao, Tang Feiqian, Jiang Gao Terrace, and Bai Xi to speak first before deciding their course of action. 

That hefty book was put together by Chen Pingan, with contributions from the Sword Immortals of the Hidden Lord lineage, taking turns to compile the files. Among them, Lin Junbi and other outsider Sword Immortals had made significant contributions, as many of the old records from the Hidden Lord lineage were unable to keep pace with the changing circumstances of the Haoran World. Mi Yu, having transcribed and consolidated the information, couldn't say he was intimately familiar with it, but in the hall, Mi Yu had already discussed and negotiated effectively with the shipowners. 

Liu Yu and Liu Shen had taken on an extra task, helping to record the discussions between both parties, and Shao Yunyan had prepared writing materials for them before leaving the hall to find Chen Pingan. 

The way to make money in the world is really just about expanding income and reducing expenditures. 

The young man pointed out that the products of the Eight Continents each had their strengths. Therefore, how to specifically explore sources of income and reduce the expenses of intercontinental shipping was a significant matter. 

The book contained prefaces in the sections on geography and shipping, filled with enlightening words, hoping for the Eight Continent ships to offer advice to their respective sects and clans. 

So tonight's discussions were not simply about bargaining between intercontinental shipping and the Sword Qi Great Wall. 

It was far more complex and far-reaching, involving all intercontinental shipping and existing trade channels that needed to be re-negotiated for goods, pricing, and returns. 

In the young man’s words, it could all be discussed openly; they could talk privately, or however they wished. 

Nalan Caihuan remained a cold observer, but the more she pondered, the more she felt there were many subtleties to grasp. If they could connect the dots, they would find it was all a straightforward calculation. 

If the Sword Qi Great Wall brandished its sword by threatening the ship owners' personal interests in business, that was one kind of bullying. 

Then the young hidden lord’s many hints reminded the merchants present to consider their own paths in cultivation and weigh their own gains and losses a bit more; the Sword Qi Great Wall not only welcomed this but even encouraged it, offering some small assistance. This was the Sword Qi Great Wall’s way of drawing the sword back into the sheath, representing a form of receiving. 

They guaranteed that all future business dealings for the ships would earn them a decent amount, at most serving as a further enhancement. 

However, if they could make all the ship owners collect money for themselves, turning the general business of their “own” mountains into real “self” businesses, that would be a timely assistance. 

In this ebb and flow, people’s hearts would no longer be as they once were. 

Yet how all these plans would pan out ultimately depended on whether they could withstand the scrutiny of worldly affairs and endure the many storms and unforeseen events to come. 

As they approached the main hall of Chunfan Studio, Chen Pingan suddenly asked, “Is there an exceptionally gifted accountant around?” 

Shao Yunyan sighed, “I once had a direct disciple who was an expert in this field; all the business of Chunfan Studio was managed by him without fault, possessing the ability of ‘creating something from nothing.’” 

Chen Pingan asked, “Is there a chance to call him back to work at Chunfan Studio?” 

Shao Yunyan smiled and asked, “Do you trust my judgment of character?” 

Chen Pingan replied, “Human hearts are hard to read; the difficulty lies not in how they were or are, but in how they will be in the future. Therefore, I can’t fully trust you. Fortunately, I have great faith in the Sword Qi Great Wall’s ability to correct mistakes.” 

Shao Yunyan nodded, “Then I’ll see if I can call him back. He has a natural gift for calculations. With tedious numbers, he has an innate intuition, and he enjoys it. I had given him a confidential letter to join a larger merchant sect in Aihai Continent; if he could first gain experience in the new Chunfan Studio, he probably wouldn’t need my letter as a stepping stone.” 

Chen Pingan said, “He must be brought back to the Upside Down Mountain.” 

Upon entering the main hall, a long negotiation began. 

Nalan Caihuan was again greatly surprised. 

The young hidden lord seemed to intentionally want everyone to be thoroughly tested on details and prices, seemingly unconcerned with rewriting a new book. 

Even the North Julu Continent ship manager, who had firmly decided not to speak, was pulled into the business table by Chen Pingan’s smiling inquiries about whether North Julu Continent had any similar or alternative items to those listed in the book. 

Back and forth, those old practitioners grew impatient; since the hidden lord made it clear it was all about business, they were not polite anymore. Once they opened their mouths, it was a matter of just a few words. 

With the North Julu Continent ship owners, who shared the same interests as the Sword Qi Great Wall, it was the same with Nanpusa Continent, and even the two quiet ships from Baoping Continent were beginning to speak more. 

Some new prices were agreed upon; the young hidden lord directly let Mi Yu erase the old text pricing in the book and rewrite it next to it. 

Wu Qiao and Tang Feiqian felt a little more at ease and then began to speak. 

Some prices had been raised, while others had inadvertently been lowered, but in any case, both sides were exchanging offers. 

Yan Ming no longer maintained his silence, and even Nalan Caihuan stopped being mute. 

More and more ship managers were openly calculating their profits in their seats. 

Earlier, more than a dozen Sword Immortals sat in attendance, with the younger hidden lord in the main seat, calling the shots. 

Now, with him being a seasoned hand at calculations, the results of who won and who lost were no longer certain. 

On the side of Aihai Continent, Jiang Gao Terrace from the Jade Purity Realm spoke a lot, and exchanges were taking place as if he was the one in charge of the Aihai Continent ships. 

The other ship owners had a certain degree of admiration for Jiang Gao Terrace; who would have thought that after having gone through life and death, he would still be so fearless? 

Jiang Gao Terrace appeared calm and exuded the aura of a fifth-level immortal, but internally he was cursing. Damn, he was being forced to bargain ruthlessly by the hidden lord; did he think himself so blind as to carry his own head in his hands like a hero? 

Chen Pingan looked up at the door. 

Before he knew it, dawn had broken. 

On the account books, there were no one-shot deals; they often included many clauses, amended repeatedly, and both sides clearly still had plenty to negotiate. 

The key was that as time passed, disputes began to arise between the continents and the ships; initially, they would hold back, but eventually, they no longer cared about appearances, with some even slamming tables and glaring at each other. After all, the young hidden lord didn’t mind these things; instead, he smiled, taking sides and saying a few inflammatory words, using the opportunity to press down prices, sipping some wine, and plainly starting to act shamelessly again. 

Everyone present was a cultivator, so they couldn’t be said to be fatigued, but whether they were tired in spirit was another matter. 

Yet all knew that once tonight’s affairs reached a final conclusion, then any slight benefit gained for their ships in this account would turn into an immense profit in the future, even if it was just a minor price difference. 

Thinking of it this way, even if it was tiring, there was a certain satisfaction in it. 

At noon, the hidden lord suggested they could return to their respective courtyards and discuss matters again behind closed doors. 

If they wanted to visit and discuss, Chunfan Studio would not obstruct them. 

The crowd in the hall immediately dispersed. 

Jiang Gao Terrace rose later, discreetly glancing at the young hidden lord, who smiled and nodded. 

Yan Ming and Nalan Caihuan also intended to discuss matters. 

Chen Pingan first approached Gao Kui, saying, “Thank you. Sword Immortal Gao can return to the Sword Qi Great Wall now.” 

Gao Kui responded indifferently, “It was just a matter of standing up, glaring at a few women, and drinking a jar of Bamboo Sea Cave wine. What’s there to thank about?” 

Chen Pingan smiled, “Some words must still be said.” 

Mi Yu chuckled, “Gao Kui, when speaking with the hidden lord, please be polite.” 

Gao Kui had never had a high opinion of Mi Yu, who was known as the embroidered pillow of the Sword Qi Great Wall. In the past, if he encountered someone like Mi Yu, who always thought about sneaking under women’s skirts, he would have rather not looked at him at all or spoken a word. 

After last night, his impression of Mi Yu hadn’t changed much, but he was now willing to converse, though not with anything nice, “Mi Yu, don’t waste your life like this. If your brother Mi Hu weren’t dragged down by you, he would have already reached the realm of immortals. You should know that at first, Yue Qing’s talent was recognized as inferior to Mi Hu’s.” 

After saying that, Gao Kui strode away. 

Mi Yu lamented, “This Gao Kui deserves to be a lifelong bachelor. I only love sincere women, and women love me sincerely; genuine feelings exchanged for real intent—what’s wrong with that?” 

Chen Pingan said, “With your behavior, if you haven’t been killed by the bachelor Sword Immortals, you should thank the Great Sword Immortal Mi Hu.” 

Mi Yu turned to look at the still listless Aihai Continent female Sword Immortal, and just as he called out, “Xie Sword Immortal,” Xie Songhua smiled and said, “Please stay far away from me.” 

Sighing, Mi Yu exited the hall, crossed the threshold, and went to build a snowman, finding a secluded corner to create a figure that resembled a girl in shape but not in spirit. 

The Great Sword Immortal Mi chose a flowerbed at Chunfan Studio, where flowers and plants remained vibrant even in the heavy winter snow. 

Nalan Caihuan, that lady, was destined not to come to such places; she was beautiful but too focused on making money. However, the girl from the Central Land would likely come here, and she would surely love the blooming immortal peonies that thrived even under the snow. When she came to the flowerbed and saw the flowers, she would spot the snowman secretly standing beneath the leaves, and then she would realize her own infatuation. 

When outsider Sword Immortals leave the Sword Qi Great Wall, local Sword Immortals often host a farewell dinner. 

Just like in the past when Huang Tong from the Taihui Sword Sect was about to return home, the old Sword Immortal Dong Sangeng personally saw him off. 

Xie Songhua also needed someone to see her off. 

In fact, Chen Pingan was merely escorting her to the entrance of Chunfan Studio. 

Xie Songhua felt somewhat displeased. 

She thought she shouldn’t leave the Upside Down Mountain like this. 

Chen Pingan suggested she could wait at Jiaolong Valley, and if she was truly bored, she could stroll around Yulong Sect to relax. 

Xie Songhua immediately became interested, asking, “Does this mean we’re targeting Jiang Gao Terrace? What about Dai Hao? How about we take care of both? The favor I owe you, you’re good at calculating, so it should be put to good use. We’re all heading north anyway; Sword Immortals travel fast.” 

Chen Pingan shook his head, “Just wait for my news.” 

Xie Songhua complained, “So indecisive! If it weren’t for the deep debt of gratitude I owe you, I wouldn’t bother talking to you. Once I reach Aihai Continent, don’t come looking for me to reminisce; I won’t have wine to offer.” 

Chen Pingan smiled, “The two little girls at the Luanque Inn will be entrusted to you, Xie Sword Immortal.” 

As soon as Xie Songhua thought of this, her mood brightened, “They’re both good seedlings; I’ll take good care of them. It might be a bit difficult for them to become Sword Immortals like their master, but they won’t escape being Earth Immortal Sword Practitioners. Chen Pingan, thank you for this, but it doesn’t count as a debt; just let me say thanks, and that’s enough.” 

Chen Pingan gave a few more reminders, emphasizing that the two girls were from the streets of the Sword Qi Great Wall and were still very young, having never seen the outside world. Teaching them the sword and the way is crucial, but how to allow them to live freely in the Haoran World without forgetting their roots will require Xie Sword Immortal’s effort. Especially before they can defend themselves, they must not mention their origins from the Sword Qi Great Wall, and they absolutely must not be impulsive when outsiders bring up gossip about the Sword Qi Great Wall during their cultivation journey; no matter how hurtful the words are, they should bear with it, treating it as part of their heart training outside of sword practice... 

Xie Songhua felt a headache coming on, saying she understood, she understood. 

As the two approached the entrance of Chunfan Studio, 

Chen Pingan finally stopped his rambling and asked a strange question, “Xie Sword Immortal, can you brew wine yourself?” 

Xie Songhua was somewhat at a loss, “Of course not.” 

Chen Pingan smiled, “I have a friend who once said his greatest wish in life was, ‘What’s happening in the mountains? Pine flowers brew wine, spring water brews tea.’” 

Xie Songhua asked directly, “Chen Pingan, are you trying to tease me after being around that Mi Yu for too long?” 

Chen Pingan couldn’t argue. 

When it came to dealing with women, Chen Pingan felt he had never been good at it, far from the adept Sword Immortal Mi Yu, and even less so than Jiang Shangzhen, who had gone from enemy to friend. Truth be told, even his good friend Qi Jinglong far surpassed him in this regard. 

Xie Songhua laughed heartily, “You really are a child; no matter how clever your mind is usually, you still can’t joke.” 

Chen Pingan let out a sigh of relief. 

Xie Songhua clasped her fists, saying, “Lord Hidden, please stop here; there’s no need for your farewell. I don’t have the habit of walking around with men.” 

Chen Pingan laughed and returned the gesture, “I can’t imagine what kind of charming man could catch the eye of Xie Sword Immortal. If we meet again in the future, I hope you’ll let me see him.” 

Xie Songhua snorted, “Charming? Charming my ass! If he dares to pursue me, I’ll chop him down.” 

Chen Pingan helplessly said, “Xie Sword Immortal, it’s not that kind of charming.” 

Xie Songhua burst into laughter, “You’re still young; you really think I wouldn’t know this little bit of knowledge? If you’ve managed to make the Hidden Lord suffer a couple of times, I’m in a good mood; now I’ll take my leave!” 

Xie Songhua walked down the street outside Chunfan Studio, taking large strides. After walking a dozen steps, she waved her hand, speaking without turning around. 

Her words were very much in line with her character. 

“The backside isn’t that big, and the waist isn’t that slim; what’s there to look at? Look at Nalan Caihuan more, that Liu Shen isn’t bad either; the table is almost collapsing under the weight.” 

Chen Pingan could only smile bitterly as he turned and stepped into the residence. 

His fingers knocked lightly as he walked slowly. 

His brother would head southeast toward Tongye Continent and would first find the old Tianjun at Taiping Mountain, along with the mountain master, Song Mao. 

Wei Jin would head to Fengyao Continent. 

Shao Yunyan and a temporarily undecided great Sword Immortal would go to Nanpusa Continent. 

Shao Yunyan's journey would have its priorities, as he was limited by his current realm; being a Jade Purity Realm Sword Practitioner alone, he couldn’t bear that responsibility. Thus, Chen Pingan had been pondering the choice of the third Sword Immortal, needing to be a local Sword Immortal who had reached at least the realm of immortals. 

Chen Pingan had considered Lu Zhi, and also thought about Chen Xi or Qi Tingji, but compared to his brother and Wind and Snow Temple’s Wei Jin, they would definitely set out later. 

However, pulling one thread could unravel the entire cloth; this choice would bring forth many hidden connections, making it exceedingly troublesome. One misstep could lead to disaster, so he would have to observe further and wait. 

In truth, at that moment on the city wall, Chen Pingan had truly not trusted the old deaf man, who was a supreme demon yet adhered to rules, but rather the peak great Sword Immortal, Lu Zhi. 

This was not to say Lu Zhi was an insider of the wilderness; far from it, but Lu Zhi would definitely not wish to die on the city wall, belonging to that kind of person who would say, “Seeing the overall situation is settled, I’ll sheathe my sword and leave.” 

Chen Qingdu actually didn’t mind Lu Zhi making such a choice, nor would Chen Pingan harbor any contempt or neglect toward Lu Zhi because of it. 

And Chen Qingdu’s decision to have Lu Zhi protect the Hidden Lord lineage was, in itself, a hint. 

Chen Pingan couldn’t understand, but it didn’t matter; it wouldn’t change the outcome. If by chance he understood, then as the new Hidden Lord of the Sword Qi Great Wall, he should do what a Hidden Lord ought to do. 

For instance, ensuring Lu Zhi could leave the Sword Qi Great Wall with a clear conscience. 

As long as he didn’t betray the Sword Qi Great Wall in the midst of a great battle, turning his sword against his own and severing heads to claim credit in the wilderness, that was acceptable. 

This was the one bottom line set by the elder Sword Immortal, Chen Qingdu, but beyond this line, everything else was at one’s discretion. 

Throughout the millennia of the Sword Qi Great Wall’s history, without discussing those who willingly chose death, how many Sword Immortals, who did not wish to die, could actually have lived on grounds of sentiment and reason, could have avoided death, yet still perished? 

All these reasons ultimately boiled down to Chen Qingdu wanting them dead. 

If one were to place themselves in the shoes of that elder Sword Immortal, what would they feel? 

This was not just a matter of a few years, or a hundred years, but an entire ten thousand years. 

Does one’s true heart matter? 

Chen Pingan could only feel that if it were him, his heart would have long since shattered into pieces, broken beyond repair, either going mad as a means of escape or completely turning to another extreme. 

Such matters are better left unthought; overthinking is futile. 

Chen Pingan began to recall the words of his brother before their parting, originally thinking that his brother would not give him even a hint of a good expression. 

However, surprisingly, before leaving, his brother still bore a smile, his words were extremely calm, even half-jokingly speaking to his younger disciple, “Learning to write without mastering the sword first, using the sword without merit before studying—brother, don’t follow your elder brother’s example in this matter.” 

At this moment, the Sword Immortal Shao Yunyan had already entered the study. 

After seating himself at the writing desk, he picked up his brush and wrote down a sentence, lightly setting it down, appearing very satisfied. 

“From small things to big, being careful with the微细, day by day, learning should be illuminated by light.” 

Chen Pingan made his way back to the main hall, sitting in the main position, momentarily free of tasks, pressing his hand on the surface of the four-immortal table, which had originally been tightly connected, now showing some looseness and slight tremors. 

When Chen Pingan lifted his hand, the table quickly returned to calm. 

He stood up, walked a few steps, then turned back, crouching down to look at the table. 

It had been stable for ages. 

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 749: A Plentiful School of Fish in the Blue Waters

In the Jia Shen camp, the leader was not a sword cultivator but rather the wooden clogs of Liu Cha's only disciple, Bei Qi. Along with them were the gate disciple of Tuo Yue Mountain, Li Zhen, Yu Si, the swordswoman Liu Bai, and others.

The group appeared at the southernmost end of the battlefield where both sides were engaged in a duel of swords. Yu Si crouched down, pinching a small handful of soil between his fingers, gently grinding it into powder. After dusting off his hands, he stood up and said, “The ebb and flow of sword intent on both sides, the degree of conversion, is about as expected. This is the only good news left.”

Liu Bai frowned and asked, “Why would we jump into a trap we clearly see? Moreover, it’s not just us at the Jia Shen camp who feel uneasy. The Jia Zi camp is still ignoring us; what’s the situation? Our Earth Immortal sword cultivators are clearly being targeted, and several have already died. By yesterday, we had lost nine, right? How many more achievements do we have to hand over to the Sword Qi Great Wall? This is war; where is the sense in being so stubborn about face?”

Mu Ji, the wooden clogs, replied, “The Jia Zi camp hasn’t revealed the specifics either. They only mentioned that after the sword duel, including the predecessors Yang Zhi and Huang Luan, who made contributions, they would be bringing back the severed heads of the sword immortals from behind to offer to the Sword Qi Great Wall as a token of gratitude after the duel.”

Liu Bai shouted angrily, “What gratitude?! Do our Earth Immortal sword cultivators have to die for nothing, for there to be those hidden sword immortal heads? It’s two completely different matters!”

Mu Ji sighed, “Yeah. I also don’t understand. I don’t get why so many of our sword cultivators have to die here, as if they must die.”

Tan smiled, “At this point, what else can we do? We can only watch with our eyes wide open.”

In the distance, on the battlefield, a sword immortal from the savage world revealed their hundred-foot tall form, standing alone on the battlefield with a sword in each hand, slamming one sword into the ground.

Above the waterfall of the Sword Qi Great Wall, the sky suddenly unleashed hundreds of bright red lightning bolts, as if the gods were enraged, wielding whips of thunder, striking wildly at the earth.

The sword immortals from the Sword Qi Great Wall responded in kind, using the clouds of sword energy to intercept the lightning, preventing it from hitting the sword formations and causing disaster to the mid-five realm sword cultivators below.

A slender female sword immortal from their side did not carry a sword; instead, her large sleeves swirled, and sword energy began to condense over several miles of land, transforming into countless flying swords that shot towards the magnificent sword formation of the Sword Qi Great Wall, which seemed to have descended from the heavens.

On the city wall, the great sword immortal Yue Qing confronted her with one of his fate-defining flying swords, the Skylark.

Amidst the torrent of magical treasures from the demon clan and this sword duel, several previously unremarkable cultivators from the savage world appeared to blossom. 

One demon cultivator, who was not a sword cultivator but a Qi practitioner from the cave level, unexpectedly obtained two ancient sword intents from the Sword Qi Great Wall after striking, which were of extremely high rank. This young man was destined to join the ranks of the hundred sword immortals, with ample resources flowing his way. Perhaps by the time he reached the Haoran world, he would even have a chance to establish a sect of his own in the sword path.

A Golden Core sword cultivator, who once thought his fate-defining flying sword was useless, achieved remarkable feats, forcing two of the enemy’s sword immortals to expend their full power in succession, saving two Earth Immortal sword cultivators, and causing the opponents’ flying sword techniques to inexplicably crash into the sword formations of the Sword Qi Great Wall. The Golden Core sword cultivators from the Sword Qi Great Wall lost two in quick succession, and the mid-five realm sword cultivators below the Earth Immortal level suffered heavy losses, directly retreating from the battlefield.

This Golden Core sword cultivator was ordered to retreat from the battlefield, later being assisted by a senior in the Ascension realm who used illusions to allow him to re-enter the battlefield several times, specifically targeting the powerful strikes of enemy sword immortals.

As for how this Golden Core sword cultivator could foresee the sword immortals’ strikes, only the Jia Zi camp knew the truth, and the Jia Shen camp had no right to question it.

Additionally, a pair of Nascent Soul sword cultivators broke through to the upper five realms during the battle.

Without these “glistening adornments,” the sword cultivators’ duel in the savage world would be a joke.

Because the rate of losses among the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall, compared to the predictions of various military camps, was quite different, significantly slower than expected.

Mu Ji remarked, “In war, it’s all about people and money. The losses on the enemy’s side are less than anticipated, but fewer doesn’t mean no casualties. Next, we must see about the divine money; in fact, this is even more crucial than the sword cultivators. Right now, the spiritual energy of the sword cultivators at the Sword Qi Great Wall is showing signs of drying up, and the spiritual energy on the battlefield is so muddled that neither side can draw from it. Meanwhile, we’re backed by the entire savage world, and with the help of two seniors using their great powers to draw energy, two streams of spiritual energy are converging here like rivers, continuously flowing towards us. But how much spiritual energy can that city wall behind accumulate? As the war goes on, how much can it support the sword immortals’ full power? The Yi Wu military camp has long conducted precise calculations on this. As long as nothing unexpected happens, the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall will only die later, but when they do, it will be extremely fast and numerous.”

Yu Si laughed, “It’s even quite possible they’ll end up exhausting themselves quietly, even if they summon their flying swords, they won’t be able to retrieve them.”

Liu Bai said solemnly, “The premise is that there are no unexpected events! That there’s no unforeseen source of spiritual energy for the Sword Qi Great Wall! But after this battle, haven’t we received plenty of unexpected surprises?!”

Mu Ji nodded, “Then let’s roughly calculate the ferry boats from the eight continents of the Haoran world. Let’s not even mention the North Ju Lu continent; if they were to pull out half of their resources, it would be possible. Fortunately, only the North Ju Lu continent can do something like this. The Tongye continent has no ferry boats; the closest to the Hanging Mountain would be the South Posa continent and the Southwest Fuyao continent. The Fuyao continent’s ferry boats, led by the Mountain Water Cave, have past grievances and wouldn’t be easy to deal with. Right now, they might be doing us a big favor. As for the Posa continent, they wouldn’t dare be too accommodating. Even if the boat owners have gone crazy and are willing to do everything to help the Sword Qi Great Wall, they still have to see if their sects dare to agree.”

Mu Ji laughed at this point, “Fortunately, the Sword Qi Great Wall has never been good at dealing with the Haoran world.”

Liu Bai, used to speaking in reverse, countered, “What if? What if someone from the Sword Qi Great Wall is able to persuade the ferry boats of the eight continents to lavishly supply the Sword Qi Great Wall?!”

Tan looked up at the Sword Qi Great Wall with a cold smile, “What do they rely on to persuade? Is it the face of the sword immortals? How can someone who could earn a fortune not do so? How did the ferry boat’s negotiator come to be? Are they expected to rely on the sword immortals to personally send divine money to them? As luck would have it, the Sword Qi Great Wall is most in need of pure divine money.”

Mu Ji looked up at the city wall and said, “If given the chance, I would really like to meet the person sitting up there and have a chat with him.”

Li Zhen said, “That also depends on whether he can survive until that day.”

Liu Bai’s mind sparked with inspiration as she was about to speak.

Mu Ji seemed to have guessed her thoughts and shook his head, “Unexpected events must be corrected by unexpected events. Over at the Hanging Mountain, there are some entities that won’t just sit by and watch.”

Mi Yu, having built a snowman and secretly picked flowers from the garden to dress the snow girl, adorned it with floral garments, mirroring how she looked when they first met.

When they reached the great hall, he spotted a young hidden official squatting on the ground, studying the table. Mi Yu stepped over the threshold, leaned against a small table, and curiously asked, “Hidden official, is this Four Immortals Table actually a valuable treasure hiding a hidden mystery? Planning to move it to the summer palace?”

Chen Pingan stood up, “I’m going out for a walk.”

Mi Yu straightened up and glanced at the Four Immortals Table, realizing it didn’t seem that valuable.

As one of the four private residences of the Hanging Mountain, Chun Fan Zhai was vast, with corridors and passages, ancient trees towering, especially famous for its unusual rock formations. The waterfalls and flowing springs harmonized beautifully with the flourishing plants. Chen Pingan and Mi Yu walked along a stone path, surrounded by mist and abundant spiritual energy.

Mi Yu asked, “Hidden official, allow me to ramble a bit more. To tightly guard one’s own bowl of rice while snatching from others is quite savory, but those people are not ordinary; they only offer benefits and still don’t remember.” 

Chen Pingan smiled, “Is it my fault for summoning so many sword immortals to support us, only for no one to die in the end?”

Mi Yu responded, “How could I dare?”

Chen Pingan explained, “With eleven sword immortals visiting the Hanging Mountain, the killing intent was so heavy that it couldn’t be faked. To put it bluntly, do sword immortals need to pretend to want to kill? Yet in the end, not a single sword was drawn. Do you believe it?”

Mi Yu said, “I don’t believe it.”

Chen Pingan nodded, “Therefore, Wu Qiu and Bai Xi and the others will believe it even less. Don’t be fooled by their later discussions; as merchants, they seem to return to their little world of accounts, but in truth, they are still worried about life and death. Many details, if you observe a bit more instead of just focusing on which of the boat owners are good-looking or flawed, it’s not hard to discover this truth.”

Mi Yu felt somewhat disgruntled.

Familiarity breeds comfort; this was his small world, but it couldn’t compare to the hidden official’s deep foresight. His only rival was the beautiful women of the world.

Chen Pingan stopped and turned to gaze at the nearby water pavilion and building, “Either kill a few more; the most powerful among those from the Central Land, Wu Qiu, or the strongest in combat, Jiang Gaotai, and the least significant, Liu Shen, who holds the deepest grudge against the Sword Qi Great Wall, must all be eliminated. Only by killing those who seem least likely to die can we force the enemy into a corner, leaving no escape, both in position and in heart.”

On the artificial hill, the jagged stones revealed small pines and cypresses growing between the crevices, lush and green.

Chen Pingan sat on a step, “If the situation were not thus, then don’t kill any, but keep them. Whom to kill, let them ponder; just give a hint, and smart people will help me pick who to kill, conversely hinting to me who would die with the least cost, requiring no reparations from Yan Ming or Nalan Caihuan, and may not even need an apology from sword immortal Sun Juyuan. Since they believe the Sword Qi Great Wall will definitely kill to establish authority, there must be deaths among the ferry boats to satisfy the 'Hidden Official' and the sword immortals. Then it’s a matter of killing friends rather than the poor path.”

Chen Pingan pointed at the twisted pines and cypresses, “If they can thrive in the wild marshes, they can surely live well here.”

Mi Yu suddenly became enlightened, the little bit of frustration dissipating.

Chen Pingan remarked, “Killing is not a game. Speaking from personal feelings, it would be satisfying to kill all those boat owners in the great hall. But if we consider it more, who should truly die? Bai Xi? He’s not the ancestor of the Mountain Water Cave. Wu Qiu? Why should he die? Jiang Gaotai, if it weren’t for my persistent meddling, would he have fallen into such dire straits due to his own desire to help himself and the ferry boats?”

Mi Yu fell silent for a moment, sitting beside Chen Pingan, and solemnly said, “Making a fortune from killing isn’t much fun, yet they all seem quite spirited and happy? If I were the Hidden Official, I would have acted much earlier. Of course, the consequences would be dire.”

Chen Pingan rarely offered comforting words to Mi Yu, “Sword immortals naturally only do what they ought to do. If I remember correctly, at my age, you were already a Golden Core sword cultivator, then at sixty-four, you reached the Nascent Soul realm, and at one hundred ninety-six, you broke through the Nascent Soul bottleneck. In fact, your talent among the many sword immortals is not at the bottom; rather, you rank quite high. Excellent talent ensures Mi Yu can rise to the upper five realms that many others dream of, but in this process, you’ve turned to familiar matters outside of sword training, which you genuinely enjoy. The outcome, in the eyes of outsiders, may not seem good, but you see no problem with it, at most feeling guilty towards your brother Mi Hu.”

Mi Yu felt somewhat awkward, “Hidden Official, you can speak freely; I’m just more interested in romance and love, flirting with women, rather than practicing swordsmanship and killing.”

Chen Pingan smiled, “A place’s environment nurtures its people. The Haoran world cannot produce so many sword cultivators, but the price for that is needing an outsider familiar with foreign customs to serve as this Hidden Official. But if I also get distracted, and my heart strays further from purity, then continuing down this path, even if I excel in scheming against people’s hearts, the bottleneck in my future cultivation will only grow larger. However, I can guarantee that as long as there are no major surprises, my achievements on the path of the sword should still surpass those of the Mi sword immortal, especially in terms of killing abilities.”

Mi Yu nodded, “Realm cannot solve all problems, but it can solve many.”

Chen Pingan replied, “Realm can solve a lot, but it cannot solve everything.”

Mi Yu praised, “The reason why the Hidden Official is the Hidden Official is not without reason.”

Chen Pingan didn’t respond to that, smiling, “Earlier, Shao Yunyan and I had a casual talk that pushed things along, indicating his stance. It’s roughly the opposite of what you’ve said; he’s trying to persuade me not to act impulsively and recklessly kill. The words were quite tactful, but if I don’t heed his advice, the next time we have a meeting, it’ll probably have to move to the Water Essence Palace or Lingzhi Zhai. Do you think Shao Yunyan is really just sitting at the doorway serving as a guardian for us at the Sword Qi Great Wall? A sword immortal’s temperament is never low.”

Mi Yu furrowed his brows tightly.

Chen Pingan waved his hand, “No need to hold a grudge against Shao Yunyan for that; as long as it makes sense, we’ll take the advice. Besides, afterward, Shao Yunyan wouldn’t mind us taking some ruthless measures. I’ve tested it, and he accepted it. Not only that, but he’s also willing to personally step in and agreed to help me find that merchant prodigy who’s good at cooking the books. So, after all the twists and turns, we’ve ended up with the result I wanted.”

Mi Yu softly said, “It’s a bit tiring.”

Not addressing him as the Hidden Official was generally considered Mi sword immortal’s heartfelt words.

Chen Pingan stood up, “You can’t just keep hitting people with sticks to confuse them; it’s time to offer some real benefits. Otherwise, when they come to their senses, they’ll still have some clever little moves. I can handle it, but I can’t afford to waste time.”

Returning to the main hall of Chun Fan Zhai, everyone had taken their seats.

Chen Pingan sat at the head seat, smiling, “No contention, no quarrels, no friends; since we’re friends now, I also have a small gift to give everyone.”

Unexpectedly, no one felt at ease; each person held their breath, many of the older boat owners had already tucked their hands into their sleeves, preparing to bolt at the slightest provocation.

With that row of sword immortals no longer present, this young Hidden Official was finally about to kill someone?

This young Hidden Official’s mind seemed vastly different from that of ordinary people; he could really pull it off!

Chen Pingan smiled, “It’s just a small gift for everyone; there’s no need to sit so rigidly.”

Mi Yu slowly stood up.

Several of the more timid boat owners nearly rose instinctively, but as soon as they started to stand, they realized something was amiss and quietly sat back down.

Mi Yu, with one hand behind his back, gently shook his robe sleeve, producing strange jade tokens that glimmered with treasure light and swirled with sword energy, each hovering in front of the fifty-four boat owners from the eight continents.

Mi Yu’s thoughts shifted slightly, and without any ripples, all the jade tokens instantly stood upright, slowly rotating so that those across from them could gaze in awe.

Everyone was too occupied to notice the abilities of a jade purity sword immortal.

Wu Qiu focused intently; the tokens were styled like the most ordinary of ‘no event’ tokens from the Haoran world. It was hard to speak of a front and back; one side was inscribed with “Sword Qi Great Wall,” and the other had “Haoran World” carved into it. However, on the side with the four characters for Sword Qi Great Wall, there were also two small characters, “Hidden Official,” and even smaller was a number: nine.

Wu Qiu quickly glanced at another place; Tang Feiqian’s was “twelve,” Jiang Gaotai’s was “sixteen.” The ferry boat overseer for Fuyao continent, Bai Xi, had the number “thirteen” in front of him. The boat owner of “Nishang” at the entrance, Liu Shen, had “ninety-six.”

Chen Pingan leaned against the Four Immortals Table.

Mi Yu started, “Don’t get caught up in the size of the numbers; in short, each is unique. This token is personally inscribed by the Hidden Official, and every single jade token contains the sword energy of two to three sword immortals. As for which sword immortals favored which tokens, aside from the Hidden Official, no one else knows how to deduce the answer. In any case, looking across the entire Haoran world, no one could replicate it. To say it’s valuable, it’s not exactly worth mentioning; you’re all merchants who’ve seen all sorts of treasures. But to say it’s worthless, it’s still a rare item, one of a kind.”

At this point, Mi Yu emphasized, “In the future, if anyone else wishes to obtain such a jade token, it will depend on whether they have the opportunity to meet the Hidden Official and whether they qualify to become a guest of Chun Fan Zhai. I can guarantee that it will be extremely difficult. Moreover, there are only ninety-nine of these jade tokens in total; no more will be made. Thus, the highest number will be ninety-nine. So if anyone sees a jade token with the number one hundred in the future, just consider it a joke.”

Shao Yunyan suddenly chimed in with a laugh, “I’m also a guest; why is it that I alone do not have a jade token? I see that the smaller the number, the more precious the guest. So I want that one with the small character ‘ninety-nine’ on it.”

Mi Yu didn’t dare to take matters into his own hands and turned to look at Chen Pingan.

Jiang Gaotai suddenly stood up, cupping his fists, and solemnly said, “Hidden Official, can I trade this jade token for the one with the number ninety-nine?”

This time, it was not that the young Hidden Official had said anything to him, but Jiang Gaotai genuinely wanted to exchange the current jade token for the one with the highest number.

A small gamble to stir feelings? 

It was hardly a small gamble. 

Jiang Gaotai had always trusted his instincts. During many crucial moments on the path of cultivation, Jiang Gaotai had relied on this inexplicable intuition to accumulate the wealth he had today.

Shao Yunyan smiled, “Jiang boat owner, are you robbing me? Isn’t that a bit too ungracious? Moreover, the smaller the number, the more likely it is that the sword immortals who infused their sword energy into the jade tokens have higher realms. Why bother fussing over the size of the number?”

Jiang Gaotai chuckled and turned back to cup his fists again, “I sincerely request that Sword Immortal Shao let it go.”

Shao Yunyan shook his head, “This matter is not negotiable.”

Chen Pingan remarked, “This jade token can be seen as a small gamble for all of you, to wager on which sword immortals’ sword energy is contained within. If you wish to exchange, it’s up to you. If you fancy the one you have, it’s completely fine; just remember to notify Mi sword immortal before leaving Chun Fan Zhai. Although I’m the one giving the gifts, I still need to keep track of who got which token. As for whether you give the jade tokens to your sects, keep them for yourself, or sell them off, treating them as mere jade tokens which aren’t valuable, that’s all up to you. Now, let’s not discuss such trivial matters; let’s continue with the important matters.”

Mi Yu resumed his seat.

Shao Yunyan and Jiang Gaotai sat down as well.
